\chapter{Homotopy Type Theory}

\section{Functoriality and Path Algebra}
    Recall from Exercise~\ref{exr:ap-application} that given $f\colon A\to B$, the congruence function
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f\colon\prod_{x,y\colon A}\;\prod_{p\colon x\eq Ay}f(x)\eq Bf(y)
    \]
    transforms paths in $A$ to paths in $B$. More precisely
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f(x,y,p)\colon f(x)\eq Bf(y),\quad\text{for }p\colon x\eq Ay,
    \]
    where the notation $\fun{ap}_f(x,y,p)$ is usually simplified to $\fun{ap}_f(p)$ or $\tilde f(p)$. The following diagram illustrates the setting
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=large]
            \fun1
                    \arrow[r,"x",bend left=40]
                    \arrow[r,"y"',bend right=40]
                    \arrow[r,phantom,"\scriptstyle p",description]
                &A
                    \arrow[r,"f"]
                &B.
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]


\begin{prop}\label{prop:ap-properties}
    Let $A,B,C\colon\univ$. Given functions\/ $f\colon A\to B$ and\/ $g\colon B\to C$ and paths\/ $p\colon x\eq Ay$ and\/ $q\colon y\eq Az$, we have:
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_x)\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x)}$.
        \item $\fun{ap}_f(p\ct q)\eq{f(x)\eq Bf(z)}\fun{ap}_f(p)\ct\fun{ap}_f(q)$.
        \item $\fun{ap}_f(p^{-1})\eq{f(y)\eq Bf(x)}\fun{ap}_f(p)^{-1}$.
        \item $\fun{ap}_g(\fun{ap}_f(p))\eq{g\circ f(x)\eq Cg\circ f(y)}\fun{ap}_{g\circ f}(p)$.
        \item $\fun{ap}_{\id_A}(p)\eq{x\eq Ay}p$.
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\needspace{2\baselineskip}
\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{enumerate}[a)]
        \item Exercise~\ref{exr:ap-application}.
        \item Exercise~\ref{exr:ap-application}.
        
        \item This easily follows by path induction on $p$. However, here we will illustrate how to deduce it from what we have proven so far.
        
        First observe that
        \begin{align*}
            \fun{ap}_f(p)\ct\fun{ap}_f(p^{-1})
                &\eq{f(x)\eq Bf(x)}\fun{ap}_f(p\ct p^{-1})
                    &&\text{; by part b)}\\
                &\eq{f(x)\eq Bf(x)}\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_x)
                    &&\text{; by } \fun{ap}_{\fun{ap}_f}(\text{inverse law})\\
                &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x)}
                    &&\text{; by part a).}
        \end{align*}
        The second equality applies $\fun{ap}_{\fun{ap}_f}$ to the witness of the inverse law, i.e., to the path $p\ct p^{-1}\eq{x\eq Ax}\fun{refl}_x$.
    
        Now consider the function
        \begin{align*}
            g &\colon (f(x)\eq Bf(x)) \to (f(y)\eq Bf(x)) \\
            g(r) &\defeq \fun{ap}_f(p)^{-1}\ct r.
        \end{align*}
        Let $\gamma$ be the witness of the equality we just proved. Applying $\fun{ap}_g$ to $\gamma^{-1}$ yields
        \begin{align*}
            \fun{ap}_f(p)^{-1}
                &\eq{f(y)\eq Bf(x)} \fun{ap}_f(p)^{-1}\ct\big(\fun{ap}_f(p) \ct\fun{ap}_f(p^{-1})\big)
                    &&\text{; }\fun{ap}_g(\gamma^{-1})\\
                &\eq{f(y)\eq Bf(x)} \big(\fun{ap}_f(p)^{-1}\ct\fun{ap}_f(p)\big) \ct\fun{ap}_f(p^{-1})
                    &&\text{; associativity}\\
                &\eq{f(y)\eq Bf(x)}\fun{ap}_f(p^{-1})
                    &&\text{; left inverse.}
        \end{align*}
        where the last equality can be proven by mirroring the deduction of the first one.

        \item Since $p\colon x\eq Ay$, we know that $\fun{ap}_f(p)\colon f(x)\eq Bf(y)$. Therefore,
        \[
            \fun{ap}_g(\fun{ap}_f(p))\colon g(f(x))\eq Cg(f(y)).
        \]
        The type of the term above is definitionally equal to $g\circ f(x)\eq C g\circ f(y)$.
        Consider the case where $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. We have
        \begin{align*}
            \fun{ap}_g(\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_x))
                &\equiv \fun{ap}_g(\fun{refl}_{f(x)})\\
                &\equiv \fun{refl}_{g(f(x))}\\
                &\equiv \fun{refl}_{g\circ f(x)}\\
                &\equiv \fun{ap}_{g\circ f}(\fun{refl}_x).
        \end{align*}
        To conclude that $\fun{ap}_g(\fun{ap}_f(p))\eq{g\circ f(x)\eq Cg\circ f(y)}\fun{ap}_{g\circ f}(p)$, we apply path induction to the motive
        \[
            C(x,y,p)\defeq \fun{ap}_g(\fun{ap}_f(p))\eq{g\circ f(x)\eq Cg\circ f(y)}\fun{ap}_{g\circ f}(p),
        \]
        with the base case $c(x)\colon C(x,x,\fun{refl}_x)$ defined as $\fun{refl}_{\fun{ap}_{g\circ f}(\fun{refl}_x)}$.

        \item For\/ $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$, since\/ $\id_A(x)\equiv x$, we have
        \begin{align*}
            \fun{ap}_{\id_A}(\fun{refl}_x)
                &\equiv \fun{refl}_{\id_A(x)}\\
                &\equiv \fun{refl}_x.
        \end{align*}
        Therefore, the conclusion follows by path induction applied to the motive
        \[
            C(x,y,p)\defeq\fun{ap}_{\id_A}(p)\eq{x\eq Ay}p
        \]
        with base case\/ $c(x)\defeq\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_x}\colon C(x,x,\fun{refl}_x)$.
        
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:ap-const}
    Let\/ $A, B\colon\univ$ and\/ $b\colon B$. Given the constant function\/ $f\colon A\to B$ defined by\/ $f(x)\defeq b$, for any path\/ $p\colon x\eq A y$, we have
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f(p) \eq{b\eq B b} \fun{refl}_b.
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    By path induction on $p$ it suffices to prove the case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv \fun{refl}_x$.
    \begin{enumerate}[-]
        \item \lhs: $\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_x)\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x)}\equiv \fun{refl}_b$.
        \item \rhs: $\fun{refl}_b$.
    \end{enumerate}
    Since both sides are definitionally equal to $\fun{refl}_b$, the equality is inhabited by $\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_b}$.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Path Whiskering}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:path-whiskering}
    Let $A$ be a type and $x,y,z\colon A$ points.
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item Given a $1$-path $p\colon x\eq Ay$ and a $2$-path $\beta\colon r\eq{y\eq Az}s$ between $1$-paths $r,s\colon y\eq Az$,
        \[
            \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=large,
                row sep=huge]
                x 
                        \arrow[r,"p"]
                    &y
                        \arrow[r,bend left=45,"r"{name=U}]
                        \arrow[r,bend right=45,"s"'{name=D}]
                    &z
                        \arrow[Rightarrow,
                            from=U,
                            to=D,
                            "\beta", 
                            shorten <= 8pt,
                            shorten >= 8pt]
            \end{tikzcd}
        \]
        we define the \textsl{left whiskering}
        \[
            p\lwct\beta\colon(p\ct r)\eq{x\eq Az}(p\ct s)
        \]
        by path induction on $\beta$: if $r\equiv s$ and $\beta\equiv\fun{refl}_r$, then $p\lwct\fun{refl}_r\defeq\fun{refl}_{p\ct r}$.
        
        \item Given a $2$-path $\alpha\colon p\eq{x\eq Ay}q$ between paths $p,q\colon x\eq Ay$ and a path $r\colon y\eq Az$,
        \[
            \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=large,
                row sep=huge]
                x
                        \arrow[r,bend left=45,"p"{name=U}]
                        \arrow[r,bend right=45,"q"'{name=D}]
                    &y 
                        \arrow[r, "r"]
                    &z
                        \arrow[Rightarrow,
                            from=U,
                            to=D,
                            "\alpha", 
                            shorten <= 8pt,
                            shorten >= 8pt]
            \end{tikzcd}
        \]
        we define the \textsl{right whiskering}
        \[
            \alpha\rwct r\colon(p\ct r)\eq{x\eq Az}(q\ct r)
        \]
        by induction on $\alpha$: if $q\equiv p$ and $\alpha\equiv\fun{refl}_p$, then $\fun{refl}_p\rwct r\defeq\fun{refl}_{p\ct r}$.
    \end{enumerate}
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:path-whiskering-defn}
    By definition,
    \begin{align*}
        \alpha\rwct r&\equiv\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_r}(\alpha)\\
        p\lwct\beta&\equiv\fun{ap}_{\fun{lct}_p}(\beta),
    \end{align*}
    where $\fun{rct}_r\defeq x\mapsto x\ct r$ and $\fun{lct}_p\defeq x\mapsto p\ct x$.
\end{rem}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:path-whiskering-associativity}
    Given a $2$-path\/ $\alpha\colon p\eq{}q$ and appropriately composable $1$-paths\/ $r$ and\/ $s$, we have the following homotopies witnessing the associativity of whiskering:
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $(\alpha\rwct r)\rwct s\eq{}\alpha\rwct(r\ct s)$.
        \item $p\lwct(q \lwct\alpha)\eq{}(p\ct q)\lwct\alpha$.
        \item $p\lwct(\alpha\rwct r)\eq{}(p\lwct\alpha)\rwct r$.
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}    
    For a) observe that
    \begin{align*}
        (\alpha\rwct r)\rwct s
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_r}
                (\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_r}(\alpha))\\
            &\eq{}\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_s\circ\fun{rct}_r}(\alpha)\\
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_{r\ct s}}(\alpha)\\
            &\equiv\alpha\rwct(r\ct s).
    \end{align*}
    The proof of b) is similar.
    
    For c) compare left and right actions:
    \begin{align*}
        \lhs&\equiv
            \fun{ap}_{\fun{lct}_p}
                (\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_r}(\alpha))\\
            &\eq{}\fun{ap}_{\fun{lct}_p\circ\fun{rct}_r}(\alpha).\\[1mm]
        \rhs&\equiv
            \fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_r}(\fun{ap}_{\fun{lct}_p}
                (\alpha))\\
            &\eq{}\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_r\circ\fun{lct}_rp}
                (\alpha).
    \end{align*}
    The conclusion follows because
    \[
        \fun{rct}_r\circ\fun{lct}_p
            \eq{}\fun{lct}_p\circ\fun{rct}_r
    \]
    since concatenation of $1$-paths is propositionally associative.
\end{proof}


\begin{defn}
    Let $A$ be a type and $a,b,c\colon A$ points. Consider paths $p,q\colon a\eq Ab$ and $r,s \colon b\eq Ac$, along with homotopies $\alpha\colon p\eq{a\eq Ab}q$ and $\beta\colon r\eq{b\eq Ac}s$, as depicted below:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge,row sep=large]
            a 
                \arrow[r,bend left=45,"p"{name=U1}]
                \arrow[r,bend right=45,"q"'{name=D1}]
            &b
                \arrow[r,bend left=45,"r"{name=U2}]
                \arrow[r,bend right=45,"s"'{name=D2}]
            &c
                \arrow[Rightarrow,from=U1,to=D1,"\alpha", 
                    shorten <= 8pt,shorten >= 8pt]
                \arrow[Rightarrow,from=U2,to=D2,"\beta", 
                    shorten <= 8pt,shorten >= 8pt]
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    The \textsl{horizontal composition} of $\alpha$ and $\beta$ is the $2$-path
    \begin{align*}
        \alpha\hct\beta&\colon(p\ct r)\eq{a\eq Ac}(q\ct s)        
    \end{align*}
    defined by path induction on $\alpha$ and $\beta$. Explicitly, if $q\equiv p$ and $\alpha\equiv\fun{refl}_p$, we define
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{refl}_p\hct\beta\colon(p\ct r)\eq{a\eq Ac}(p\ct s)
    \end{align*}
    by induction on $\beta$ as follows: if $s\equiv r$ and $\beta\equiv\fun{refl}_r$, then
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:refl-hct}
        \fun{refl}_p\hct\fun{refl}_r\defeq\fun{refl}_{p\ct r}.
    \end{equation}
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}
    Given 2-paths $\alpha\colon p\eq{x\eq A y} q$ and $\gamma\colon q\eq{x\eq A y} r$, their \textsl{vertical composition} is their concatenation as paths in the identity type $x\eq A y$:
    \[
        \alpha\ct\gamma \colon p\eq{x\eq A y} r.
    \]
\end{defn}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:interchange-law} {\upshape[Interchange Law]}
    Let\/ $A$ be a type. Consider the configuration of paths and homotopies depicted in the following commutative diagram:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge,
            row sep=huge]
            x
                \arrow[r, bend left=60, "p"{name=U1}]
                \arrow[r, "q"{name=M1, description}]
                \arrow[r, bend right=60, "u"'{name=D1}]
            & y
                \arrow[r, bend left=60, "r"{name=U2}]
                \arrow[r, "s"{name=M2, description}]
                \arrow[r, bend right=60, "v"'{name=D2}]
            & z
            % Left Column 2-cells
            \arrow[Rightarrow,
                from=U1,
                to=M1,
                "\alpha",
                shorten <=3pt,
                shorten >= 1pt]
            \arrow[Rightarrow,
                from=M1,
                to=D1,
                "\gamma",
                shorten <=2pt,
                shorten >= 3pt]
            % Right Column 2-cells
            \arrow[Rightarrow,
                from=U2,
                to=M2,
                "\beta",
                shorten <=3pt,
                shorten >= 1pt]
            \arrow[Rightarrow,
                from=M2,
                to=D2,
                "\delta",
                shorten <=2pt,
                shorten >= 3pt]
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    The horizontal and vertical compositions satisfy:
    \[
        (\alpha\hct\beta)\ct(\gamma\hct\delta)
        \eq{}
        (\alpha\ct\gamma)\hct(\beta\ct\delta).
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    Let us first observe that the types match. We have:
    \begin{align*}
        \alpha\hct\beta &\colon (p\ct r)\eq{x\eq Az}(q\ct s)\\
        \gamma\hct\delta &\colon (q\ct s)\eq{x\eq Az}(u\ct v).
    \end{align*}
    Thus, the \lhs is a path of type $(p\ct r)\eq{x\eq Az}(u\ct v)$.
    Similarly, for the right-hand side components:
    \begin{align*}
        \alpha\ct\gamma &\colon p\eq{x\eq Ay}u\\
        \beta\ct\delta &\colon r\eq{y\eq Az}v.
    \end{align*}
    Thus, the \rhs is also a path of type $(p\ct r)\eq{x\eq Az}(u\ct v)$.
    
    Since the types agree, we proceed by path induction.
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Step 1.] Induction on $\alpha$. We assume $\alpha$ is $\fun{refl}_p$, which definitionally forces the endpoint $q$ to be $p$. Consequently, the type of $\gamma$ becomes $p\eq{x\eq Ay}u$.

        \item[Step 2.] Induction on $\gamma$. We assume $\gamma$ is $\fun{refl}_p$, which forces $u$ to be $p$.

        \item[Step 3.] Induction on $\beta$, and then on $\delta$. Applying the same logic to the right column, we assume $\beta$ and $\delta$ are $\fun{refl}_r$, which forces $s \equiv r$ and $v \equiv r$.
        
        \item[Step 4.] Computation. In this base case, all paths are definitionally reflexivity. We compute both sides:
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs&\equiv(\fun{refl}_p\hct\fun{refl}_r)
                \ct(\fun{refl}_p\hct\fun{refl}_r)\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_{p\ct r}
                        \ct \fun{refl}_{p\ct r}\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_{p\ct r}.
                        &&;\ \eqref{eq:refl-hct}\\[1mm]
            \rhs&\equiv(\fun{refl}_p\ct\fun{refl}_p)
                \hct(\fun{refl}_r\ct\fun{refl}_r)\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_p\hct\fun{refl}_r\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_{p\ct r}.
                        &&;\ \eqref{eq:refl-hct}
        \end{align*}
    \end{description}
    Since both sides reduce to the same term $\fun{refl}_{p\ct r}$ in the base case, the path induction principle ensures they are equal in the general case.
\end{proof}

\section{Pointed Types and Loop Spaces}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:pointed-type}
    A \textsl{pointed type}\/ $(A,a)$ is a type\/ $A\colon\univ$ together with a point\/ $a\colon A$, called its \textsl{basepoint}. We write
    \[
        \puniv\defeq\sum_{A:\,\univ}A
    \]
    for the type of pointed types in the universe\/ $\univ$.
\end{defn}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:n-loop-space}
    Given a pointed type $(A,a)$, we define the \textsl{loop space} of $(A,a)$ as the following pointed type:
    \begin{align*}
        \Omega&\colon\puniv\to\puniv\\
        \Omega(\dep{A,a})&\defeq\dep{a\eq Aa,\fun{refl}_a}.        
    \end{align*}
    An element of the underlying type $a\eq Aa$ is called a \textsl{loop} at $a$.
    
    For $n\colon\N$, we define the iterated loop space operation $\Omega^n\colon\puniv\to\puniv$ by recursion as follows: 
    \begin{align*}
        C&\defeq\puniv\to\puniv\\
        c_0&\defeq\id_\puniv\\
        c_s&\colon\N\to C\to C\\
        c_s(n,f)&\defeq f\circ\Omega\\
        \Omega^n&\defeq\fun{rec}_\N(C,c_0,c_s,n).
    \end{align*}
    Then, using the definitional equation
    \[
        \fun{rec}_\N(C,c_0,c_s,\fun{succ}(n))
        \equiv c_s(n,\fun{rec}_\N(C,c_0,c_s,n)),
    \]
    we obtain
    \[
        \Omega^{n+1}(\dep{A,a})
            \equiv\Omega^n(\Omega(\dep{A,a})).
    \]
\end{defn}

\begin{ntn}\label{ntn:loop-space}
    By abuse of notation, we will sometimes identify $\Omega(\dep{A,a})$ with $\pi_1(\Omega(\dep{A,a}))\equiv a\eq Aa$. The following definition is an example.
\end{ntn}

\begin{defn}
    Given a function $f\colon A\to B$ and a point $a\colon A$, the \textsl{induced map on loops} is the function
    \[
        \Omega f\colon\Omega(\dep{A,a})\to\Omega(\dep{B,f(a)})
    \]
    defined by
    \[
        \Omega f(p)\defeq\fun{ap}_f(p).
    \]
    Note that by part a) of Proposition~\ref{prop:ap-properties}, we have $\Omega f(\fun{refl}_a) \equiv \fun{refl}_{f(a)}$, meaning that $\Omega f$ preserves the basepoint definitionally.
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}
    Since $\Omega^2(\dep{A,a})\equiv\Omega(\dep{a\eq Aa,\fun{refl}_a})$, it follows that
    \[
        \Omega^2(\dep{A,a})
            \equiv
            \dep{
                \fun{refl}_a\eq{a\eq Aa}\fun{refl}_a,
                \fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_a}
            }.
    \]
\end{rem}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:Omega-abuse}
    Sometimes the notation is abused and $\Omega(\dep{A,a})$ is identified with $a\eq Aa$, i.e., as $\pi_1(\dep{a\eq Aa,\fun{refl}_a})$.

    Note however that the reason to define $\Omega\colon\puniv\to\puniv$ and not from $\puniv$ to $\univ$, is to enable the definition of $\Omega^n$ for $n\colon\N$.

    In particular, it is customary to refer to \textit{a point in the loop space\/ $\Omega(\dep{A,a})$} as a path $p\colon a\eq Aa$.
    
    Similarly, \textit{a point} in the second loop space $\Omega^2(\dep{A,a})$ refers to a homotopy 
    \[
        \alpha\colon\fun{refl}_a\eq{a\eq Aa}\fun{refl}_a
    \]
    between the trivial loop and itself.

    By induction, \textit{a point} in $\Omega^n(\dep{A,a})$ is an $n$-dimensional path from the trivial $(n-1)$-dimensional path to itself.
\end{rem}

\begin{thm} {\upshape[Eckmann-Hilton]}
    The composition operation on the second loop space
    \[
        \Omega^2(A)\times\Omega^2(A)\to\Omega^2(A)
    \]
    is commutative: $\alpha\ct\beta\eq{\Omega^2(A)}\beta\ct\alpha$, for any\/ $\alpha,\beta\colon\Omega^2(A)$.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    Introduce the $2$-loop
    \[
        e \defeq \fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_a}
        \colon \fun{refl}_a \eq{\Omega(A)} \fun{refl}_a,
    \]
    which is the identity element of the second loop space $\Omega^2(A)$.
    
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Horizontal $=$ vertical:] Consider the expression
        \[
            (\alpha\hct e)\ct(e\hct\beta).
        \]
        Using the unit laws for horizontal composition (which hold propositionally by path induction), we have $\alpha\hct e \eq{a\eq Aa} \alpha$ and $e\hct\beta \eq{a\eq Aa} \beta$. Thus, we have a path:
        \begin{equation}\label{eq:eckmann-1}
            (\alpha\hct e)\ct(e\hct\beta) \eq{a\eq Aa} \alpha\ct\beta.
        \end{equation}
        On the other hand, applying the Interchange Law Lemma~\ref{lem:interchange-law} to the original expression yields:
        \[
            (\alpha\hct e)\ct(e\hct\beta) \eq{a\eq Aa} (\alpha\ct e)\hct(e\ct\beta).
        \]
        Using the unit laws for vertical composition, namely
        \[
            \alpha\ct e \eq{a\eq Aa} \alpha
            \quad\text{and}\quad
            e\ct\beta \eq{a\eq Aa} \beta,
        \]
        the right-hand side becomes $\alpha\hct\beta$. Comparing this result with \eqref{eq:eckmann-1}, we conclude:
        \begin{equation}\label{eq:hct=ct}
            \alpha\hct\beta\eq{a\eq Aa}\alpha\ct\beta.
        \end{equation}
        
        \item[Commutativity:] Now consider the expression with terms swapped:
        \[
            (e\hct\beta)\ct(\alpha\hct e).
        \]
        Using the horizontal unit laws first:
        \[
            (e\hct\beta)\ct(\alpha\hct e)
                \eq{a\eq Aa}\beta\ct\alpha.
        \]
        Alternatively, applying the Interchange Law first:
        \[
            (e\hct\beta)\ct(\alpha \hct e) 
                \eq{a\eq Aa}(e\ct\alpha)\hct(\beta\ct e).
        \]
        Using the vertical unit laws on the right side, this reduces to $\alpha\hct\beta$. 
        
        Combining these chains of equalities with \eqref{eq:hct=ct}, we obtain:
        \[
            \beta\ct\alpha
                \eq{a\eq Aa}\alpha\hct\beta
                \eq{a\eq Aa}\alpha\ct\beta,
        \]
        as desired.
    \end{description}
\end{proof}

\section{Fibrations and Transport}

\label{rem:fibration}
Recall from classical topology that a \textsl{fibration} is a continuous map $\pi\colon E\to B$ with the homotopy-lifting property:
\[
    \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=large, column sep=huge]
        X
            \arrow[r,"f"]
            \arrow[d,hook,"i_0"']
        &E
            \arrow[d,"\pi"] \\
        X\times I
            \arrow[r,"\forall H"']
            \arrow[ur,dashed,"\exists\tilde{H}"]
        &B
    \end{tikzcd}
\]
In this context, $E$ is the \textsl{total space}\footnote{After the French \textit{Espace}.} and $B$ the \textsl{base space} of the fibration.

\textsl{Serre fibrations} lift paths, path homotopies, and higher-dimensional volumes. For instance, in the case of paths, the diagram above becomes:
\[
    \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=large, column sep=large]
        \{0\}
            \arrow[r,"e_0"]
            \arrow[d,hook,"i"']
        & E
            \arrow[d,"\pi"] \\
        I
            \arrow[r,"\forall\gamma"']
            \arrow[ur,dashed,"\exists\tilde{\gamma}"]
        & B
    \end{tikzcd}
\]
In Homotopy Type Theory, given a type family $P\colon A\to\univ$, the first projection $\fun{\pi}_1\colon \sum_{x\colon A}P(x)\to A$ is analogous to a fibration with \textsl{total space} $\sum_{x\colon A}P(x)$ and \textsl{base space} $A$. This structural analogy is established by the lemma below.

Given $a,b\colon A$, the type family $P$ structurally relates the fibers $P(a)$ and $P(b)$. Although a point $u\colon P(a)$ cannot be directly compared with $v\colon P(b)$ due to type mismatch, it is possible to establish a connection between the pairs $\dep{a,u}$ and $\dep{b,v}$ within the $\Sigma$-type. Specifically, if there exists a path $p\colon a\eq A b$, we can transport $u$ along $p$ to obtain an element $\fun{transport}^P(p,u)\colon P(b)$. Since this transported term inhabits the same fiber as $v$, the comparison becomes well-defined. More precisely:

\begin{thm}{\upshape[Path Lifting Property]}\label{thm:path-lift}
    Let\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$ be a type family over\/~$A$ and let\/ $E\defeq\sum_{x\colon A}P(x)$ be its total space. Given $a,b\colon A$, there exists a function
    \[
        \fun{lift}\colon\prod_{u\colon P(a)}\;
            \prod_{p\colon a\eq Ab}
            \dep{a,u}\eq E\dep{b,\fun{transport}^P(p,u)}
    \]
    \needspace{2\baselineskip}
    satisfying the following properties:
    \begin{enumerate}[i),font=\upshape]
        \item $\fun{lift}(u,p)\colon\dep{a,u}\eq E \dep{b,\fun{transport}^P(p,u)}$.
        \item $\fun{lift}(u,\fun{refl}_a)\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{a,u}}$.
        \item $\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{lift}(u,p))\eq{a\eq Ab}p$.
    \end{enumerate}
    where\/ $\pi_1\colon E\to A$ denotes the first projection.\footnotemark
\end{thm}
\footnotetext{Since\/ $\pi_1$ maps the total space to the base type\/ $A$, the functorial action\/ $\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}$ projects paths in\/ $E$ to paths in\/ $A$.}


\begin{proof}
    Consider the motive family\/ $C\colon\prod_{x\colon A}(a\eq Ax)\to\univ$, defined by
    \[
        C(x,p)\defeq
            \dep{a,u}\eq E\dep{x,\fun{transport}^P(p,u)}.
    \]
    Since\/ $\fun{transport}^P(\fun{refl}_a,u)\equiv u$, we have
    \[
        C(a,\fun{refl}_a)\equiv\dep{a,u}\eq E\dep{a,u},
    \]
    and we can specify the base case\/ $c\defeq\fun{refl}_{\dep{a,u}}$ to define, by \nref{lpar:based-path-induction},
    \[
        \fun{lift}(u,p)\defeq\fun{ind}'_{\eq A}(a,C,c,x,p).
    \]
    We can use based path induction again to verify that
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{\fun{\pi}_1}(\fun{lift}(u,p)) \eq{a\eq Ax} p.
    \]
    For the base case, we know definitionally that\/ $\fun{lift}(u,\fun{refl}_a) \equiv \fun{refl}_{\dep{a,u}}$. Thus,
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{\fun{\pi}_1}(\fun{lift}(u,\fun{refl}_a))
        \equiv \fun{ap}_{\fun{\pi}_1}(\fun{refl}_{(a,u)})
        \equiv \fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\dep{a,u})}
        \equiv \fun{refl}_a.
    \]
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:section-type}
    The lemma can be represented by the following diagram, where the horizontal arrows represent paths ---i.e., terms of the propositional equalities between their ends--- and the vertical arrows, functions:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=large,column sep=huge]
            \dep{a,u}
                \arrow[r,"{\fun{lift}(u,p)}"]
                \arrow[d,"\pi_1"']
            &\dep{x,\fun{transport}^P(p,u)}
                \arrow[d,"\pi_1"] \\
            a
                \arrow[r,"p"']
            &x
        \end{tikzcd}
        \qquad;\ u\colon P(a),\;p\colon a\eq Ax.
    \]
    Note also that a term $f\colon\prod_{x\colon A}P(x)$ can be regarded as a \textsl{section} of the fibration induced by~$P$.

    In particular, given that\/ $\fun{transport}^P(\fun{refl}_a,u)\equiv u$, we deduce that yielding a witness of\/ $\dep{a,u}\eq E\dep{a,v}$ is exactly the same as yielding a witness of
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:Sigma-trivial-equality}
        u\eq{P(a)}v.
    \end{equation}
\end{rem}

\begin{ntn}\label{ntn:p_*}
    When\/ $P$ is clear from the context we will simply write
    \[
        p_*(u)\defeq\fun{transport}^P(p,u)\colon P(x).
    \]
    In particular,
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:refl-*}
        (\fun{refl}_a)_*(u)\equiv u.
    \end{equation}
\end{ntn}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:sec}
    Let $A,B\colon\univ$. Given $b\colon B$ we define the \textsl{section} function
    \[
        \fun{sec}_b\colon A\to A\times B,\quad a\mapsto(a,b).
    \]
    Note that
    \begin{align*}
        \pi_1\circ\fun{sec}_b
            &\equiv\pi_1\circ(\lambda x.\,(x,b))
            \equiv\lambda x.\,\pi_1((x,b))
            \equiv\lambda x.\,x
            \equiv\id_A.\\
        \pi_2\circ\fun{sec}_b
            &\equiv\pi_2\circ(\lambda x.\,(x,b))
            \equiv\lambda x.\,\pi_2((x,b))
            \equiv\lambda x.\,b.
    \end{align*}
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:sec-lift}
    In the particular case where $P$ is a constant family $P(x)\equiv B$ for $x\colon A$, given $p\colon a\eq Aa'$, we have
    \begin{enumerate}[i)]
        \item $\fun{lift}(b,p)\eq{(a,b)\eq{A\times B}(a',b)}\fun{ap}_{\fun{sec}_b}(p)$,
        \item $\fun{lift}(b,\fun{refl}_a)\equiv\fun{refl}_{(a,b)}$,
        \item $\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{lift}(b,p))\eq{a\eq Aa'}p$.
    \end{enumerate}
    Part~ii) is property ii) of Theorem~\ref{thm:path-lift}. The equality of part~i) follows from part~ii) by induction on $p$.
    \[
        \begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1,
            >=stealth,
            font=\small]
            % Points
            \coordinate (start) at (0,0);
            \coordinate (end) at (4,0);
        
            \fill (start) circle (1.5pt) node[left] {$(a,b)$};
            \fill (end) circle (1.5pt) node[right] {$(a',b)$};
        
            % Top Path: lift(b,p)
            \draw[-latex] (start) to[out=40, in=135] 
                node[midway, above,black]
                    {$\fun{lift}(b,p)$} (end);
        
            % Bottom Path: ap(sec_b, p)
            \draw[-latex,
                thick,
                teal] (start) to[out=-45, in=-150] 
                node[midway, below,black]
                    {$\fun{ap}_{\fun{sec}_b}(p)$} (end);
        
            % The 2-path (Equality)
            \node at (2,0) {$\downarrow\eq{}$};
        \end{tikzpicture}
    \]
    For iii) observe that
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{lift}(b,p)) 
        \eq{} \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{ap}_{\fun{sec}_b}(p))
        \eq{} \fun{ap}_{\pi_1 \circ \fun{sec}_b}(p)
        \equiv \fun{ap}_{\fun{id}_A}(p)
        \eq{} p.
    \]
\end{rem}

\begin{lem}{\upshape[Dependent map]}\label{lem:dependent-map}
    Let\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$. If\/ $f\colon\prod_{x\colon A}P(x)$, then there is a map
    \[
        \fun{apd}_f\colon\prod_{x,y\colon A}\;
            \prod_{p\colon x\eq Ay}
                p_*(f(x))\eq{P(y)}f(y)
    \]
    satisfying $\fun{apd}_f(\fun{refl}_x)\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x)}$.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    Fix $a\colon A$ and consider the motive
    \begin{align*}
        C&\colon\prod_{a\colon A}(a\eq Ax)\to\univ\\
        C(x,p)&\defeq p_*(f(a))\eq{P(x)}f(x).
    \end{align*}
    Since
    \begin{align*}
        C(a,\fun{refl}_a)
            &\equiv (\fun{refl}_a)_*(f(a))\eq{P(a)}f(a)\\
            &\equiv f(a)\eq{P(a)}f(a)
                &&\text{; \eqref{eq:refl-*}},
    \end{align*}
    we can specify $c\defeq\fun{refl}_{f(a)}$ and obtain $\fun{apd}_f$ by based path induction.
\end{proof}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:constant-fibration}
    If\/ $P \colon A \to \univ$ is defined by\/ $P(x) \defeq B$ for a fixed\/ $B \colon \univ$, then for any\/ $x, y \colon A$ and\/ $p \colon x \eq A y$ and\/ $b \colon B$ we have a path
    \[
        \fun{transportconst}^B_p(b) \colon \fun{transport}^P(p, b) \eq B b
    \]
    satisfying\/ $\fun{transportconst}^B_{\fun{refl}_x}\defeq\lambda b.\,\fun{refl}_b$.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    See Exercise \ref{exr:constant-fibration}.
\end{proof}

\begin{lem}
    Let\/ $f\colon A\to B$ and define the constant family\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$ by\/ $P(x)\defeq B$. For any path\/ $p\colon x\eq Ay$, we have
    \[
        \fun{apd}_f(p)\eq{p_*(f(x))\eq B f(y)}
            \fun{transportconst}^B_p(f(x))\ct\fun{ap}_f(p).
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    First note that $C(x,p)$ is well defined because
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{apd}_f(p)&\colon p_*(f(x))\eq{P(y)}f(y)
            &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:dependent-map}.}\\
        \fun{transportconst}^B_p(f(x))&\colon p_*(f(x))\eq Bf(x)
            &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:constant-fibration}.}\\
        \fun{ap}_f(p)&\colon f(x)\eq Bf(y).
    \end{align*}
    Fix\/ $a\colon A$ and let\/ $C\colon\prod_{x\colon A}(a\eq Ax)\to\univ$ be defined by
    \[
        C(x,p)\defeq\fun{apd}_f(p)\eq{p_*(f(a))\eq Bf(x)}
            \fun{transportconst}^B_p(f(a))\ct\fun{ap}_f(p).
    \]
    To verify the base case:
    \begin{align*}
        C(a,\fun{refl}_a)
            &\equiv\fun{apd}_f(\fun{refl}_a)
                \eq{(\fun{refl}_a)_*(f(a))\eq Bf(a)}
                \fun{transportconst}^B_{\fun{refl}_a}(f(a))
                \ct\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_a)\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(a)}
                \eq{f(a)\eq Bf(a)}
                \fun{refl}_{f(a)}\ct\fun{refl}_{f(a)}\\
            &\equiv \fun{refl}_{f(a)}
                \eq{f(a)\eq Bf(a)}
                \fun{refl}_{f(a)}.
    \end{align*}
    Therefore, we can specify the base case\/ $c\defeq\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_{f(a)}}$ to complete the proof by based path induction.
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}
    We can represent the previous lemma in a propositionally commutative path diagram, where ``composition'' means concatenation:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=2.8cm,row sep=1.5cm]
            p_*(f(x))
                    \arrow[r,"\fun{transportconst}^B_p(f(x))"]
                    \arrow[rd,"\fun{apd}_f(p)"']&f(x)
                    \arrow[d,"\fun{ap}_f(p)"]\\
                &f(y)
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]    
\end{rem}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:transport-composition}
    Let\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$ be a type family. Given paths\/ $p\colon x\eq Ay$ and\/ $q\colon y\eq Az$, and a term\/ $u\colon P(x)$, we have
    \[
        q_*(p_*(u))\eq{P(z)}(p\ct q)_*(u).
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    First, observe that both sides of the equation inhabit $P(z)$. To prove equality, we fix $x\colon A$ and proceed by based path induction on $p$.

    The motive of the induction is the family of types defined by
    \begin{align*}
        D\colon&\prod_{y\colon A}(x\eq Ay)\to\univ\\ 
        D(y,p)\defeq&\prod_{u\colon P(x)}\;
        \prod_{z\colon A}\;\prod_{q\colon y\eq Az}
            q_*(p_*(u))\eq{P(z)}(p\ct q)_*(u).
    \end{align*}
        
    We must construct a term of type $D(x, \fun{refl}_x)$. Substituting $y$ with $x$ and $p$ with $\fun{refl}_x$, the goal becomes
    \[
        \prod_{u\colon P(x)}\;
            \prod_{z\colon A}\;
            \prod_{q\colon x\eq Az} 
                q_*((\fun{refl}_x)_*(u))\eq{P(z)}
                    (\fun{refl}_x\ct q)_*(u).
    \]
    Using the definitional equalities $(\fun{refl}_x)_*(u) \equiv u$ and $\fun{refl}_x\ct q \equiv q$, this reduces to
    \[
        \prod_{u\colon P(x)}\;
            \prod_{z\colon A}\;
                \prod_{q\colon x\eq Az}
                    q_*(u)\eq{P(z)}q_*(u),
    \]
    which is inhabited by $\lambda u,z,q.\,\fun{refl}_{q_*(u)}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:transportinv}
    Let\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$ be a type family. For any path\/ $p\colon x\eq{A}y$ and elements\/ $u\colon P(x)$ and\/ $v\colon P(y)$, there are paths
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transportinv}_l^P(p,u)
            &\colon (p^{-1})_*(p_*(u)) \eq{P(x)}u,\\
        \fun{transportinv}_r^P(p,v)
            &\colon p_*((p^{-1})_*(v)) \eq{P(y)}v.
    \end{align*}
    Moreover,
    \begin{alignat*}2
        \fun{transportinv}^P_l(\fun{refl}_x,u)
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_u,
        &\quad
        \fun{transportinv}^P_r(\fun{refl}_x,v)
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_v.
    \end{alignat*}
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    The expressions are well-typed: given $u\colon P(x)$ and $v\colon P(y)$, we have
    \begin{alignat*}{2}
        p_*(u) &\colon P(y), &\qquad (p^{-1})_*(v) &\colon P(x).
    \end{alignat*}
    
    We can now proceed by path induction on $p$. It suffices to assume $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case, definitionally, $p^{-1}\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. Since transport along reflexivity acts as the identity function, the left-hand side of the first identity type reduces as follows:
    \[
        (\fun{refl}_x)_*\bigl((\fun{refl}_x)_*(u)\bigr) \equiv (\fun{refl}_x)_*(u) \equiv u,
    \]
    The calculation for $v$ is identical. Thus, in both cases, the goal is proved by $\fun{refl}$.
    %
    
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}
    In calculus, the \textit{Chain Rule} establishes how to compute the derivative of a composition $P\circ f$ in the direction of a vector $v$
    \[
        d(P\circ f)_x(v) = dP_{f(x)}(df_x(v)).
    \]
    In more advanced Differential Geometry, this corresponds to the definition of \textit{pullback connection}: given a bundle $P$ over $B$ equipped with a connection (transport), and a map $f\colon A\to B$, we can create a \textit{pullback bundle} $f^*P$ over $A$. The natural way to transport objects in this new bundle $f^*P$ is simply to map the path into $B$ and use the original transport there:
    \[
        \nabla^{\text{pullback}}_v = \nabla^{\text{original}}_{f_*v}.
    \]
    In HoTT, the analogous statement is given by the following
\end{rem}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:post-composition-transport}
    For a function\/ $f \colon A \to B$, a type family\/ $P \colon B \to \univ$, and any\/ $p \colon x \eq A y$ and\/ $u \colon P(f(x))$, we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{P\circ f}(p,u) \eq{P(f(y))}
            \fun{transport}^P(\fun{ap}_f(p),u).
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    Since both sides of the equality are inhabitants of $P(f(y))$, we can proceed to proving it by path induction on $p$.
    
    For the motive, define
    \[
        C\colon \prod_{y\colon A} (x\eq A y)\to \univ
    \]
    by
    \[
        C(y,p) \defeq
            \prod_{u\colon P(f(x))}
                \fun{transport}^{P\circ f}(p,u) \eq{P(f(y))}
                    \fun{transport}^P(\fun{ap}_f(p),u).
    \]
    Evaluating at the base case, we have
    \begin{align*}
        C(x,\fun{refl}_x)
            &\equiv \prod_{u\colon P(f(x))}
                \fun{transport}^{P\circ f}(\fun{refl}_x,u)
                    \eq{P(f(x))}
                    \fun{transport}^P(\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_x),u) \\
            &\equiv \prod_{u\colon P(f(x))}
                u \eq{P(f(x))}
                    \fun{transport}^P(\fun{refl}_{f(x)},u) \\
            &\equiv \prod_{u\colon P(f(x))}
                u \eq{P(f(x))} u,
    \end{align*}
    which is inhabited by $\lambda u\colon P(f(x)).\,\fun{refl}_u$.
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:Pf-diagram}
    The lemma is illustrated in the following diagram
    \[
        \begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1.2,>=stealth,font=\small]
            \draw[thick,name path=A]
                (0.5,0) node[left] {$A$} to[out=10,in=170] (6,0);
                
            \draw[thick,name path=B]
                (0.5,2.0) node[left] {$B$} to[out=10,in=170] (6,2.0);
                
            \draw[gray,thin,name path=Pfx]
                (1,2) -- (1,5.5)
                node[above,black] {$P(f(x))$};
                
            \draw[gray,thin,name path=Pfy]
                (5,2) -- (5,5.5)
                node[above,black] {$P(f(y))$};
                
            \path[name path=Lx] (1,-0.5) -- (1,1);
            \path[name path=Ly] (5,-0.5) -- (5,1);
            
            \path [name intersections={of=A and Lx,by=x}];
            \fill (x) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$x$};
            
            \path [name intersections={of=A and Ly,by=y}];
            \fill (y) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$y$};
            
            \path [name intersections={of=B and Pfx,by=fx}];
            \fill (fx) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$f(x)$};
            
            \path [name intersections={of=B and Pfy,by=fy}];
            \fill (fy) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$f(y)$};
            
            \draw[-latex,gray,dashed] 
                (x) -- node[midway,left,black] {$f$} (fx);
            \draw[-latex,gray,dashed] 
                (y) -- node[midway,right,black] {$f$} (fy);
                
            \draw[-latex]
                (x) to[out=30,in=150]
                node[midway,above] {$p$} (y);
                
            \draw[-latex]
                (fx) to[out=30,in=150]
                node[midway,above] {$\fun{ap}_f(p)$} (fy);
                
            \coordinate (u) at (1, 3.7);
            \fill (u) circle (1.5pt) node[left] {$u$};
    
            \coordinate (v) at (5, 4);
            \fill (v) circle (1.5pt) node[right] {$(y,p_*(u))$};
    
            \draw[dashed,teal] (u) to[out=15,in=170]
                node[midway,above,black] {$\fun{lift}(u,p)$} (v);
    
            \coordinate (tu) at (5, 5.0);
            \fill (tu) circle (1.5pt) node[right,align=left] 
                {$\fun{transport}^{P\circ f}(p,u)$\\ 
                \quad$\eq{P(f(y))}
                    \fun{transport}^P(\fun{ap}_f(p),u)$};

            \draw[-latex,teal,thick] (v) -- (tu);
            
            \draw[-latex,orange,thick]
                (u) to[out=35,in=165] (tu);
        \end{tikzpicture}
    \]
\end{rem}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:dependent-post-composition-transport}
    Let\/ $P,Q\colon A\to\univ$ be type families and\/ $f\colon\prod_{x\colon A}P(x)\to Q(x)$ a family map. For any path\/ $p\colon x\eq A y$ and term\/ $u\colon P(x)$, we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^Q(p,f_x(u)) \eq{Q(y)} f_y(\fun{transport}^P(p,u)).
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    Since $\fun{transport}^P(p,u)\colon P(y)$, both sides inhabit $Q(y)$. Therefore, we can proceed with based path induction on $p$ to proving it.
    
    Fix $a\colon A$ and consider the motive 
    \begin{align*}
        C&\colon\prod_{x\colon A}(a\eq Ax)\to\univ\\
        C(x,p)&\defeq\prod_{u\colon P(a)}
            \fun{transport}^Q(p,f_a(u))\eq{Q(x)}
                f_x(\fun{transport}^P(p,u)).
    \end{align*}
    For the base case we obtain
    \begin{align*}
        C(a,\fun{refl}_a)
            &\equiv\prod_{u\colon P(a)}
                \fun{transport}^Q(\fun{refl}_a,f_a(u))\eq{Q(a)}
                    f_a(\fun{transport}^P(\fun{refl}_a,u))\\
            &\equiv\prod_{u\colon P(a)}f_a(u)\eq{Q(a)}f_a(u),
    \end{align*}
    which is inhabited by $\lambda u\colon P(a).\,\fun{refl}_{f_a(u)}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:general-post-composition-transport}
    Let\/ $A, A'\colon\univ$ be types, let\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ and\/ $B'\colon A'\to\univ$ be type families, and let\/ $g\colon A\to A'$ be a function. Given a family of functions\/ $h\colon\prod_{a\colon A}B(a)\to B'(g(a))$, a path\/ $p\colon x\eq{A}y$, and an element\/ $u\colon B(x)$, there is a path
    \[
        \fun{ap}_g(p)_*(h(x,u))\eq{B'(g(y))}h(y,p_*(u)).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    This theorem can be proved by combining Lemmas~\ref{lem:post-composition-transport} and~\ref{lem:dependent-post-composition-transport}. However, we provide an alternative proof below using path induction.

    First, let us verify that the equality is well-typed:
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{ap}_g(p)&\colon g(x)\eq{A'}g(y),\\
        \fun{ap}_g(p)_*
            &\equiv\fun{transport}^{B'}(\fun{ap}_g(p)).
    \end{align*}
    Therefore,
    \[
        \explain[B'(g(y))]
        {\fun{ap}_g(p)_*(\explain[B'(g(x))]{h(x,u)})}
        \eq{B'(g(y))}
        \explain[B'(g(y))]{h(y,\explain[B(y)]{p_*(u)})}.
    \]
    By path induction on $p$, we may assume $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case, $\fun{ap}_g(p)$ computes definitionally to $\fun{refl}_{g(x)}$. Since transport along reflexivity is the identity, both sides compute definitionally to $h(x,u)$, and the equality is witnessed by $\fun{refl}_{h(x,u)}$.
\end{proof}

\section{Function Homotopies}

\subsection{The Homotopy Relation}

\begin{ntn}
    Given a type family $P\colon A\to\univ$, we will sometimes denote the type of sections\footnote{Remark \ref{rem:section-type}.} $\prod_{x\colon A}P(x)$ by $\Gamma(P)$.
\end{ntn}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:homotopy}
    Let\/ $f,g\colon\prod_{x\colon A}P(x)$ be two sections of the family\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$. A \textsl{homotopy} from\/ $f$ to\/ $g$ is a dependent function of type
    \[
        f\sim g\defeq\prod_{x\colon A}f(x)\eq{P(x)}g(x).
    \]
\end{defn}

\begin{xmpl}\label{xmpl:refl-is-homotopy}
    For any function $f\colon A\to B$, the dependent function
    \[
        \lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{f(x)} \;\colon \prod_{x\colon A} f(x) \eq B f(x)
    \]
    is a homotopy from $f$ to $f$. This is often called the \textsl{reflexive homotopy}.
\end{xmpl}


\begin{xmpl}\label{xmpl:uniq-as-homotopy}${}$    
    As defined in \nref{lpar:Pi-types-over-product},
    \[
        \fun{uniq}_{A\times B}
            \colon(\pi_1,\pi_2)\sim\id_{A\times B},
    \]
    where $(\pi_1,\pi_2)\defeq\lambda x.\,(\pi_1(x),\pi_2(x))$.
\end{xmpl}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:homotopy-equivalence-relation}
    % Define a length to store the width of the longest subscript.
    \newlength{\maxsubwidth}
    % Measure the widest subscript (the third one) in scriptstyle (standard for limits).
    \settowidth{\maxsubwidth}{$\scriptstyle f,g,h\colon\Gamma(P)$}
    % Define a helper command to wrap the subscript in a centered box of that fixed width.
    \newcommand{\alignedprod}[1]{\prod_{\makebox[\maxsubwidth][c]{$\scriptstyle #1$}}}
    Homotopy is an equivalence relation on each dependent function type\/ $\prod_{x\colon A}P(x)$. That is, we have elements of the types
    \begin{align*}
        &\alignedprod{f\colon\Gamma(P)}
            f\sim f\\
        &\alignedprod{f,g\colon\Gamma(P)}
            (f\sim g)\to(g\sim f)\\
        &\alignedprod{f,g,h\colon\Gamma(P)}
            (f\sim g)\to(g\sim h)\to(f\sim h).
    \end{align*}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    We have the following inhabitants for each of the\/ $\Pi$-types:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textit{Reflexivity:}\/ $\lambda f\colon\Gamma(P).\,\lambda x\colon A.\,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}$.
        \item \textit{Symmetry:}\/ $\lambda f,g\colon\Gamma(P).\,\lambda \eta\colon f\sim g.\,\lambda x\colon A.\,\eta(x)^{-1}$.
        \item \textit{Transitivity:}\/ $\lambda f,g,h\colon\Gamma(P).\,\lambda\eta\colon f\sim g.\,\lambda\vartheta\colon g\sim h.\,\lambda x\colon A.\,\eta(x)\ct\vartheta(x)$.
    \end{itemize}
\end{proof}

\needspace{2\baselineskip}
\begin{defns}\label{defn:homotopy-inverse-and-ct}${}$
    \begin{itemize}
        \item Given a homotopy $\eta\colon f\sim g$, its \textsl{inverse} is the homotopy $\eta^{-1}\colon g\sim f$ defined by
        \[
            \eta^{-1}\defeq\lambda x.\,\eta(x)^{-1}.
        \]
        
        \item Given homotopies $\eta\colon f\sim g$ and $\vartheta\colon g\sim h$, their \textsl{composition} (a.k.a.\ \textsl{vertical concatenation}) is the homotopy $\eta\ct\vartheta\colon f\sim h$ defined by
        \[
            \eta\ct\vartheta\defeq\lambda x.\,
                \eta(x)\ct\vartheta(x).
        \]
    \end{itemize}
\end{defns}

\subsection{Types as Categories}\label{types-as-categories}

\label{rem:types-as-categories}
Types admit different interpretations: depending on the circumstances, they can be viewed as sets, propositions, or spaces. Another way to think of types is as categories. In this analogy we have
\begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
    \item[Objects.] These are the elements of the type: $x,y\colon A$ represent the objects that populate the category $A$.

    \item[Arrows.] Given two objects $x,y\colon A$, an arrow is a path $p\colon x\eq Ay$.

    \item[Composition.] Path composition corresponds to concatenation. Note that for paths\/ $p\colon x\eq{A}y$ and\/ $q\colon y\eq{A}z$, the concatenation\/ $p\ct q\colon x\eq{A}z$ is written in diagrammatic order, which reverses standard categorical notation. To align with categorical conventions, one may alternatively define\/ $q\circ p\defeq p\ct q$. Furthermore, this concatenation is propositionally associative.

    \item[Identity.] Given $x\colon A$ the identity for concatenation is $\fun{refl}_x$. Note that $\fun{refl}_x$ is the propositional unit of concatenation. 

    \item[Functors.] A function $f\colon A\to B$ acts as a functor between the corresponding categories:
    \begin{center}
        \begin{tabular}{lll}
            \small
            \textbf{Feature}
                &\textbf{Domain}
                &\textbf{Codomain}\\
            \hline\rule{0mm}{3.5mm}\small
            Objects
                &$x\colon A$
                &$f(x)\colon B$\\[0.7mm]
            \small
            Morphisms
                &$p\colon x\eq A y$
                &$\tilde f(p)\colon f(x)\eq Bf(y)$\\[0.7mm]
            \small
            Composition
                &$p\ct q$
                &$\tilde f(p)\ct\tilde f(q)$
        \end{tabular}
    \end{center}

    \item[Natural transformations.]\label{nat-transformation} These are the homotopies: given $f,g\colon A\to B$, a natural transformation between them is an inhabitant of the homotopy type $\eta\colon f\sim g$. To see this we need to show the (propositional) commutativity of the square
    \begin{equation}\label{tik:nat-transformation}
        \begin{tikzcd}
            f(x)
                    \arrow[r,"\fun{ap}_f(p)"]
                    \arrow[d,"\eta_x"']
                &f(y)
                    \arrow[d,"\eta_y"]\\
            g(x)
                    \arrow[r,"\fun{ap}_g(p)"']
                &g(y)
        \end{tikzcd}
    \end{equation}
    i.e., for every $p\colon x\eq Ay$, the type
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:nat-transformation}
        \fun{ap}_f(p)\ct\eta_y\eq{f(x)\eq Bg(y)}\eta_x\ct\fun{ap}_g(p)
    \end{equation}
    is inhabited. This follows by based path induction on $p$ using the motive $D\colon\prod_{y\colon A}(x\eq Ay)\to\univ$ defined by
    \[
        D(y,p)\defeq
            \fun{ap}_f(p)\ct\eta_y\eq{f(x)\eq Bg(y)}\eta_x\ct\fun{ap}_g(p),
    \]
    which satisfies
    \begin{align*}
        D(x,\fun{refl}_x)
            &\defeq\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_x)\ct\eta_x
                \eq{f(x)\eq Bg(x)}\eta_x\ct\fun{ap}_g(\fun{refl}_x)\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x)}\ct\eta_x
                \eq{f(x)\eq Bg(x)}\eta_x\ct\fun{refl}_{g(x)}\\
            &\equiv\eta_x\eq{f(x)\eq Bg(x)}\eta_x\ct\fun{refl}_{g(x)}.
    \end{align*}
    By Lemma~\ref{lem:right-unit-law}, $\fun{ru}(\eta_x)\colon\eta_x\ct\fun{refl}_{g(x)}\eq{f(x)\eq Bg(x)}\eta_x$. Hence, $\fun{ru}(\eta_x)^{-1}$ is an inhabitant of $D(x,\fun{refl}_x)$.\footnote{To achieve independence of our definition of concatenation, we could also have used the left unit law $\fun{lu}$, that satisfies $\fun{lu}(p)\colon\fun{refl}_x\ct p\eq{x\eq Ay}p$, arriving at $\fun{lu}(\eta_x)\ct\fun{ru}(\eta_x)^{-1}$.}
\end{description}

\subsection{The Algebra of Homotopies}

\begin{prop}{\upshape[Function whiskering]}\label{prop:whiskering}
    The homotopy relation is compatible with right and left composition:
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Right:] Given\/ $\eta\colon f\sim g$ and a right composable function\/ $h$, we have
        \[
            \eta\rwct h\defeq\lambda z.\,\eta(h(z))\colon f\circ h\sim g\circ h.
        \]
        \item[Left:] Given a left composable function\/ $h$ and\/ $\eta\colon f\sim g$, we have
        \[
            h\lwct\eta\defeq\lambda x.\,\fun{ap}_h(\eta(x))\colon h\circ f\sim h\circ g.
        \]
    \end{description}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    Assume that\/ $f,g\colon A\to B$ and let\/ $\eta\colon f\sim g$ be a homotopy.

    First, consider the case where\/ $h\colon C\to A$. Given\/ $z\colon C$, we have\/ $h(z)\colon A$ and therefore a path\/ $\eta(h(z))\colon f(h(z))\eq B g(h(z))$. Hence, the term\/ $\lambda z.\,\eta(h(z))$ is a well-defined witness of\/ $f\circ h\sim g\circ h$.

    For the case where\/ $h\colon B\to C$, the function\/ $\fun{ap}_h$ constructs a witness of the equality\/ $h(f(x))\eq C h(g(x))$ from the witness\/ $\eta(x)$ of\/ $f(x)\eq B g(x)$. Thus, the term\/ $\lambda x.\,\fun{ap}_h(\eta(x))$ is a well-defined witness of\/ $h\circ f\sim h\circ g$.
    
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:whiskering-with-id}
    In the particular case where $f\equiv g$ and $\eta\equiv\fun{refl}_f$, defined by $x\mapsto\fun{refl}_{f(x)}$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{refl}_f\rwct h
            &\equiv\lambda z.\,\fun{refl}_f(h(z))\\
            &\equiv\lambda z.\,\fun{refl_{f(h(z))}}\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f\circ h}
    \intertext{and}
        h\lwct\fun{refl}_f
            &\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{ap}_h(\fun{refl}_f(x))\\
            &\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{ap}_h(\fun{refl}_{f(x)})\\
            &\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{h(f(x))}
                &&\text{; Exr.~\ref{exr:ap-application} a)}\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{h\circ f}.
    \end{align*}
\end{rem}

\needspace{3\baselineskip}
\begin{prop}\label{prop:whiskering-distributivity}
    Function whiskering\footnote{Definition \ref{defn:homotopy-inverse-and-ct}.} preserves inverses and vertical composition.\footnote{Thus, function whiskering is a homomorphism of the groupoid structure of homotopies.}

    More precisely; let\/ $\eta\colon f\sim g$ and\/ $\vartheta\colon g\sim h$, then
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Right Whiskering:] Given\/ $k\colon A'\to A$, the following hold definitionally:
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item $(\eta^{-1})\rwct k\equiv(\eta\rwct k)^{-1}$.
            \item $(\eta\ct\vartheta)\rwct k\equiv(\eta\rwct k)\ct(\vartheta\rwct k)$.
        \end{enumerate}
        
        \item[Left Whiskering:] Given\/ $k\colon B\to B'$, we have homotopies:
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item $k\lwct(\eta^{-1})\sim(k\lwct\eta)^{-1}$.
            \item $k\lwct(\eta\ct\vartheta) \sim (k\lwct\eta)\ct(k\lwct\vartheta)$.
        \end{enumerate}
    \end{description}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    In the case of right whiskering, the properties follow immediately from $\lambda$-conversion:
    \begin{align*}
        (\eta^{-1}\rwct k)(x)
            &\equiv\eta^{-1}(k(x))\\
            &\equiv\eta(k(x))^{-1}\\
            &\equiv(\eta\rwct k)(x)^{-1}\\
            &\equiv(\eta\rwct k)^{-1}(x).
    \intertext{Similarly for composition:}
        ((\eta\ct\vartheta)\rwct k)(x)
            &\equiv(\eta\ct\vartheta)(k(x))\\
            &\equiv\eta(k(x))\ct\vartheta(k(x))\\
            &\equiv(\eta\rwct k)(x)\ct(\vartheta\rwct k)(x)\\
            &\equiv((\eta\rwct k)\ct(\vartheta\rwct k))(x).
    \end{align*}
    The properties for left whiskering follow pointwise from the functorial properties of $\fun{ap}_k$ (Proposition~\ref{prop:ap-properties}):
    \begin{align*}
        (k\lwct\eta^{-1})(x)
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_k(\eta(x)^{-1})\\
            &\eq{k(g(x))\eq{B'}k(f(x))} \fun{ap}_k(\eta(x))^{-1}\\
            &\equiv(k\lwct\eta)(x)^{-1}\\
            &\equiv(k\lwct\eta)^{-1}(x).
    \intertext{And for composition:}
        (k\lwct(\eta\ct\vartheta))(x) 
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_k(\eta(x)\ct\vartheta(x))\\
            &\eq{k(f(x))\eq{B'}k(h(x))} \fun{ap}_k(\eta(x))\ct\fun{ap}_k(\vartheta(x))\\
            &\equiv(k\lwct\eta)(x)\ct(k\lwct\vartheta)(x)\\
            &\equiv((k\lwct\eta)\ct(k\lwct\vartheta))(x).
    \end{align*}
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:whiskering-associativity}
  Given a homotopy\/ $\eta$ and appropriately composable functions\/ $h$ and\/ $k$, we have\footnote{Compare with Proposition~\ref{prop:path-whiskering-associativity}.}
  \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
      \item $(\eta\rwct h)\rwct k\equiv \eta\rwct(h\circ k)$.
      \item $k\lwct(h\lwct\eta)=(k\circ h)\lwct\eta$.
      \item $h\lwct(\eta\rwct k)\equiv(h\lwct\eta)\rwct k$.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    The first equation is a direct consequence of the definitions. The second follows from Proposition~\ref{prop:ap-properties}. For the third we have,
    \begin{align*}
        h\lwct(\eta\rwct k)
            &\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{ap}_h(\eta(k(x))\\
            &\equiv\lambda x.\,(h\lwct\eta)(k(x))\\
            &\equiv\lambda x.\,(h\lwct\eta)\circ k(x)\\
            &\equiv (h\lwct\eta)\rwct k.
    \end{align*}
\end{proof}

\subsection{Evaluating a homotopy on another homotopy}\label{homotopy-evaluated-on-homotopy}
Suppose that in the context where we have two function $f,g\colon A\to B$ and a homotopy $\eta\colon f\sim g$, we also have a third type $C$, two functions $u,v\colon C\to A$ and another homotopy $\vartheta\colon u\sim v$, as depicted in the diagram
\[
    \begin{tikzcd}
        C
                \arrow[r,"u",bend left=49]
                \arrow[r,"v"',bend right=49]
                \arrow[r,"\scriptstyle\vartheta",phantom]
            &A
                \arrow[r,"f",bend left=49]
                \arrow[r,"g"',bend right=49]
                \arrow[r,"\scriptstyle\eta",phantom]
            &B
    \end{tikzcd}
\]
For every $z\colon C$, we can plug the path $\vartheta(z)$ into the naturality equation \eqref{eq:nat-transformation} using the endpoints $x\defeq u(z)$ and $y\defeq v(z)$, and obtain
\[
    \fun{ap}_f(\vartheta(z))\ct\eta(v(z))
    \eq{}\eta(u(z))\ct\fun{ap}_g(\vartheta(z)).
\]
Thus, abstracting $z$ and using the whiskering notation, we deduce that
\begin{equation}\label{eq:homotopy-evaluated-on-homotopy}
     (f\lwct \vartheta)\ct(\eta\rwct v)
     \sim
     (\eta\rwct u)\ct(g\lwct\vartheta).
\end{equation}
is inhabited. This can be visualized as a commutative square where the vertices are functions and the edges homotopies:
\begin{equation}\label{tik:homotopy-evaluated-on-homotopy}
    \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge,row sep=huge]
        f\circ u
            \arrow[r,"\eta\rwct u"]
            \arrow[d,"f\lwct \vartheta"'] &
        g\circ u
            \arrow[d,"g\lwct \vartheta"] \\
        f\circ v
            \arrow[r,"\eta\rwct v"'] &
        g\circ v
    \end{tikzcd}
\end{equation}


\subsection{Sections of Path Spaces}

\begin{defn}
    Let $A$ be a type and $E\defeq\sum_{x,y\colon A}x\eq Ay$ its total path space. The \textsl{reflexivity section} $\rho_A$ is the map that assigns to every point its trivial loop:
    \[
        \rho_A\colon A\to E,
        \quad x\mapsto(x,x,\fun{refl}_x).
    \]
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}
    Let $C$ be a family over the path space $E$ of $A$. Given a dependent function $f$ defined on $E$
    \[
        f\colon\prod_{\omega\colon E}C(\omega),
    \]
    the composition of $f\circ\rho_A$ is the dependent function
    \[
        f\circ\rho_A\defeq\lambda x.\, f(x,x,\fun{refl}_x)
        \colon\prod_{x\colon A}C(x,x,\fun{refl}_x).
    \]
    
\end{rem}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:pre-composition-with-rho}
    With the preceding notation, let\/ $C\colon E\to\univ$ be a type family. Then given two dependent functions\/ $f,g\colon\prod_{\omega\colon E}C(\omega)$, if their compositions with\/ $\rho_A$ are homotopic, i.e.,
    \[
        f\circ\fun{\rho}_A\sim g\circ\fun{\rho}_A,
    \]
    then\/ $f\sim g$.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    By definition of homotopy, we must construct a term of type
    \[
        f(x,y,p) \eq{C(x,y,p)} g(x,y,p)
    \]
    for all $x,y \colon A$ and $p\colon x\eq Ay$.
    
    Fix $x \colon A$. By based path induction on $p$, it suffices to construct the term for the base case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case, the required type becomes
    \[
        f(x, x, \fun{refl}_x) \eq{C(x,x,\fun{refl}_x)} g(x, x, \fun{refl}_x),
    \]
    which is exactly the type inhabited by the hypothesis.
\end{proof}


\section{Equivalences}

\begin{defns}\label{defns:isequiv-qinv}${}$
    \begin{itemize}
        \item A function $f\colon A\to B$ is an \textsl{equivalence} if the type $\fun{isequiv}(f)$ is inhabited, where
        \[
            \fun{isequiv}(f)\defeq
                \Bigl(\sum_{g\colon B\to A}f\circ g \sim \id_B\Bigr)
                \times
                \Bigl(\sum_{h\colon B\to A}h\circ f\sim\id_A\Bigr).
        \]
    
        \item A \textsl{quasi-inverse} of a function $f \colon A \to B$ is a triple $\dep{g,(\eta,\vartheta)}$ consisting of a function $g\colon B\to A$ and homotopies $\eta\colon f\circ g\sim \id_B$ and $\vartheta\colon g\circ f\sim \id_A$. Formally, it is an inhabitant of the type
        \[
            \fun{qinv}(f)\defeq\sum_{g\colon B\to A}
                (f\circ g\sim\id_B)\times(g\circ f\sim\id_A).
        \]
    \end{itemize}
\end{defns}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:equivalence-of-quasi-inverses}
    If\/ $f\colon A\to B$ has two quasi-inverses
    \[
        \dep{g,(\eta,\vartheta)}\colon\fun{qinv}(f)
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        \dep{g',(\eta',\vartheta')}\colon\fun{qinv}(f),
    \]
    then\/ $g\sim g'$.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    Let\/ $y\colon B$. Since\/ $\eta'\colon f\circ g'\sim\id_B$, we have the path\/ $\eta'(y)^{-1}\colon y\eq B f(g'(y))$. Hence,
    \begin{align*}
        g(y)&\eq A g(f(g'(y)))
                &&\text{; by }\fun{ap}_g(\eta'(y)^{-1})\\
            &\equiv (g\circ f)(g'(y))\\
             &\eq A g'(y)
                &&\text{; by }\vartheta(g'(y)).
    \end{align*}
    Thus, $g \sim g'$.
\end{proof}

\begin{ntn}\label{ntn:quasi-inverse}
    Given a quasi-invertible function\/ $f\colon A\to B$, we will write\/ $f^{-1}$ to refer to an arbitrary quasi-inverse of\/ $f$. By\/ {\upshape Lemma~\ref{lem:equivalence-of-quasi-inverses}}, this notation is unambiguous up to homotopy.
\end{ntn}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:equivalence-composition}
    If\/ $f \colon A \to B$ and\/ $g \colon B \to C$ are equivalences with inhabitants
    \[
        (\dep{h_1,\eta_1},\dep{k_1,\vartheta_1})
            \colon\fun{isequiv}(f)
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        (\dep{h_2,\eta_2},\dep{k_2,\vartheta_2})
            \colon\fun{isequiv}(g),
    \]
    then their composition\/ $g\circ f$ is an equivalence inhabited by
    \[
        (\dep{h_1\circ h_2,\eta},\dep{k_1\circ k_2,\vartheta})
            \colon\fun{isequiv}(g\circ f),
    \]
    where the homotopies are defined by whiskering:
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:equivalence-composition}
        \begin{aligned}
            \eta&\defeq
                (g\lwct\eta_1\rwct h_2)\ct\eta_2
                    \colon g\circ f\circ h_1\circ h_2\sim\id_C\\
            \vartheta&\defeq
                (k_1\lwct\vartheta_2\rwct f)\ct\vartheta_1
                    \colon k_1\circ k_2\circ g \circ f\sim \id_A.
        \end{aligned}
    \end{equation}
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    The hypotheses provide the following homotopies:
    \begin{align*}
        \eta_1 &\colon f\circ h_1\sim\id_B, &
        \eta_2 &\colon g\circ h_2\sim\id_C, \\
        \vartheta_1 &\colon k_1\circ f\sim\id_A, &
        \vartheta_2 &\colon k_2\circ g\sim\id_B.
    \end{align*}
    Whiskering these yields the intermediate steps:
    \begin{align*}
        g\lwct\eta_1 &\colon g\circ f\circ h_1\sim g, \\
        \vartheta_2\rwct f&\colon k_2\circ g\circ f\sim f.
    \end{align*}
    By Proposition~\ref{prop:whiskering-associativity} (associativity of whiskering), we obtain:
    \begin{align*}
        g\lwct\eta_1\rwct h_2 &\colon g\circ f\circ h_1\circ h_2\sim g\circ h_2, \\
        k_1\lwct\vartheta_2\rwct f &\colon k_1\circ k_2\circ g\circ f\sim k_1\circ f.
    \end{align*}
    Finally, by Proposition~\ref{prop:homotopy-equivalence-relation} (homotopy transitivity), utilizing\/ $\eta_2$ and\/ $\vartheta_1$, we obtain the homotopies in~\eqref{eq:equivalence-composition}.
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:inverse-of-inverse-of-equivalence}
    Notation~\ref{ntn:quasi-inverse} allows us to restate Lemma~\ref{lem:equivalence-of-quasi-inverses} and the symmetry of the quasi-inverse definition as
    \[
        (f^{-1})^{-1}\sim f,
    \]
    whenever $f$ has a quasi-inverse.
\end{rem}



\begin{prop}\label{prop:qinv<->isequiv}
Let\/ $f\colon A\to B$. Then:
  \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
    \item There is a canonical map\/ $\fun{qinv}(f)\to\fun{isequiv}(f)$
        \begin{align*}
            \dep{g,(\eta,\vartheta)}
                \mapsto(\dep{g,\eta},\dep{g,\vartheta}).
        \end{align*}
    \item There is a map\/ $\fun{isequiv}(f)\to\fun{qinv}(f)$.
  \end{enumerate}
  Consequently, the type\/ $\fun{qinv}(f)$ is inhabited if, and only if, $\fun{isequiv}(f)$ is inhabited.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}${}$
  \begin{enumerate}[a)]
    \item This follows immediately from the definition, setting $h \defeq g$.

    \item Let $(\dep{g,\eta},\dep{h,\vartheta})\colon\fun{isequiv}(f)$. By definition, we have homotopies:
    \[
      \eta\colon f\circ g\sim\id_B
      \quad\text{and}\quad
      \vartheta\colon h\circ f\sim\id_A.
    \]
    Using the whiskering operations, we obtain:
    \begin{align*}
      h\lwct\eta &\colon h\circ f\circ g\sim h, \\
      \vartheta\rwct g &\colon h\circ f\circ g\sim g.
    \end{align*}
    Evaluating these at a point $y\colon B$ gives paths
    \[
       \fun{ap}_h(\eta(y))\colon h(f(g(y)))\eq B h(y)
       \quad\text{and}\quad
       \vartheta(g(y))\colon h(f(g(y)))\eq A g(y).
    \]
    We can therefore define a homotopy $\gamma\colon g\sim h$ by
    \[
        \gamma(y) \defeq \vartheta(g(y))^{-1} \ct \fun{ap}_h(\eta(y)).
    \]
    We now construct the required left homotopy $\vartheta'\colon g \circ f \sim \id_A$. For any $x\colon A$, we have the path $\gamma(f(x))\colon g(f(x))\eq A h(f(x))$. Concatenating this with $\vartheta(x)$ yields
    \[
      \gamma(f(x))\ct\vartheta(x)\colon g(f(x))\eq A x.
    \]
    Thus, we define the map to be $\dep{g,(\eta,\vartheta')}$, where $\vartheta'(x) \defeq \gamma(f(x))\ct\vartheta(x)$.
  \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:equivalence}
    An \textsl{equivalence} from $A$ to $B$ is a function $f\colon A\to B$ together with an inhabitant of $\fun{isequiv}(f)$, i.e., a proof that it is an equivalence. We write $A\simeq B$ for the type of equivalences from $A$ to $B$, i.e., the type
    \[
        A\simeq B\defeq\!\!\!\sum_{f\colon A\to B}\fun{isequiv}(f).
    \]
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}
    Two types $A$ and $B$ are \textsl{logically equivalent} when the type
    \[
        (A\to B)\times(B\to A)
    \]
    is inhabited. While equivalent types are logically equivalent, the reciprocal is not generally true.\footnote{See, however, Lemma~\ref{lem:mere-proposition-equivalence}.}
\end{rem}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:qinv-composition}
    The following properties hold
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\dep{\id_A,(\fun{refl}_{\id_A},\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}\colon\fun{qinv}(\id_A)$
        
        \item Given $f\colon A\to B$ and $g\colon B\to C$ we have,
        \[
            \left.\begin{aligned}
                \dep{f^{-1},(\eta_f,\vartheta_f)}
                    &\colon\fun{qinv}(f)\\
                \dep{g^{-1},(\eta_g,\vartheta_g)}
                    &\colon\fun{qinv}(g)
            \end{aligned}\right\}
            \implies\dep{g^{-1}\circ f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}
                \colon\fun{qinv}(g\circ f),
        \]
        where
        \begin{align*}
            \eta&\defeq
                (g\lwct\eta_f\rwct g^{-1})\ct\eta_g
                    \colon g\circ f\circ f^{-1}\circ g^{-1}\sim\id_C\\
            \vartheta&\defeq
                (f^{-1}\lwct\vartheta_g\rwct f)\ct\vartheta_f
                    \colon f^{-1}\circ g^{-1}\circ g\circ f\sim\id_A.
        \end{align*}
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{enumerate}[a)]
        \item By definition
        \[
            \fun{qinv}(\id_A)\equiv\sum_{g\colon A\to A}
                (\id_A\circ g\sim\id_A)
                \times(g\circ\id_A\sim\id_A).
        \]
        Since $\id_A\circ\id_A\equiv\id_A$, we can take $g\equiv\id_A$ and observe that
        \[
            \fun{refl}_{\id_A}\colon\id_A\eq{A\to A}\id_A
        \]
        defines the homotopy $x\mapsto\fun{refl}_x$ between $\id_A$ and itself.

        \item By Proposition~\ref{prop:qinv<->isequiv}, this is a direct consequence of Lemma~\ref{lem:equivalence-composition} applied to the case where $h_1\equiv k_1\equiv f^{-1}$ and $h_2\equiv k_2\equiv g^{-1}$.
    \end{enumerate}    
\end{proof}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:qinv-composition}
    Part b) of Proposition~\ref{prop:qinv-composition}, allows us to define the \textsl{composition} of quasi-inverses by
    \[
        \dep{f^{-1},(\eta_f,\vartheta_f)}
            \circ\dep{g^{-1},(\eta_g,\vartheta_g)}
            \defeq\dep{g^{-1}\circ f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}
    \]
    with
    \begin{align*}
        \eta&\defeq
            (g\lwct\eta_f\rwct g^{-1})\ct\eta_g\\
        \vartheta&\defeq
            (f^{-1}\lwct\vartheta_g\rwct f)\ct\vartheta_f.
    \end{align*}
\end{defn}

\begin{cor}\label{cor:qinv-composition-with-id}
    In the particular case where one of the functions is the identity, we have
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\dep{\id_A,(\fun{refl}_{\id_A},\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}\circ\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}\equiv\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta\ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}$

        \item $\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}\circ\dep{\id_A,(\fun{refl}_{\id_A},\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}\equiv\dep{f^{-1},(\eta\ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A},\vartheta)}$
    \end{enumerate}
\end{cor}

\needspace{2\baselineskip}
\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{enumerate}[a)]
        \item By definition,
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs&\equiv\dep{f^{-1},(\eta',\vartheta')}\\[1mm]
            \eta'&\equiv(f\lwct\fun{refl}_{\id_A}\rwct f^{-1})\ct\eta\\
                &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f\circ f^{-1}}\ct\eta
                    &&\text{; Rem.~\ref{rem:whiskering-with-id}}\\
                &\equiv\lambda x.\,
                    \fun{refl}_{f\circ f^{-1}(x)}\ct\eta(x)\\
                &\equiv\lambda x.\,\eta(x)\\
                &\equiv\eta.\\[1mm]
            \vartheta'&\equiv(\id_A\lwct\vartheta\rwct\id_A)
                    \ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A}\\
                &\equiv\vartheta\ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A}
                    &&\text{; Prop. \ref{prop:whiskering}}.
        \end{align*}

        \item Similarly,
        \begin{align*}
            \rhs&\equiv\dep{f^{-1},(\eta',\vartheta')}\\[1mm]
            \eta'&\equiv(\id_A\lwct\eta\rwct\id_A)
                    \ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A}\\
                &\equiv\eta\ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A}.
                    &&\text{; Prop. \ref{prop:whiskering}}\\[1mm]
            \vartheta'&\equiv
                (f^{-1}\lwct\fun{refl}_{\id_A}\rwct f)
                    \ct\vartheta\\
                &\equiv\vartheta
                    &&\text{; Idem part a)}
        \end{align*}
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}


\begin{ntn}\label{ntn:abuse-equivalence}
    We will sometimes abbreviate the equivalence
    \[
        \dep{f,(\dep{g,\eta},\dep{h,\vartheta})}
            \colon A\simeq B
    \]
    by writing simply\/ $f\colon A\simeq B$.
\end{ntn}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:equivalence-is-an-equivalence-relation}
    Type equivalence is an equivalence relation on\/ $\univ$. More specifically:
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item For any\/ $A$, the identity function\/ $\id_A$ is an equivalence; hence\/ $A\simeq A$.
        
        \item For any\/ $f\colon A\simeq B$, we have an equivalence\/ $f^{-1}\colon B\simeq A$.
        
        \item For any\/ $f\colon A\simeq B$ and\/ $g\colon B\simeq C$, we have\/ $g\circ f\colon A\simeq C$.
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{enumerate}[a)]
        \item Let\/ $\fun{refl} \defeq \lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_x$. Since\/ $\id_A \circ \id_A \equiv \id_A$, we clearly have a homotopy\/ $\fun{refl}\colon \id_A\circ\id_A\sim\id_A$.
        Therefore,
        \[
            (\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}},\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}})
                \colon\fun{isequiv}(\id_A).
        \]
        Hence,
        \[
            \dep{
                \id_A,
                (
                    \dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}},
                    \dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}}
                )
            }
            \colon A\simeq A.
        \]

        \item Suppose that $f\colon A\simeq B$. Then,
        \begin{align*}
            \dep{f,\omega}&\colon A\simeq B
                &&\text{; Notn.~\ref{ntn:abuse-equivalence}}\\
            \omega\equiv(\dep{g,\eta},\dep{h,\vartheta})
                &\colon\fun{isequiv}(f)
                &&\text{; Defns.~\ref{defn:equivalence} \& \ref{defns:isequiv-qinv}}\\
            \dep{g,(\eta,\vartheta')}&\colon\fun{qinv}(f)
                &&\text{; Prop.~\ref{prop:qinv<->isequiv}}\\
            \dep{f,(\vartheta',\eta)}&\colon\fun{qinv}(g)
                &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:equivalence-of-quasi-inverses}}\\
            \dep{g,(\dep{f,\vartheta'},\dep{f,\eta})}
                &\colon B\simeq A
                &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:equivalence-of-quasi-inverses}}.
        \end{align*}

        \item Suppose that\/ $f\colon A\simeq B$ and\/ $g\colon B\simeq C$. This translates into
        \begin{align*}
            \dep{f,(\dep{h_1,\eta_1},\dep{k_1,\vartheta_1})}
                &\colon A\simeq B, &
            \dep{g,(\dep{h_2,\eta_2},\dep{k_2,\vartheta_2})}
                &\colon B\simeq C,
        \end{align*}
        with
        \begin{align*}
            \eta_1 &\colon f\circ h_1\sim\id_B, &
            \eta_2 &\colon g\circ h_2\sim\id_C, \\
            \vartheta_1 &\colon k_1\circ f\sim\id_A, &
            \vartheta_2 &\colon k_2\circ g\sim\id_B.
        \end{align*}
        Then, we have the intermediate homotopies:
        \begin{align*}
            g\lwct\eta_1 &\colon g\circ f\circ h_1\sim g, &
            \vartheta_2\rwct f &\colon k_2\circ g\circ f\sim f.
        \end{align*}
        By Proposition~\ref{prop:whiskering-associativity} (associativity of whiskering), we obtain:
        \begin{align*}
            g\lwct\eta_1\rwct h_2 &\colon g\circ f\circ h_1\circ h_2\sim g\circ h_2, \\
            k_1\lwct\vartheta_2\rwct f &\colon k_1\circ k_2\circ g\circ f\sim k_1\circ f.
        \end{align*}
        By Proposition~\ref{prop:homotopy-equivalence-relation} (homotopy transitivity), utilizing\/ $\eta_2$ and\/ $\vartheta_1$, we deduce that
        \[
            (g\circ f)\circ(h_1\circ h_2)\sim \id_C
            \quad\text{and}\quad
            (k_1\circ k_2)\circ(g\circ f)\sim\id_A
        \]
        are inhabited. Thus, according to Notation~\ref{ntn:abuse-equivalence}, we have\/ $g\circ f\colon A\simeq C$.
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:id-equivalence-inverse}
    Given that $\dep{g,(\eta,\vartheta)}\colon\fun{qinv}(f)\iff\dep{f,(\vartheta,\eta)}\colon\fun{qinv}(g)$,
    we deduce that $\dep{f,(\dep{g,\eta},\dep{g,\vartheta})}^{-1}\equiv\dep{g,(\dep{f,\vartheta},\dep{f,\eta})}$. In particular,
    \[
        \dep{\id_A,
        (\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}},\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}})}^{-1}
        \equiv\dep{\id_A,
        (\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}},\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}})}.
    \]
\end{rem}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:half-adjoint-equivalence}
    Let\/ $f\colon A\to B$ be a function. A \emph{coherent quasi-inverse} (a.k.a.~\textsl{half-adjoint equivalence}) of\/ $f$ consists of a quasi-inverse\/ $\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}$ along with a higher homotopy
    \[
        \tau\colon\prod_{x\colon A}
            \fun{ap}_f(\vartheta_x)\eq{f(f^{-1}(f(x)))
                \eq Bf(x)}\eta_{f(x)}.
    \]
    as illustrated next
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge]
            f(f^{-1}(f(x)))
                    \arrow[r,
                        bend left=45,
                        "\fun{ap}_f(\vartheta_x)"{name=U,above}]
                    \arrow[r,
                        bend right=45,
                        "\eta_{f(x)}"{name=D,below}]
            &f(x)
                    \arrow[Rightarrow,
                        from=U,to=D,
                        "\tau_x",
                        shorten <=6pt,
                        shorten >=6pt]
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    Using function whiskering [cf.~Proposition~\ref{prop:whiskering}], the coherence term $\tau$ can be seen as an homotopy
    \[
        \tau\colon f\lwct\vartheta\sim\eta\rwct f.
    \]
\end{defn}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:coherent-quasi-inverse}
    Let\/ $f\colon A\to B$ be an equivalence. If $\dep{g,(\eta,\vartheta)}$ is a quasi-inverse of $f$, there is an homotopy $\eta'\colon f\circ g\sim\id_B$, such that $\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta)}$ is a coherent quasi-inverse.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    By definition, $g\colon B\to A$, $\eta\colon f\circ g\sim\id_B$, and $\vartheta\colon g\circ f\sim\id_A$.

    We define the new right homotopy $\eta'\colon f\circ g\sim\id_B$ by requiring the following diagram of homotopies to commute:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge, row sep=large]
            f\circ g\circ f\circ g
                \arrow[r,"f\lwct\vartheta\rwct g"]
                \arrow[d,"\eta\rwct(f\circ g)"'] &
            f\circ g
                \arrow[d,"\eta"] \\
            f\circ g
                \arrow[r,"\eta'"',dashed] &
            \id_B
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    To complete the proof, we need to show an inhabitant of $f\lwct\vartheta\sim\eta'\rwct f$. By right-whiskering the diagram defining $\eta'$ with $f$, we obtain:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge, row sep=large]
            f\circ g\circ f\circ g\circ f
                \arrow[r,"f\lwct\vartheta\rwct(g\circ f)"]
                \arrow[d,"\eta\rwct(f\circ g\circ f)"'] &
            f\circ g\circ f
                \arrow[d,"\eta\rwct f"] \\
            f\circ g\circ f
                \arrow[r,"\eta'\rwct f"'] &
            f
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    This reduces our goal to proving that $f\lwct\vartheta$ fits the bottom edge of this square.

    Evaluating the naturality of $\eta$ on the homotopy $f\lwct\vartheta\colon f\circ g\circ f\sim f$, as defined in \eqref{tik:homotopy-evaluated-on-homotopy}, yields the commutative square:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge, row sep=large]
            f\circ g\circ f\circ g\circ f
                \arrow[r,"f\lwct(g\circ f)\lwct\vartheta"]
                \arrow[d,"\eta\rwct(f\circ g\circ f)"'] &
            f\circ g\circ f
                \arrow[d,"\eta\rwct f"] \\
            f\circ g\circ f
                \arrow[r,"f\lwct\vartheta"'] &
            f
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    Comparing the last two diagrams reduces the goal to showing that their top edges are homotopic; that is,
    \[\tag{$\ast$}
        f\lwct\vartheta\rwct(g\circ f)
        \sim f\lwct(g\circ f)\lwct\vartheta.
    \]
    Evaluating the naturality of $\vartheta$ on itself using \eqref{tik:homotopy-evaluated-on-homotopy} gives
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge,row sep=large]
            (g\circ f)\circ(g\circ f)
                \arrow[r,"\vartheta\rwct(g\circ f)"]
                \arrow[d,"(g\circ f)\lwct\vartheta"'] &
            g\circ f
                \arrow[d,"\vartheta"] \\
            g\circ f
                \arrow[r,"\vartheta"']
                &\id_A
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    By canceling $\vartheta$, we deduce that $\vartheta\rwct(g\circ f)\sim(g\circ f)\lwct\vartheta$. The conclusion~($\ast$) follows by whiskering this homotopy with $f$ on the left.
\end{proof}


\begin{thm} {\upshape[Transport as a coherent equivalence]}
    \label{thm:coherent-transport}
    Let\/ $A$ be a type. Given a path\/ $p\colon x\eq Ay$ and a type family\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$, the transport function
    \[
        f\defeq\fun{transport}^P(p,\dummy)\colon P(x)\to P(y)
    \]
    is a half-adjoint equivalence with quasi-inverse
    \[
        g\defeq\fun{transport}^P(p^{-1},\dummy)\colon P(y)\to P(x)
    \]
    and homotopies
    \[
        \eta\colon f\circ g\sim\id_{P(y)}
        \quad\text{and\/}\quad
        \vartheta\colon g\circ f\sim\id_{P(x)}.
    \]
    together with the coherence condition
    \[
        \tau\colon f\lwct\vartheta\sim\eta\rwct f.
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    By path induction on $p$, to construct $\eta$, $\vartheta$ and $\tau$, it suffices to assume that $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. Under this assumption, the inverse path $p^{-1}$ is also definitionally $\fun{refl}_x$. The functions $f$ and $g$ both reduce definitionally to $\id_{P(x)}$. Consequently, the compositions $f\circ g$ and $g\circ f$ evaluate to $\id_{P(x)}$, allowing us to define the homotopies as reflexivity:
    \begin{align*}
        \eta&\defeq v\mapsto\fun{refl}_v\\
        \vartheta&\defeq u\mapsto\fun{refl}_u
    \end{align*}
    Substituting these into the coherence condition leads to the goal
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{\id_{P(x)}}(\fun{refl}_u)\eq{u\eq{P(x)}u}
            \fun{refl}_{u}.
    \]
    Since $\fun{ap}_{\id_{P(x)}}(\fun{refl}_u)\equiv\fun{refl}_u$, this type reduces to $\fun{refl}_u\eq{u\eq{P(x)}u}\fun{refl}_u$, which is trivially inhabited by $\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_u}$. The conclusion follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:f-equiv-implies-apf-equiv}
    If\/ $f\colon A\to B$ is an equivalence, then for any\/ $a,a'\colon A$, the function
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f\colon(a\eq Aa')\to(f(a)\eq Bf(a'))
    \]
    is also an equivalence.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    Let $\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}$ be a quasi-inverse of $f$. By Theorem~\ref{thm:coherent-quasi-inverse}, we may assume this quasi-inverse is coherent, providing a homotopy $\tau\colon f\lwct\vartheta\sim\eta\rwct f$.

    For the inverse function $h\colon(f(a)\eq Bf(a'))\to(a\eq Aa')$ consider
    \[
        h(q)\defeq\vartheta_a^{-1}\ct\fun{ap}_{f^{-1}}(q)\ct\vartheta_{a'}.
    \]

    To construct a right homotopy $\fun{ap}_f\circ h\sim\id_{f(a)\eq Bf(a')}$, let $q\colon f(a)\eq Bf(a')$. Using the fact that $\fun{ap}_f$ distributes over concatenation, we obtain
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f(h(q))
        \eq{f(a)\eq Bf(a')}
        \fun{ap}_f(\vartheta_a)^{-1}
            \ct\fun{ap}_{f\circ f^{-1}}(q)
            \ct\fun{ap}_f(\vartheta_{a'}).
    \]
    Substituting the coherence $\tau$ evaluated at $a$ and $a'$ yields
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f(h(q))
