        \eq{f(a)\eq Bf(a')}
        \eta_{f(a)}^{-1}
            \ct\fun{ap}_{f\circ f^{-1}}(q)
            \ct\eta_{f(a')}.
    \]
    The naturality equation \eqref{eq:nat-transformation} for $\eta\colon f\circ f^{-1}\sim\id_B$ evaluated on $q$ states that
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{f\circ f^{-1}}(q)\ct\eta_{f(a')}
        \eq{f(f^{-1}(f(a)))\eq Bf(a')}
        \eta_{f(a)}\ct q.
    \]
    Left-concatenating with $\eta_{f(a)}^{-1}$, we recover the \rhs of the previous equation. Thus,
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f(h(q))\eq{f(a)\eq Bf(a')}q.
    \]

    To construct a left homotopy $h\circ\fun{ap}_f\sim\id_{a\eq Aa'}$, let $p\colon a\eq Aa'$. The definition of $h$ yields
    \[
        h(\fun{ap}_f(p))
        \eq{a\eq Aa'}
        \vartheta_a^{-1}
            \ct\fun{ap}_{f^{-1}\circ f}(p)
            \ct\vartheta_{a'}.
    \]
    The naturality of $\vartheta$ evaluated on $p$ states that
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{f^{-1}\circ f}(p)
            \ct\vartheta_{a'}
        \eq{f^{-1}(f(a))\eq Aa'}
        \vartheta_a\ct p.
    \]
    Left-concatenating with $\vartheta_a^{-1}$, we obtain
    \[
        \vartheta_a^{-1}
            \ct\fun{ap}_{f^{-1}\circ f}(p)
            \ct\vartheta_{a'}
        \eq{a\eq Aa'}
        p.
    \]
    Therefore, $h(\fun{ap}_f(p))\eq{a\eq Aa'}p$, which completes the proof.
\end{proof}

\section{Observational Equality Framework}
In classical Type Theory, equality is often regarded as \textit{opaque}---essentially a mystery. It is defined as \emph{intensional} (not to be confused with intentional), meaning that for two objects to be equal, they must follow the exact same construction.

Homotopy Type Theory attempts to bridge this gap. By interpreting the inhabitants of the type $x\eq Ay$ as paths from $x$ to $y$ in the \textit{space} $A$, it becomes possible to determine when two objects behave equivalently, independent of their specific construction. This shared behavioral appearance is termed \textit{observational equality}. The rest of this chapter is dedicated to describing the observational equality for each of the basic types introduced in Chapter~1.

Technically, the strategy involves using the $\fun{transport}$ function to construct a homotopy between the actual identity type (which remains intensional) and a description relative to the type's internal structure. This description acts as a specific \emph{implementation}, encoding an equivalent equality that is no longer intensional (opaque), but \textit{observational} (visible).

To achieve this for each basic type, we define a type $\fun{Code}(x,y)$ associated with the identity $x\eq Ay$. We then prove that $\fun{Code}(x,y)\simeq(x\eq Ay)$. This process requires defining an $\fun{encode}$ function (derived from $\fun{transport}$) and a quasi-inverse $\fun{decode}$ that maps in the opposite direction, from $\fun{Code}(x,y)$ to $x\eq Ay$.

This approach consists of the following

\subsection{Observational Equality Framework}\label{observational-framework}
\begin{description}
    [font=\normalfont\scshape]
    \item[Code family.]
    Define a family that structurally represents the identity type:
    \[
        \fun{Code} \colon A \to A \to \univ.
    \]

    \item[Base code.]
    Select an element that corresponds to reflexivity:
    \[
        c \colon\fun{Code}(x,x).
    \]

    \item[Encode function.]
    For any $x,y\colon A$ and path $p\colon x\eq{A}y$, define the map
    \[
        \fun{encode}\colon (x\eq{A}y) \to \fun{Code}(x,y).
    \]
    Applying transport to the base code $c$ with $C_x\defeq\lambda z.\,\fun{Code}(x,z)\colon A\to\univ$, we obtain
    \[
        \fun{encode}(p) \defeq \fun{transport}^{C_x}(p, c) \colon C_x(y).
    \]
    Note that, by definition of transport, $\fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x) \equiv c$.

    \item[Decode function.]
    Construct a quasi-inverse to $\fun{encode}$
    \[
        \fun{decode} \colon \prod_{y\colon A} \fun{Code}(x,y) \to (x\eq{A}y).
    \]
\end{description}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:framework-qinv}
    Given $x,y\colon A$, we have to verify that the functions
    \[
        \fun{encode}(x,y)\colon(x\eq Ay)\to\fun{Code}(x,y)
    \]
    and
    \[
        \fun{decode}(x,y)\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to(x\eq Ay)
    \]
    satisfy
        \[
            \fun{decode}(x,y,\fun{encode}(x,y,p))\eq{x\eq Ay}p,
        \]
        for $p\colon x\eq Ay$, and
        \[
            \fun{encode}(x,y,\fun{decode}(x,y,d))\eq{\fun{Code}(x,y)}d,
        \]
    for $d\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)$.
\end{rem}

\begin{rem}
    The $\fun{decode}$ function acts as an \textit{introduction rule} (or constructor) for the identity type of points in the space $A$, as it generates paths from structured data. Establishing that $\fun{encode}$ and $\fun{decode}$ are quasi-inverses justifies an \textit{induction principle}: to prove a property for all paths, it suffices to consider those constructed by $\fun{decode}$. Conversely, the $\fun{encode}$ function serves as an \textit{elimination rule}, extracting structural features from a given path.
\end{rem}

\subsection{Extended Observational Framework}\label{extended-framework}

There are two additional requirements to the \nameref{observational-framework} that imply further properties of the pair $\fun{encode}$/$\fun{decode}$. They are requirements to be fulfilled for arbitrary $x,y\colon A$.

\begin{center}
    \begin{tabular}{ll}
        \textsc{Inversion map:}
            &$\fun{inv}\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to\fun{Code}(y,x)$\\
            [1.5ex]
        \textsc{Concatenation:}
            &$\ect\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to\fun{Code}
            (y,z)\to\fun{Code}(x,z)$\\
            [1.5ex]
        \textsc{Unit laws:}
            &$\fun{inv}(c)\equiv c
            \quad\text{\&}\quad
            c\ect d\equiv d$
    \end{tabular}    
\end{center}
where $c\colon\fun{Code}(x,x)$ is the base code and the unit laws hold for $d\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)$.\footnote{In some cases the second unit law is relaxed to $c\ect d\eq{\fun{Code}(x,z)}d$.}


\begin{defn}{[Groupoid]}
    A \textsl{groupoid} is a category in which every morphism is an isomorphism. 
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}
    In Homotopy Type Theory, every type $A$ constitutes a (weak) groupoid,\footnote{See also Remark~\ref{rem:types-as-categories}.} often called the \textsl{fundamental groupoid} of $A$:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \textit{Objects:} The terms $a, b \colon A$.
        \item \textit{Morphisms:} The paths $p\colon a\eq Ab$.
        \item \textit{Identity:} The reflexivity path $\fun{refl}_a$.
        \item \textit{Composition:} Path concatenation $(p,q)\mapsto p\ct q$.
        \item \textit{Inverse:} Path inversion $p\mapsto p^{-1}$.
    \end{itemize}
    Note that in HoTT, the groupoid laws hold only \textit{propositionally} (up to a path one level higher), not structurally (definitionally). This is why types are formally called \textsl{$\infty$-groupoids}.
\end{rem}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:extended-framework}
    Let the tuple\/ $(A,\fun{Code}, c,\fun{encode}, \fun{decode}, \fun{inv}, {}\ect{})$ be defined as in the\/ {\upshape Extended Observational Equality Framework}. Then the\/ $\fun{decode}$ function preserves the groupoid structure of identity types:
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\itshape]
        \item[Reflexivity:] $\fun{decode}(x, x, c)\eq{x\eq Ax}\fun{refl}_x$.
        \item[Symmetry:] $\fun{decode}(y,x,\fun{inv}(d)) \eq{y\eq Ax}\fun{decode}(x,y,d)^{-1}$.
        \item[Transitivity:] $\fun{decode}(x,z,d\ect e)\eq{x\eq Az}\fun{decode}(x,y,d) \ct \fun{decode}(y, z, e)$.
    \end{description}
\end{thm}

\needspace{2\baselineskip}
\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\itshape]

        \item[Reflexivity.]
        By the definition in the framework,
        \[
            \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x)
                \equiv
                \fun{transport}^{C_x}(\fun{refl}_x,c)\equiv c.
        \]
        Applying $\fun{decode}$ to both sides yields
        \[
            \fun{refl}_x\eq{x\eq Ay}\fun{decode}(x,x,c).
        \]

        \item[Symmetry.]
        Consider the equality
        \[
            \fun{encode}(p^{-1})
            \eq{\fun{Code}(x,y)}
            \fun{inv}(\fun{encode}(p)).
        \]
        To prove it by path induction on $p$ it suffices to assume $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$:
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs &\equiv \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x^{-1}) \equiv \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x) \equiv c.\\
            \rhs &\equiv \fun{inv}(\fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x)) \equiv \fun{inv}(c).
        \end{align*}
        By the hypothesis $\fun{inv}(c) \equiv c$, the \lhs and \rhs are definitionally equal.
        Thus, $\fun{encode}$ preserves inverses. The result follows applying $\fun{decode}$.

        \item[Transitivity.]
        Consider
        \[
            \fun{encode}(p\ct q)
            \eq{\fun{Code}(x,y)}
            \fun{encode}(p)\ect\fun{encode}(q).
        \]
        By path induction on $p$, assume $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. Then
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs&\equiv\fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x\ct q)
                \equiv\fun{encode}(q).\\
            \rhs&\equiv
                \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x)\ect\fun{encode}(q)
                \equiv c \ect \fun{encode}(q).
        \end{align*}
        By the hypothesis $c\ect d\equiv d$, and so the \rhs reduces to $\fun{encode}(q)$. Thus, $\fun{encode}$ preserves concatenation. Applying $\fun{decode}$ to both sides yields the conclusion. \qedhere
    \end{description}
\end{proof}

\section{Equality in Cartesian Products}\label{equality-in-cartesian-products}

In this section we apply the observational framework \ref{observational-framework} to the product $A\times B$.

\textsc{Code family:}
\begin{align*}
    \fun{Code}&\colon(A\times B)\to(A\times B)\to\univ\\
    \fun{Code}(x,y)&\defeq
        (\pi_1(x)\eq A\pi_1(y))
        \times
        (\pi_2(x)\eq B\pi_2(y)).
\end{align*}

\textsc{Base code:}
\[
    c\defeq(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)})
        \colon\fun{Code}(x,x).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
    c\equiv(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_x)
        ,\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_x)).
\]

\textsc{Encode function:}

For $C_x\defeq\fun{Code}(x,\dummy)$, the encode function becomes
\begin{align*}
    \fun{encode}&\colon(x\eq{A\times B}y)\to\fun{Code}(x,y)\\
    \fun{encode}(p)
        &\defeq\fun{transport}^{C_x}(p,c).
\end{align*}
In particular, for $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$, we obtain
\begin{align*}
    \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x)
        &\equiv\fun{transport}^{C_x}
            (\fun{refl}_x,c)\\
        &\equiv c\\
        &\equiv(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_x)
            ,\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_x)),
\end{align*}
which implies, by induction on $p$, that
\[
    \fun{encode}(p)\eq{\fun{Code}(x,y)}(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(p)
        ,\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(p)).
\]
We define the function
\begin{align*}
        \fun{pair}^\times\colon\prod_{x,y\colon A\times B}
            (x\eq{A\times B}y)
            &\to\fun{Code}(x,y)\\
        (x,y,p)&\mapsto
            (\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(p),\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(p))\\
        (x,x,\fun{refl}_x)&\mapsto
            (\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)}),
    \end{align*}
and adopt it as our implementation of $\fun{encode}$.


The following function \textit{constructs} a path between pairs from paths between their components:
\[
    \fun{pair}^=\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to (x\eq{A\times B}y).
\]
It is defined as follows:
\begin{enumerate}[-]
    \item By induction on\/ $x$, it is enough to consider the case where\/ $x$ is a pair\/ $(a,b)$. In this case, we must define a function of type
    \[
        \prod_{y:A\times B}
            \big(
            (a\eq A\fun{\pi}_1(y))\times(b\eq B\fun{\pi}_2(y)) 
            \big)
            \to\big((a,b)\eq{A\times B}y\big).
    \]
    \item Now, by induction on\/ $y$, we reduce to the case where\/ $y$ is a pair\/ $(a',b')$. That is, we must define a function of type
    \[
        \big((a\eq Aa')\times(b\eq Bb')\big)
        \to\big((a,b)\eq{A\times B}(a',b')\big).
    \]
    \item Since the domain is a product type, we can curry the function. This means we need to specify a dependent function of type
    \[
        \prod_{p\colon a\eq Aa'}\;
        \prod_{q\colon b\eq Bb'}
            (a,b)\eq{A\times B}(a',b').
    \]
    \item Path induction on\/ $p$ allows us to reduce the definition to the case where\/ $a'\equiv a$ and\/ $p\equiv \fun{refl}_a$. Thus, we must define a dependent function of type
    \[
        \prod_{q\colon b\eq Bb'}(a,b)\eq{A\times B}(a,b').
    \]
    \item Finally, by path induction on\/ $q$, this reduces to the case where\/ $b'\equiv b$ and\/ $q\equiv\fun{refl}_b$. We are left to define a single term of type
    \[
        (a,b)\eq{A\times B}(a,b).
    \]
    \item This is accomplished by choosing the reflexivity path
    \[
        \fun{refl}_{(a,b)}.
    \]
\end{enumerate}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:AxB-goal-reduction}
    The type
    \[
        \prod_{x,y\colon A\times B}\;
        \prod_{\omega\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)}
        P(x,y,\omega)
    \]
    is inhabited if, and only if, for all\/ $a\colon A$ and\/ $b\colon B$, the term
    \[
        P((a,b),(a,b),(\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b))
    \]
    has a witness.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    By induction on $x$, it suffices to consider the case where $x\equiv(a,b)$. The goal becomes
    \[
        \prod_{y\colon A\times B}\;
        \prod_{\omega\colon(a\eq A\pi_1(y))
        \times(b\eq B\pi_2(y))}
        P((a,b),y,\omega).
    \]
    Similarly, induction on $y$ reduces the goal to the case where $y\equiv(a',b')$
    \[
        \prod_{\omega\colon(a\eq Aa')
        \times(b\eq Bb')}
        P((a,b),(a',b'),\omega).
    \]
    The same reasoning allows us to decompose $\omega$ into components $(p,q)$ and find a section of:
    \[
        \prod_{p\colon a\eq Aa'}\;\prod_{q\colon b\eq Bb'}
        P((a,b),(a',b'),(p,q)).
    \]
    Path induction on $p$ contracts the endpoint $a'$ to $a$ and the path to $\fun{refl}_a$, yielding
    \[
        \prod_{q\colon b\eq Bb'}P((a,b),(a,b'),(\fun{refl}_a,q)).
    \]
    Finally, path induction on $q$ contracts $b'$ to $b$, leaving us with
    \[
        P((a,b),(a,b),(\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b)),
    \]
    as desired.
\end{proof}


\begin{thm}
    Let\/ $A,B\colon\univ$ be two types. For any\/ $x,y\colon A\times B$, the function\/ $\fun{pair}^\times(x,y)$ is an equivalence with quasi-inverse\/ $\fun{pair}^=(x,y)$. Consequently:
    \[
        (x\eq{A\times B}y)\simeq\fun{Code}(x,y).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    We must show that $\fun{pair}^\times$ and $\fun{pair}^=$ are quasi-inverses.
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\fun{pair}^=(x,y)\circ\fun{pair}^\times(x,y)\sim\id$.
         
        We have to prove that
        \[
            \prod_{x,y\colon A\times B}\;\prod_{p\colon x\eq{A\times B}y}
                \bigl(\fun{pair}^=(x,y)\circ\fun{pair}^\times(x,y)\bigr)(p)\eq{x\eq{A\times B}y}p.
        \]
        By path induction it suffices to consider the case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$, which reduces the goal to
        \[
            \bigl(\fun{pair}^=(x,x)\circ\fun{pair}^\times(x,x)\bigr)(\fun{refl}_x)
                \eq{x\eq{A\times B}x}\fun{refl}_x.
        \]
        By the definitions of $\fun{pair}^\times$ and $\fun{pair}^=$, we have
        \begin{align*}
            \bigl(\fun{pair}^=(x,x)\circ\fun{pair}^\times(x,x)\bigr)(\fun{refl}_x)
                &\equiv\fun{pair}^=(x,x,\fun{pair}^\times(x,x,\fun{refl}_x))\\
                &\equiv\fun{pair}^=(x,x,
                    (\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)}
                    ,\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)}))\\
                &\equiv \fun{refl}_{(\pi_1(x),\pi_2(x))}.
        \end{align*}
        Let $\alpha\colon(\pi_1(x),\pi_2(x))\eq{A\times B}x$ be the path given by the uniqueness principle. The action on paths $\fun{ap}$ of the map $\fun{refl}\defeq z\mapsto\fun{refl}_z$ applied to $\alpha$ yields:
        \[
            \fun{ap}_{\fun{refl}}(\alpha)
                \colon\fun{refl}_{(\pi_1(x),\pi_2(x))}
                \eq{x\eq{A\times B}x}\fun{refl}_x.
        \]

        \item $\fun{pair}^\times(x,y)\circ\fun{pair}^=(x,y)\sim\id$.
        
        We have to prove that
        \[
            \prod_{x,y\colon A\times B}\;
            \prod_{\omega\colon(\pi_1(x)\eq A\pi_1(y))\times (\pi_2(x)\eq B\pi_2(y))}
                \bigl(\fun{pair}^\times(x,y)\circ\fun{pair}^=(x,y)\bigr)(\omega)
                \eq{}\omega.
        \]
        Applying Lemma~\ref{lem:AxB-goal-reduction}, the goal reduces to
        \begin{align*}
            \bigl(\fun{pair}^\times((a,b)&,(a,b))\circ\fun{pair}^=((a,b),(a,b))\bigr)
            (\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b)\\
                &\equiv\fun{pair}^\times\bigl((a,b),(a,b),
                   \fun{pair}^=((a,b),(a,b),(\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b))
                    \bigr)\\
                &\equiv\fun{pair}^\times((a,b),(a,b),\fun{refl}_{(a,b)})\\
                &\equiv(\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b).
        \end{align*}
        Thus, the output matches the input, as desired.
    \end{enumerate}
    Since both composites are homotopic to the identity, $\fun{pair}^=\colon\fun{qinv}(\fun{pair}^\times)$.
    %
    
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}\label{cor:cartesian-uniqueness}
    Given $x\colon A\times B$, we have
    \[
        x\eq{A\times B}(\pi_1(x),\pi_2(x)).
    \]
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
    Take $y\defeq(\pi_1(x),\pi_2(x))\colon A\times B$. Then
    \[
        \pi_1(y)\equiv\pi_1(x)
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        \pi_2(y)\equiv\pi_2(x).
    \]
    Therefore,
    \[
        (\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)})\colon
        (\pi_1(x)\eq A\pi_1(y))\times(\pi_2(x)\eq B\pi_2(y)),
    \]
    and the theorem implies that $\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)})\colon x\eq{A\times B}y$.
    %
    
\end{proof}

\textbf{Extended framework}. To apply the extended framework \ref{extended-framework} we set
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}&\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to\fun{Code}(y,x)\\
    \fun{inv}(p,q)&\defeq(p^{-1},q^{-1})\\
\intertext{and}
    \ect&\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to\fun{Code}(y,z)
        \to\fun{Code}(x,z)\\
    (p,q)\ect(p',q')&\defeq(p\ct p',q\ct q'),
\end{align*}
which are clearly well defined. Moreover
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}(c)&\equiv
        \fun{inv}(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},
            \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)})\\
        &\equiv(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)}^{-1},
            \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)}^{-1})\\
        &\equiv(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},
            \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)})\\
        &\equiv c
\intertext{and, for $d\equiv(p,q)$, we have}
    c\ect d&\equiv(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)}\ct p,
        \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)}\ct q)\\
        &\equiv(p,q).
\end{align*}

\begin{rem}
    The following table is a summary of the functions introduced above:
    
    \vspace{-0.7\baselineskip}
    \small
    \[
        \begin{tabular}{lll}
            \hline
            &\textbf{Function}
            &\textbf{Definition}\\
            \hline\\[-3.5mm]
             $\fun{pair}^\times$
            & Encode
            &
            $(x\eq{A\times B}y)\to\fun{Code}(x,y)$\\
            $c$
            & Base code
            &$(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},
                \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)})$\\
            $\fun{pair}^=$
            & Decode
            &
            $\fun{Code}(x,y)\to(x\eq{A\times B}y)$\\
            $\fun{inv}$
            & Inverse
            & $(p,q)\mapsto(p^{-1},q^{-1})$\\
            ${}\ect{}$
            & Concatenation
            &$(p,q)\ect(p',q')\equiv(p\ct p',q\ct q')$\\
            \hline
        \end{tabular}
    \]
    \normalsize
\end{rem}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:product-groupoid-functor}
    Let\/ $A,B\colon\univ$. Then, for all\/ $x,y,z\colon A\times B$, and paths
    \begin{alignat*}{2}
        p&\colon\pi_1(x)\eq A\pi_1(y),\quad& p'&\colon\pi_1(y)\eq A\pi_1(z),\\
        q&\colon\pi_2(x)\eq B\pi_2(y),\quad& q'&\colon\pi_2(y)\eq B\pi_2(z),
    \end{alignat*}
    \needspace{2\baselineskip}
    we have
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)})\equiv\fun{refl}_x$
        \item $\fun{pair}^=(p^{-1},q^{-1})\eq{A\times B}\fun{pair}^=(p,q)^{-1}$
        \item $\fun{pair}^=(p\ct p',q\ct q')\eq{A\times B}\fun{pair}^=(p,q)\ct\fun{pair}^=(p',q')$
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    This is a corollary of Theorem~\ref{thm:extended-framework}.\footnote{Note also that parts b) and c) are easily derived from Lemma~\ref{lem:AxB-goal-reduction}.}
\end{proof}
    
\begin{prop}\label{prop:pair-properties}
    Let\/ $A,B\colon\univ$. Then, for all\/ $x,y,z\colon A\times B$, the following equality types are inhabited:
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item For any\/ $p\colon\pi_1(x)\eq A\pi_1(y)$ and\/ $q\colon\pi_2(x)\eq B\pi_2(y)$,
        \[ \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{pair}^=(p,q))\eq A p \]
        
        \item For any\/ $p\colon\pi_1(x)\eq A\pi_1(y)$ and\/ $q\colon\pi_2(x)\eq B\pi_2(y)$,
        \[ \fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(\fun{pair}^=(p,q))\eq B q \]
        
        \item For any\/ $r\colon x\eq{A\times B}y$,
        \[ \fun{pair}^=(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(r), \fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(r))\eq{A\times B}r \]
        
        \item For any\/ $r\colon x\eq{A\times B}y$,
        \[ \fun{pair}^=(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(r)^{-1}, \fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(r)^{-1})\eq{A\times B}r^{-1} \]
        
        \item For any\/ $r\colon x\eq{A\times B}y$ and\/ $s\colon y\eq{A\times B}z$,
        \[ \fun{pair}^=(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(r)\ct\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(s), \fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(r)\ct\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(s))\eq{A\times B}r\ct s \]
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\needspace{3\baselineskip}
\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item We must show that $\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{pair}^=(p,q))\eq A p$. By Lemma~\ref{lem:AxB-goal-reduction}, it suffices to check the case where $x\equiv y \equiv (a,b)$, $p\equiv\fun{refl}_a$, and $q\equiv\fun{refl}_b$. The equality holds definitionally:
        \begin{align*}
            \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b))
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_{(a,b)})\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_a.
        \end{align*}
        
        \item Analogous to i), replacing $\pi_1$ with $\pi_2$.
        
        \item We proceed by path induction on $r$. It suffices to prove the case where $y\equiv x$ and $r\equiv\fun{refl}_x$:
        \[
            \fun{pair}^=(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_x),\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_x)) \eq{x\eq{A\times B}x} \fun{refl}_x.
        \]
        This reduces to
        \[
            \fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)}) \eq{x\eq{A\times B}x} \fun{refl}_x,
        \]
        whose inhabitation is granted by part a) of Proposition~\ref{prop:product-groupoid-functor}.
        
        \item This follows from part b) of Proposition~\ref{prop:product-groupoid-functor} by path induction on~$r$.
        
        \item We proceed by path induction on both\/ $r$ and\/ $s$. It suffices to consider the base case where\/ $y\equiv x$ and\/ $z\equiv x$, and both paths are the reflexivity path\/ $\fun{refl}_x$. The goal reduces to proving
        \[
            \fun{pair}^=(\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_x)\ct\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_x), \fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_x)\ct\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_x)) \eq{A\times B} \fun{refl}_x\ct\fun{refl}_x.
        \]
        By the definitional equalities for the action on paths and the concatenation of reflexivity paths, this simplifies to
        \[
            \fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(x)}, \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(x)}) \eq{A\times B} \fun{refl}_x,
        \]
        whose inhabitation is granted by part a) of Proposition~\ref{prop:product-groupoid-functor}.
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}


\begin{ntn}
    Given type families\/ $A,B \colon Z\to\univ$, we denote by\/ $A\times B\colon Z\to\univ$ the type family defined by\/ $(A\times B)(z)\defeq A(z)\times B(z)$.
\end{ntn}

\begin{thm}
    Fix $z\colon Z$ and $x\colon(A\times B)(z)$. Then, for $w\colon Z$ and $p\colon z\eq Zw$, we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{A\times B}(p, x) \eq{A(w)\times B(w)}
        (\fun{transport}^A(p, \pi_1(x)), \fun{transport}^B
            (p, \pi_2(x))).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    By based path induction on $p$ it suffices to consider the case $w\equiv z$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_z$. According to \nref{lpar:transport}, the goal becomes
    \begin{align*}
        x\eq{A(z)\times B(z)}(\pi_1(x),\pi_2(x)).
    \end{align*}
    Hence, the conclusion follows from Corollary~\ref{cor:cartesian-uniqueness}.
    %
    
\end{proof}



\begin{defn}
    Given functions\/ $f\colon A \to A'$ and\/ $g\colon B \to B'$, we define the \textsl{product} function
    \[
        f\times g\colon A\times B\to A'\times B'
    \]
    by its action on elements:
    \[
        (f\times g)(x)\defeq(f(\pi_1(x)),g(\pi_2(x))).
    \]
    In particular, $f\times g(a,b)\equiv (f(a),g(b))$ for $a\colon A$ and $b\colon B$.
\end{defn}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:pair-fxg}
    Let\/ $f\colon A\to A'$ and\/ $g\colon B\to B'$ be two functions.
    Given\/ $x,y\colon A\times B$ and\/ $\rho\colon(\pi_1(x)\eq A\pi_1(y))\times(\pi_2(x)\eq B\pi_2(y))$, we have
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{f\times g}(\fun{pair}^=(\rho))
        \eq{A'\times B'}
        \fun{pair}^=(\fun{ap}_f(\pi_1(\rho)),\fun{ap}_g(\pi_2(\rho))).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    By Lemma~\ref{lem:AxB-goal-reduction}, it suffices to consider the case where\/ $x\equiv y\equiv(a,b)$ and\/ $\rho\equiv(\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b)$. In this case, the goal becomes
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{f\times g}(\fun{pair}^=
        (\fun{refl}_a,\fun{refl}_b))
        \eq{A'\times B'}
        \fun{pair}^=(\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_a),\fun{ap}_g(\fun{refl}_b)).
    \]
    Computing the terms, we have:
    \begin{itemize}
        \item \lhs: $\fun{ap}_{f\times g}(\fun{refl}_{(a,b)}) \equiv \fun{refl}_{(f(a),g(b))}$.
        \item \rhs: $\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_{f(a)}, \fun{refl}_{g(b)}) \equiv \fun{refl}_{(f(a),g(b))}$.
    \end{itemize}
    Thus, $\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_{(f(a),g(b))}}$ is a witness of the target identity type.
\end{proof}

\section{Equality in the Boolean Type}\label{equality-in-the-boolean-type}

To characterize the identity type of the booleans, we instantiate the \nameref{observational-framework}.

\textsc{Code family:}
    We define the code family $\fun{Code}\colon\fun2\to\fun2\to\univ$ by double induction on $\fun2$:
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{Code}(0_{\fun2}, 0_{\fun2}) &\defeq \fun1 & \fun{Code}(0_{\fun2}, 1_{\fun2}) &\defeq \fun0 \\
        \fun{Code}(1_{\fun2}, 0_{\fun2}) &\defeq \fun0 & \fun{Code}(1_{\fun2}, 1_{\fun2}) &\defeq \fun1.
    \end{align*}

\textsc{Base code:}
    The base code $c_x\colon\fun{Code}(x,x)$ is defined by induction on $x\colon\fun2$ as\footnote{Since $\fun{Code}(x,x)$ is not definitionally equal to $\fun1$, and $c_x$ must be of type $\fun{Code}(x,x)$, we cannot define it as the constant map $\lambda x.\,\fun\star$.}
    \[
        c_{0_{\fun2}} \defeq \fun\star \quad\text{and}\quad c_{1_{\fun2}} \defeq \fun\star.
    \]

\textsc{Encode function:}
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{encode}\colon\prod_{x,y\colon\fun2}(x\eq{\fun2}y)
            &\to\fun{Code}(x,y)\\
        (x,y,p)&\mapsto\fun{transport}^{C_x}(p,c_x),
    \end{align*}
    which is well-defined because $C_x(y)\equiv\fun{Code}(x,y)$.

\textsc{Decode function:} It proceeds by double induction on $x$ and $y$:
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{decode}\colon\prod_{x,y\colon\fun2}\fun{Code}(x,y)
            &\to(x\eq{\fun2}y)\\
        (0_{\fun2},0_{\fun2},\fun\star)
            &\mapsto\fun{refl}_{0_{\fun2}}\\
        (0_{\fun2},1_{\fun2},\zeta)
            &\mapsto\fun{rec}_{\fun0}(\zeta)\\
        (1_{\fun2},0_{\fun2},\zeta)
            &\mapsto\fun{rec}_{\fun0}(\zeta)\\
        (1_{\fun2},1_{\fun2},\fun\star)
            &\mapsto\fun{refl}_{1_{\fun2}}
    \end{align*}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:bool-equality}
    For any $x,y\colon\fun2$, the functions $\fun{encode}(x,y)$ and $\fun{decode}(x,y)$ are quasi-inverses.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    Following Remark~\ref{rem:framework-qinv}, we must verify that the compositions are pointwise homotopic to the respective identity functions.

    First, let $p\colon x\eq{\fun2}y$. By path induction on $p$, it suffices to check the case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. By definition of $\fun{encode}$, we have
    \[
        \fun{encode}(x,x,\fun{refl}_x) \equiv c_x.
    \]
    \needspace{2\baselineskip}
    By induction on $x$:
    \begin{enumerate}[-]
        \item If $x\equiv0_{\fun2}$, then $c_{0_{\fun2}}\equiv\fun\star$, and $\fun{decode}(0_{\fun2},0_{\fun2},\fun\star)\equiv\fun{refl}_{0_{\fun2}}$.
        
        \item If $x\equiv1_{\fun2}$, then $c_{1_{\fun2}}\equiv\fun\star$, and $\fun{decode}(1_{\fun2},1_{\fun2},\fun\star)\equiv\fun{refl}_{1_{\fun2}}$.
    \end{enumerate}
    Thus, $\fun{decode}(x,x,\fun{encode}(x,x,\fun{refl}_x))\eq{}\fun{refl}_x$.

    Second, let $d\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)$. We proceed by double induction on $x$ and $y$:
    \begin{enumerate}[-]
        \item If $x,y\equiv0_{\fun2}$, then $d\colon\fun1$ and induction on $d$ yields $\fun{decode}(0_{\fun2},0_{\fun2},\fun\star)\equiv\fun{refl}_{0_\fun2}$. Thus, 
        \[
            \fun{encode}(
                0_{\fun2},
                0_{\fun2},
                \fun{decode}(0_{\fun2},0_{\fun2},\fun\star)
                )
            \equiv\fun{encode}(
                0_{\fun2},
                0_{\fun2},
                \fun{refl}_{0_{\fun2}}
                )
            \equiv c_{0_{\fun2}}
            \equiv\fun\star.
        \]

        \item If $x,y\equiv1_{\fun2}$, then $d\colon\fun1$ and induction on $d$ yields $\fun{decode}(1_{\fun2},1_{\fun2},\fun\star)\equiv\fun{refl}_{1_\fun2}$. Thus,
        \[
            \fun{encode}(
                1_{\fun2},
                1_{\fun2},
                \fun{decode}(1_{\fun2},1_{\fun2},\fun\star)
                )
            \equiv\fun{encode}(
                1_{\fun2},
                1_{\fun2},
                \fun{refl}_{1_{\fun2}}
                )
            \equiv c_{1_{\fun2}}\equiv\fun\star.
        \]
        
        \item If $x\equiv1_{\fun2}$ and $y\equiv0_{\fun2}$, or the other way around, then $d\colon\fun0$, and the goal is vacuously satisfied.
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\textbf{Extended framework}. We define:

    \textsc{Inversion map:}
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{inv}\colon\prod_{x,y\colon\fun2}&\fun{Code}(x,y)
            \to\fun{Code}(y,x)\\
        &\begin{array}{cccc}
            x & y & \zeta & \fun{inv}(x,y,\zeta) \\
            \hline
            0_{\fun2} & 0_{\fun2} & \zeta & \zeta \\
            1_{\fun2} & 1_{\fun2} & \zeta & \zeta \\
            0_{\fun2} & 1_{\fun2} & \zeta & \fun{rec}_{\fun0}(\zeta) \\
            1_{\fun2} & 0_{\fun2} & \zeta & \fun{rec}_{\fun0}(\zeta) \\
        \end{array}
    \intertext{\textsc{Concatenation:}}
        {\ect}\colon\prod_{x,y,z\colon\fun2}&\fun{Code}(x,y)
            \to\fun{Code}(y,z) \to \fun{Code}(x,z)\\
        &\qquad u\mapsto v\mapsto u\ect v\\
        &\begin{array}{cccc}
            x&y&u&u\ect v\\
            \hline
            0_{\fun2}&0_{\fun2}&\fun1&v\\
            1_{\fun2}&1_{\fun2}&\fun1&v\\
            0_{\fun2}&1_{\fun2}&\fun0&\fun{rec}_{\fun0}(u)\\
            1_{\fun2}&0_{\fun2}&\fun0&\fun{rec}_{\fun0}(u)
        \end{array}
    \end{align*}
    \needspace{2\baselineskip}
    \textsc{Unit laws:}

    To show that $\fun{inv}(x,x,c_x)\eq{\fun{Code}(x,x)}c_x$ it suffices to consider the cases $x\equiv0_{\fun2}$ and $x\equiv1_{\fun2}$. In both cases $c_x\equiv\fun\star$, and $\fun{inv}(x,x,\fun\star)\equiv\fun\star$ by definition.

    To show that $c_x\ect v\eq{\fun{Code}(x,z)}v$, by induction on $x$, we must only verify the cases $x\equiv0_{\fun2}$ and $x\equiv1_{\fun2}$, where the concatenation satisfies $c_x\ect v\equiv v$ by definition.


\section{Equality in \textSigma-Types}\label{equality-in-Sigma-types}

Let $A\colon\univ$ be a type and $P\colon A\to\univ$ a type family. Given a path $p\colon\omega\eq E\omega'$ between points $\omega$ and $\omega'$ in the total space $E\defeq\sum_{x\colon A}P(x)$, the behavior of the first and second projections is asymmetric. While $\pi_1$ yields a path $\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(p)\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega')$, the second components $\pi_2(\omega)$ and $\pi_2(\omega')$ cannot be compared because they inhabit the fibers $P(\pi_1(\omega))$ and $P(\pi_1(\omega'))$, which are not necessarily the same type.

\begin{defn}
    Let $P\colon A\to\univ$ be a type family and let $E\defeq\sum_{x\colon A}P(x)$ be its total space.
    For any $x\colon A$, the \textsl{fiber inclusion} is defined as
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{in}_x&\colon P(x)\to E\\
        \fun{in}_x(u)&\defeq\dep{x,u}.
    \end{align*}
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:fiber-inclusion}
    The fiber inclusion embeds the fiber $P(x)$ into the total space. Consequently, given a path $\gamma\colon u\eq{P(x)} v$ in the fiber, the functorial action $\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}$ yields a path $\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}(\gamma)\colon\dep{x,u}\eq E\dep{x,v}$ in the total space.
\end{rem}

\separator

Applying the observational framework \ref{observational-framework} to the total space $E$ we define the

\textsc{Code family:}
\begin{align*}
    \fun{Code}
        &\colon E\to E\to\univ\\
    \fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')
        &\defeq\sum_{q\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega')}
            \fun{transport}^P(q,\pi_2(\omega))
            \eq{P(\pi_1(\omega'))}
            \pi_2(\omega').
\end{align*}

\textsc{Base code:}
\[
    c\defeq
        \dep{
            \fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)}, \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}
        }
        \colon\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega).
\]
Another way to express the first component of $c$ is by observing that
\[
    \fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)}\equiv\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\omega).
\]
For the second component of $c$, since $\pi_2$ is a dependent function,\footnote{See \nref{lpar:Sigma-induction}, equation \eqref{eq:Sigma-pi-2}.} we have to use the dependent application map $\fun{apd}$.\footnote{See Lemma~\ref{lem:dependent-map}.} Thus, $\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}\equiv\fun{apd}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_\omega)$ and $c$ can be written as
\[
    c\equiv
        \dep{
            \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_\omega),\fun{apd}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_\omega)
        }.
\]

\textsc{Encode function:}
The transport family\/ $C_\omega\defeq\fun{Code}(\omega,\dummy)$ yields
\begin{align*}
    \fun{encode}&\colon(\omega\eq{E}\omega') \to \fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')\\
    \fun{encode}(p) &\defeq \fun{transport}^{C_\omega}(p, c).
\end{align*}
In particular, for $\omega'\equiv\omega$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_\omega$, we obtain
\begin{align*}
    \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_\omega)
        &\equiv\fun{transport}^{C_\omega}(\fun{refl}_\omega,c)\\
        &\equiv c\\
        &\equiv\dep{\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_\omega)
            ,\fun{apd}_{\pi_2}(\fun{refl}_\omega)}.
\end{align*}
Hence, path induction on $p$ implies that
\[
    \fun{encode}(p)\eq{\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')}
        \dep{
            \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(p),\fun{apd}_{\pi_2}(p)
        }.
\]
Therefore, we take the \rhs to define the encode function
\begin{align*}
        f&\colon\prod_{\omega,\omega'\colon E}
            (\omega\eq E\omega')
            \to\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')\\
        f(\omega,\omega',p)&\defeq
            \dep{
                \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(p),\fun{apd}_{\pi_2}(p)
            },
    \end{align*}
which satisfies:
\[
    f(\fun{refl}_\omega)\equiv
        \dep{
            \fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)},
            \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}
        }.
\]  

\textsc{Decode function:}

We have to define a backward function
\[
    g\colon\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')\to(\omega\eq E\omega').
\]
Let $u\defeq\pi_2(\omega)$ and $v\defeq\pi_2(\omega')$. The domain is the type of pairs $\dep{q,\gamma}$ where $q\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega')$ and $\gamma\colon q_*(u)\eq{P(\pi_1(\omega'))}v$.

By induction on $\omega$ and $\omega'$, it suffices to consider the case where $\omega\equiv\dep{x,u}$ and $\omega'\equiv\dep{y,v}$. The domain is then the type of pairs $\dep{q,\gamma}$ where $q\colon x\eq Ay$ and $\gamma\colon q_*(u)\eq{P(y)}v$.
    
We proceed in two steps:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item By the Path Lifting Theorem~\ref{thm:path-lift}, we have
    \[
        \alpha\defeq\fun{lift}(u,q)
            \colon\dep{x,u}\eq E\dep{y,q_*(u)}.
    \]
    
    \item We need to connect $\dep{y,q_*(u)}$ to $\dep{y,v}$. Since these two points share the same first component, we can use the fiber inclusion function [cf.~Remark~\ref{rem:fiber-inclusion}] to obtain a vertical path:
    \[
        \beta\defeq\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_{y}}(\gamma)
            \colon\dep{y,q_*(u)}\eq E\dep{y,v}.
    \]
\end{enumerate}
We can now define $g$ by concatenating both paths:
\[
    g(\dep{q,\gamma})\defeq\alpha\ct\beta.
\]
Here is a picture illustrating the construction
\[
    \begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1.2,>=stealth,font=\small]
        \draw[thick,name path=A]
            (0,0) to[out=10,in=170] (6,0)
            node[right] {$A$};
        
        \draw[gray,thin,name path=Px]
            (1,-0.5) -- (1,4.5)
            node[above,black] {$P(x)$};
        \draw[gray,thin,name path=Py]
            (5,-0.5) -- (5,4.5)
            node[above,black] {$P(y)$};
    
        \path [name intersections={of=A and Px,by=x}];
        \fill (x) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {};
    
        \path [name intersections={of=A and Py,by=y}];
        \fill (y) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {};
        
        \fill (x) circle (1.5pt)
            node[above left] {$x\equiv\pi_1(\omega)$};
        \fill (y) circle (1.5pt)
            node[above right] {$y \equiv \pi_1(\omega')$};
        
        \draw[-latex]
            (x) to[out=40,in=145]
            node[midway,above] {$q$} (y);
    
        \coordinate (u) at (1,2);
        \fill (u) circle (2pt)
            node[left] {$\omega\equiv\dep{x,u}$};
    
        \coordinate (qu) at (5,2.2);
        \fill[gray] (qu) circle (1.5pt)
            node[right,black] {$\dep{y,q_*(u)}$};
    
        \coordinate (v) at (5,3.8);
        \fill (v) circle (2pt)
            node[above right] {$\omega'\equiv\dep{y,v}$};
    
        \draw[-latex,teal,thick,dashed]
            (u) to[out=15,in=165] 
            node[midway,above,sloped,black] 
                {$\alpha\defeq\fun{lift}(u,q)$} (qu);
    
        \draw[-latex,teal,thick]
            (qu) -- 
            node[midway,right,black]
                {$\beta\defeq\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_y}(\gamma)$} (v);
        
        \draw[-latex,orange,thick]
            (u) to[out=45,in=180] 
            node[pos=0.70,above left,text=black]
                {$g(\dep{q,\gamma})\defeq\alpha\ct\beta$} (v);
    \end{tikzpicture}
\]

\begin{rem}
    By Theorem~\ref{thm:path-lift} and Proposition~\ref{prop:ap-properties}, respectively, we know that $\fun{lift}(\dep{u,\fun{refl}_x})\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}}$ and $\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}(\fun{refl}_u)\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}}$. Therefore,
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:Sigma-trivial-decoding}
        g(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u})
            \equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}}.
    \end{equation}
\end{rem}

\textbf{Note.} What follows is a generalization of Lemma~\ref{lem:AxB-goal-reduction} to $\Sigma$-types.

\begin{lem}\label{lem:Sigma-goal-reduction}
    Let\/ $E\defeq\sum_{x\colon A}P(x)$. For any type family\/ $Q(x,\omega',\varepsilon)$, the type
    \[
        \prod_{\omega,\omega'\colon E}\;
        \prod_{\varepsilon\colon\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')}
        Q(\omega,\omega',\varepsilon)
    \]
    is inhabited if, and only if, for all\/ $x\colon A$ and\/ $u\colon P(x)$, the term
    \[
        Q(\dep{x,u},\dep{x,u},\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u})
    \]
    has a witness.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    By induction on $\omega$, it suffices to consider the case $\omega\equiv\dep{x,u}$ with $x\colon A$ and $u\colon P(x)$. The goal becomes
    \[
        \prod_{\omega'\colon E}\;
        \prod_{\varepsilon\colon\fun{Code}((\dep{x,u}),\omega')}
        Q(\dep{x,u},\omega',\varepsilon).
    \]
    Similarly, induction on $\omega'$ reduces the goal to the case $\omega'\equiv\dep{y,v}$ with $y\colon A$ and $v\colon P(y)$, which yields
    \[
        \prod_{\varepsilon\colon\fun{Code}(\dep{x,u},\dep{y,v})}
        Q(\dep{x,u},\dep{y,v},\varepsilon).
    \]
    Since
    \[
        \fun{Code}(\dep{x,u},\dep{y,v})
            \defeq\sum_{p\colon x\eq Ay}
        \fun{transport}^P(p,u) \eq{P(y)}v,
    \]
    we can replace $\varepsilon$ with $\dep{p,q}$, where $p\colon x\eq Ay$ and $q\colon\fun{transport}^P(p,u)\eq{P(y)}v$. The goal becomes
    \[
        Q(\dep{x,u},\dep{y,v},\dep{p,q}).
    \]
    Now, path induction on $p$ reduces this to $a'\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. Thus, the type of $q$ reduces to $u\eq{P(x)}v$. Finally, path induction on $q$ takes us to the conclusion.
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:pair-equivalence}
    Let\/ $A\colon\univ$ be a type and\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$ a type family. Denote the total space\/ $\sum_{x\colon A}P(x)$ by\/ $E$. Then, for any\/ $\omega,\omega'\colon E$, there is an equivalence
    \[
        (\omega\eq E\omega')\simeq\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega').
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    We have to verify two compositions:
    \begin{enumerate}
        \item $f\circ g\sim\id$.

        We have to show that, given $\omega,\omega'\colon E$
        \[
            \prod_{\varepsilon\colon\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')}
            f(g(\varepsilon))
            \eq{\fun{Code}
            (\omega,\omega')}\varepsilon.
        \]
        By Lemma~\ref{lem:Sigma-goal-reduction} it suffices to prove that in the case $\omega\equiv\omega'\equiv\dep{x,u}$ and $\varepsilon\equiv\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u}$, it is
        \[
            f(g(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u}))
            \equiv
            \dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u}.
        \]
        But
        \begin{align*}
            f(g(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u}))
                &\equiv f(\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}})
                    &&\text{; \eqref{eq:Sigma-trivial-decoding}}\\
                &\equiv\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u}
                    &&\text{; Def.~of }f.
        \end{align*}

        \needspace{2\baselineskip}
        \item $g\circ f\sim\id$.

        We have to prove that for $\rho\colon\omega,\omega'\colon E$, we have
        \[
            g(f(\rho))
            \eq{\omega\eq E\omega'}
            \rho.
        \]
        By based path induction on $\rho$ we can set $\omega'\equiv\omega$ and $\rho\equiv\fun{refl}_\omega$. Then
        \begin{align*}
            g(f(\fun{refl}_\omega))
                &\equiv g(
                    \dep{
                        \fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)},
                        \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}
                    }
                )
                    &&\text{; Def.~of }f\\
                &\equiv\fun{refl}_{
                        \dep{\pi_1(\omega),\pi_2(\omega)}
                    }
                    &&\text{;
                        \eqref{eq:Sigma-trivial-decoding}}\\
                &\eq{\omega\eq E\omega'}
                    \fun{refl}_\omega
                    &&\text{; }\fun{ap}_{\fun{refl}}.
        \end{align*}
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}\label{cor:Sigma-uniqueness}
    With the preceding notation, given\/ $\omega\colon E$, we have
    \[
        \omega\eq E\dep{\pi_1(\omega),\pi_2(\omega)}.
    \]
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
    Applying the theorem with $\omega\colon E$ and $\omega'\defeq\dep{\pi_1(\omega),\pi_2(\omega)}$, we obtain a map (the backward direction of the equivalence):
    \[
        \sum_{p\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega)}
        p_*(\pi_2(\omega))\eq{P(\pi_1(\omega))}\pi_2(\omega)
        \to
        (\omega\eq E\dep{\pi_1(\omega),\pi_2(\omega)}).
    \]
    We select the pair $\dep{\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}}$ in the domain. Note that the second component is well-typed because $(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)})_*$ is the identity function. Evaluating the map at this pair yields the desired witness in the codomain.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:lift-pair}
    Let\/ $A, B\colon\univ$.
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item If\/ $P\colon A\to\univ$ is the constant family\/ $P(x)\equiv B$, then for any\/ $b\colon B$ and\/ $p\colon a\eq A a'$, we have
        \[
            \fun{lift}(b,p) \eq{(a,b)\eq{A\times B}(a',b)} \fun{pair}^=(p,\fun{refl}_b).
        \]
        \item For any\/ $x\colon A$ and\/ $\gamma\colon u\eq B v$, the fiber inclusion\/ $\fun{in}_x\colon B\to A\times B$ satisfies
        \[
            \fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}(\gamma) \eq{(x,u)\eq{A\times B}(x,v)}\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x, \gamma).
        \]
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    We proceed by path induction in each case.
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item By induction on $p$ it suffices to assume $a'\equiv a$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_a$.
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item \lhs: $\fun{lift}(b,\fun{refl}_a)\equiv\fun{refl}_{(a,b)}$.
            \item \rhs: $\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_a, \fun{refl}_b)\equiv\fun{refl}_{(a,b)}$.
        \end{enumerate}
        Thus, the equality is witnessed by $\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_{(a,b)}}$.

        \item By induction on $\gamma$ it suffices to assume $v\equiv u$ and $\gamma\equiv\fun{refl}_u$.
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item \lhs: $\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}(\fun{refl}_u)\equiv\fun{refl}_{\fun{in}_x(u)} \equiv \fun{refl}_{(x,u)}$.
            \item \rhs: $\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x, \fun{refl}_u)\equiv\fun{refl}_{(x,u)}$.
        \end{enumerate}
        Thus, the equality is witnessed by $\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_{(x,u)}}$.\qedhere
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:total-space-of-constant}
    If the type family $P\colon A\to\univ$ is constant, say $P(x)\equiv B$ for all $x\colon A$, then the total space $E$ becomes $A\times B$ and, by Lemma~\ref{lem:constant-fibration}, we have $p_*(b)\eq Bb$ for $b\colon B$. Thus, the backward function of the equivalence reduces to
    \[
        g\colon\sum_{q\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega')}
            \pi_2(\omega)\eq B\pi_2(\omega')
            \to(\omega\eq{A\times B}\omega'),
    \]
    i.e.,
    \[
        g\colon\prod_{\omega,\omega'\colon A\times B}
        (\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega'))
            \times(\pi_2(\omega)\eq B\pi_2(\omega'))
            \to
            (\omega\eq{A\times B}\omega'),
    \]
    which has the same signature as $\fun{pair}^=$. In fact, given $\omega,\omega'\colon A\times B$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        g(q,\gamma)
            &\equiv \fun{lift}(\pi_2(\omega),q)
                \ct\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_{\pi_1(\omega')}}(\gamma)
                    &&\text{; Def.\ of }g \\
            &\eq{A\times B}\fun{pair}^=
                (q,\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)})
                \ct
                \fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega')},\gamma)
                    &&\text{; Prop.~\ref{prop:lift-pair}}\\
            &\eq{A\times B}\fun{pair}^=(q
                \ct \fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega')}, 
                \fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}\ct\gamma)
                    &&\text{; Prop.~\ref{prop:product-groupoid-functor} c)}\\
            &\eq{A\times B}\fun{pair}^=(q,\gamma)
                    &&\text{; Unit laws.}
    \end{align*}
    In consequence, for the general case, we introduce the following
\end{rem}

\begin{defn}\label{defn:Sigma-pair}
    The \textsl{dependent pair equality constructor}, denoted by\/ $\fun{pair}^=$, is the backward function of the equivalence established in Theorem~\ref{thm:pair-equivalence}. It constructs a path in the total space $E\defeq\sum_{x\colon A}P(x)$ from a path in the base $A$ and a path in the fiber. Its signature is:
    \[
        \fun{pair}^=\colon \prod_{\omega,\omega'\colon E}
        \Biggl(
            \sum_{p\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega')}
                p_*(\pi_2(\omega))\eq{P(\pi_1(\omega'))}\pi_2(\omega')
        \Biggr)
        \to(\omega\eq E\omega').
    \]
    Moreover,
    \[
        \fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\gamma})
            \equiv\fun{lift}(\pi_2(\omega),p)
            \ct\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_{\pi_1(\omega')}}(\gamma).
    \]
\end{defn}

\begin{rem}\label{rem:pair=-at-base-code}
    By definition, when $\omega'\equiv\omega\equiv\dep{x,u}$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{pair}^=(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\gamma})
            &\equiv\fun{lift}(u,\fun{refl}_x)
                \ct\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}(\gamma)\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}}
                \ct\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}(\gamma)\\
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_{\fun{in}_x}(\gamma).
        \intertext{In particular, for $\gamma\equiv\fun{refl}_u\colon u\eq{P(x)}u$,}
            \fun{pair}^=(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u})
                &\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}}.
    \end{align*}
\end{rem}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:ap_pi1-pair=}
  Let\/ $A$ be a type and\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ a type family. Suppose\/ $w_1,w_2\colon\sum_{x:A}B(x)$ with\/ $w_1\equiv\dep{x_1,y_1}$ and\/ $w_2\equiv\dep{x_2,y_2}$. Then, for any paths\/ $p\colon x_1\eq Ax_2$ and\/ $q\colon p_*(y_1)\eq{B(x_2)}y_2$, we have
  \[
    \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{pair}^=(p,q))\eq{x_1\eq Ax_2}p.
  \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
  By path induction on $p$ we may assume that $x_2\equiv x_1$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_{x_1}$. In this case, the transport $p_*(y_1)$ evaluates to $y_1$, and therefore $q$ is a path of type $y_1\eq{B(x_1)}y_2$. We can now proceed by path induction on $q$, which allows us to assume $y_2\equiv y_1$ and $q\equiv\fun{refl}_{y_1}$.

  Thus, the term $\fun{pair}^=(p,q)$ reduces definitionally to $\fun{refl}_{(x_1,y_1)}$. Applying the function $\pi_1$ to this path yields $\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(\fun{refl}_{\dep{x_1,y_1}})$, which is definitionally equal to $\fun{refl}_{x_1}$. Since $p\equiv\fun{refl}_{x_1}$, both sides of the equation are definitionally equal to $\fun{refl}_{x_1}$. Thus, the identity path $\fun{refl}_{\fun{refl}_{x_1}}$ witnesses the required propositional equality.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop} {\upshape[\textSigma-conmmutativity]} \label{prop:sigma-commutativity}
    Let $B,C\colon\univ$. Given a type family
    \[
        D\colon B\to C\to\univ,
    \]
    the map
    \begin{align*}
        \chi\colon\Bigl(
            \sum_{b\colon B}\;
            \sum_{c\colon C}D(b,c)
        \Bigr)
        &\to
        \Bigl(
            \sum_{c\colon C}\;\sum_{b\colon B}D(b,c)
        \Bigr)\\
        \dep{b,\dep{c,d}}&\mapsto\dep{c,\dep{b,d}}
    \end{align*}
    induces an equivalence.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    The map is well-defined because, in both expression the requirement is $d\colon D(b,c)$ for $b\colon B$ and $c\colon C$. The verification of the invertibility of this function is straightforward.

\end{proof}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:sigma-associativity} {\upshape[\textSigma-associativity]}
    Let\/ $X\colon\univ$ be a type, $A\colon X\to\univ$ a type family over\/ $X$, and\/ $B\colon\Sigma_XA\to\univ$ a type family over the total space. Then, the map
    \begin{align*}
        f\colon\sum_{x\colon X\vphantom(}\;
        \sum_{u\colon A(x)}B(\dep{x,u})
        &\to
        \sum_{\omega\colon\Sigma_XA}B(\omega)\\
        \dep{x,\dep{u,z}}&\mapsto\dep{\dep{x,u},z}
    \end{align*}
    induces an equivalence.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    Define the backward map
    \begin{align*}
        g\colon\Big(\sum_{\omega\colon\Sigma_XA}
            B(\omega)\Big)
        &\to
        \sum_{x\colon X\vphantom(};
        \sum_{u\colon A(x)}B(\dep{x,u})\\
        \dep{\dep{x,u},z}&\mapsto\dep{x,\dep{u,z}}.
    \end{align*}
    Verifying that $f$ and $g$ are quasi-inverses is straightforward.
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:composite-transport}
    Let\/ $A\colon X\to\univ$ be a type family with total space\/ $\Sigma_XA$. Let\/ $B\colon \Sigma_XA\to\univ$ be a second type family. Define the composite type family\/ $\Sigma_AB\colon X\to\univ$ as $x\mapsto\sum_{u\colon A(x)}B(\dep{x,u})$. If\/ $\Sigma_{\Sigma_XA\,}B$ is the total space of\/ $B$, then
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item By the associativity of\/ $\Sigma$-types, $\Sigma_{\Sigma_XA\,}B$ is equivalent to the total space of the composite family, forming a tower of fibrations:
        \[
            \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=large,font=\small]
                \Sigma_X(\Sigma_AB)
                        \arrow[rdd,"\pi_1^{\Sigma_AB}"']
                    &\Sigma_{\Sigma_XA}B
                        \arrow[d,"\pi_1^B"]
                        \arrow[l,"\simeq"']\\
                    &\Sigma_XA
                        \arrow[d,"\pi_1^A"]
                        \arrow[r,"B"]
                    &\univ\\
                \univ
                    &X
                        \arrow[l,"\Sigma_AB"]
                        \arrow[r,"A"']
                    &\univ
            \end{tikzcd}
        \]

        \item For any path\/ $p\colon x\eq Xy$ and any\/ $\dep{u,z}\colon \Sigma_AB(x)$, we have
        \[
            \fun{transport}^{\Sigma_AB}(p,\dep{u,z})
            \eq{\Sigma_AB(y)}
                \dep{
                    p_*(u),
                    \fun{transport}^B(\fun{pair}^=
                    (\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}},z))
                },
        \]
        where\/ $p_*(u)\equiv \fun{transport}^A(p)(u)$. Hence, if
        \[
            \sigma_p(\dep{u,z})\defeq
            \dep{
                p_*(u),
                \fun{transport}^B(\fun{pair}^=
                (\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}},z)),
            }
        \]
        the following diagram commutes propositionally:
        \[
            \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge, row sep=large]
                \Sigma_AB(x)
                        \arrow[r,"\fun{transport}^{\Sigma_AB}(p)"]
                        \arrow[d,equal,"\text{\upshape def\,}"']
                    &\Sigma_AB(y)
                        \arrow[d,equal,"\text{\upshape\,def}"]\\
                \displaystyle\sum_{u\colon A(x)}\!\!\!B(x,u)
                        \arrow[r,"\sigma_p"']
                    &\displaystyle\sum_{v\colon A(y)}
                        \!\!\!B(y,v)
            \end{tikzcd}
        \]
    \end{enumerate}
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    The commutativity of the triangle follows easily from Proposition~\ref{prop:sigma-associativity} and induction on the $\Sigma$-types:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}
            \dep{x,\dep{u,z}}
                    \arrow[rdd,mapsto]
                &\dep{\dep{x,u},z}
                    \arrow[l,mapsto]
                    \arrow[d,mapsto]\\
                &\dep{x,u}\arrow[d,mapsto]\\
                &x
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    since, by definition,
    \[
        \Sigma_X(\Sigma_AB)\equiv\sum_{x\colon X\vphantom(}\;
            \sum_{u\colon A(x)}B(\dep{x,u})
    \]
    The proof of b) has two parts:
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Type verification.]
        Let $\omega\defeq\dep{x,u}\colon\Sigma_XA$ and $\omega'\defeq\dep{y,p_*(u)}\colon\Sigma_XA$.
        Then, according to Definition~\ref{defn:Sigma-pair}, we have:
        \begin{itemize}
            \item $p\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq X\pi_1(\omega')$,
            \item $\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}\colon p_*(u) \eq{A(\pi_1(\omega'))}p_*(u)$,
            \item $\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}}\colon \dom(\fun{pair}^=)$,
            \item $\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}}) \colon\omega\eq{\Sigma_XA}\omega'$,
            \item $\fun{transport}^B(\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p, \fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}}))\colon B(\omega)\to B(\omega')$.
        \end{itemize}
        Thus, we obtain
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs&\defeq\explain[\Sigma_AB(y)]
                {\explain[\Sigma_AB(x)\to\Sigma_AB(y)]
                    {\fun{transport}^{\Sigma_AB}(p)}
                \explain[\Sigma_AB(x)]
                    {(\dep{u,z})}}\\[3mm]
            \rhs&\defeq\bigdep{
                \explain[A(y)]{p_*(u)},\,
                \explain[B(\dep{y,p_*(u)})]{
                    \fun{transport}^B\!
                    \bigl(
                    \explain[\text{path in }\Sigma_XA]
                    {\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}})}
                    \bigr)
                    (\explain[B(\dep{x,u})]{z})
                }
            },
        \end{align*}
        which shows that both sides are elements of $\Sigma_AB(y)$. In the case of the \rhs, this is because the first component lies in $A(y)$ and the second in $B(\dep{y,v})$ with $v \defeq p_*(u)\colon A(y)$, as required.

        \item[Inhabitation.] Since the statement holds for every path $p\colon x\eq Xy$, by path induction, to prove that there is a witness of
        \[
            \lhs\eq{\Sigma_AB(y)}\rhs
        \]
        it suffices to consider the case where $y \equiv x$ and $p \equiv \fun{refl}_x$. The goal reduces as follows:
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs
                &\equiv\fun{transport}^{\Sigma_AB}(\fun{refl}_x)(\dep{u,z})\\
                &\equiv\dep{u,z}.\\[1ex]
            \rhs
                &\equiv\bigdep{
                (\fun{refl}_x)_*(u),\fun{transport}^B
                (
                \fun{pair}^=
                (\dep{
                \fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_{(\fun{refl}_x)_*(u)}
                })
                )
                (z)
                }\\
            &\equiv\bigdep{u,\fun{transport}^B
            (
                \fun{pair}^=(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u})
            )(z)}\\
            &\equiv     
            \bigl(
                u,\fun{transport}^B(\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}})(z)
            \bigr)\\
            &\equiv\dep{u,z}.
        \end{align*}
        Thus, $\lhs\equiv\rhs$ definitionally.\qedhere
    \end{description}
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}\label{cor:transport-in-dependent-second-component}
    Let\/ $W$ and\/ $X$ be types, and let\/ $A\colon W\to\univ$ be the constant type family defined by\/ $A(w)\defeq X$. Let\/ $B\colon\Sigma_W A\to\univ$ be a second type family. Define the composite type family\/ $\Sigma_A B\colon W\to\univ$ by\/ $w\mapsto\sum_{x\colon X}B(\dep{w,x})$.
    
    For any path\/ $p\colon w_1\eq Ww_2$ and any element\/ $\dep{x,z}\colon\Sigma_AB(w_1)$, we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{\Sigma_A B}(p)(\dep{x,z})
        \eq{}
        \bigdep{x,\fun{transport}^{w\mapsto B(\dep{w,x})}(p)(z)}.
    \]
    The following diagram commutes propositionally:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge, row sep=large]
            \Sigma_AB(w_1)
                    \arrow[r,"\fun{transport}^{\Sigma_A B}(p)"] 
                    \arrow[d,"\text{\upshape def }"',equal,no head]
                &\Sigma_AB(w_2)
                    \arrow[d,"\text{\,\upshape def}",equal,no head]\\
            \sum_{x\colon X}B(\dep{w_1,x})
                    \arrow[r,"\sigma_p"']
                &\sum_{x\colon X}B(\dep{w_2,x})
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    where the bottom map is defined component-wise as
    \[
        \sigma_p(\dep{x,z})
            \defeq
            \bigdep{
                x,
                \fun{transport}^{w\mapsto B(\dep{w,x})}(p)(z)
            }.
    \]
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
    We apply part b) of the theorem. Since $A$ is the constant family, by Exercise~\ref{exr:constant-fibration}, $p_*(x)\equiv\fun{transport}^A(p)(x)\eq Xx$. Substituting this into the \rhs of the theorem's formula, we obtain
    \[
        \bigdep{
            x,
            \fun{transport}^B\bigl(
                \fun{pair}^=(
                    \dep{p,\fun{refl}_x}
                )
            \bigr)(z)
        }.
    \]
    The term $\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\fun{refl}_x})$ represents a path in the total space $\Sigma_WA$ from $\dep{w_1,x}$ to $\dep{w_2,x}$. Transporting $z$ along this path in the family $B$ is definitionally equivalent to transporting $z$ along $p$ in the partially applied family $w\mapsto B(\dep{w,x})$. This yields the desired equality. 
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}
    For $\omega,\omega'\colon E$, a canonical pair $\dep{p,u}\colon\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')$ is given by
    \begin{alignat*}2
        p&\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega'),
        &\quad u&\colon p_*(\pi_2(\omega))
            \eq{P(\pi_1(\omega'))}\pi_2(\omega')
    \end{alignat*}
\end{rem}

\textbf{Extended framework.} To apply the extended framework~\ref{extended-framework} to the $\Sigma$-type, we define
\begin{align}
    \fun{inv}
        &\colon\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')
            \to\fun{Code}(\omega',\omega)\nonumber\\
    \fun{inv}(\dep{p,\gamma})
        &\defeq\bigdep{p^{-1},(p^{-1})_*(\gamma^{-1})
        \ct
        \fun{transportinv}_l^P(p,\pi_2(\omega))}.
        \label{eq:Sigma-inv}\\[1mm]
    \ect
        &\colon\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega')
            \to\fun{Code}(\omega',\omega'')
            \to\fun{Code}(\omega,\omega'')\nonumber\\
    \dep{p,\gamma}\ect\dep{p',\gamma'}
        &\defeq\dep{p\ct p',p'_*(\gamma)\ct\gamma'}.\nonumber
\end{align}
To verify the unit laws, observe that
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}(c)
        &\equiv\fun{inv}(\dep{\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)}
            ,\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}})\\
        &\equiv\dep{\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)}^{-1}
            ,\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}}
            &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:transportinv}}\\
        &\equiv c,\\
    c\ect\dep{p,\gamma}
        &\equiv\dep{\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)}
            ,\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}}\ect\dep{p,\gamma}\\
        &\equiv\dep{\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)}\ct p
            ,\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}\ct\gamma}\\
        &\equiv\dep{p,\gamma}.
\end{align*}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:Sigma-pair=-properties}
    Given elements\/ $\omega,\omega',\omega''\colon E$ and paths
    \begin{alignat*}{4}
    p\phantom{'}
        &\colon\pi_1(\omega)
        &&\eq A\pi_1(\omega'),
        &\quad \gamma\phantom{'}
        &\colon p_*(\pi_2(\omega))
        &&\eq{P(\pi_1(\omega'))} \pi_2(\omega'),\\
    p'
        &\colon\pi_1(\omega')
        &&\eq A\pi_2(\omega''),
        &\quad\gamma'
        &\colon p'_*(\pi_2(\omega'))
        &&\eq{P(\pi_1(\omega''))}\pi_2(\omega''),
    \end{alignat*}
    we have
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\fun{pair}^=(\dep{\fun{refl}_{\pi_1(\omega)},\fun{refl}_{\pi_2(\omega)}})\equiv\fun{refl}_\omega$

        \item $\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p^{-1},(p^{-1})_*(\gamma^{-1})
            \ct \fun{transportinv}_l^P(p, \pi_2(\omega))})
            \eq E\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\gamma})^{-1}$
            
        \item $\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p\ct p',\gamma\ct\gamma'})\eq E\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\gamma})\ct\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p',\gamma'})$
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    This is a direct consequence of Theorem~\ref{thm:extended-framework}.\footnote{Note also that parts b) and c) are easily derived from Lemma~\ref{lem:Sigma-goal-reduction}.}
    \[
    \begin{tikzpicture}[
        >=stealth, 
        scale=1.0,
        font=\small,
        every node/.style={scale=0.9},
        dot/.style={circle, fill, inner sep=1.5pt}
        ]
    
        % Coordinates
        \coordinate (A) at (0,0.3);
        \coordinate (B) at (4,0.3);
        \coordinate (C) at (8,0.3);
    
        % Base Line
        \draw[thick, -latex] (A) -- node[below] {$p$} (B);
        \draw[thick, -latex] (B) -- node[below] {$p'$} (C);
        \node[dot, label=below:$x$] at (A) {};
        \node[dot, label=below:$x'$] at (B) {};
        \node[dot, label=below:$x''$] at (C) {};
    
        % Fibers (visualized as vertical dashed lines)
        \draw[gray] (0,0.5) -- (0,5)
            node[above,black] {$P(x)$};
        \draw[gray] (4,0.5) -- (4,5)
            node[above,black] {$P(x')$};
        \draw[gray] (8,0.5) -- (8,5)
            node[above,black] {$P(x'')$};
    
        % Fiber over x
        \node[dot, label=left:{$\omega\equiv\dep{x,u}$}] (u) at (0,1.5) {};
    
        % Fiber over x'
        \node[dot, label=below right:{$p_*(u)$}] (pu) at (4,1.5) {};
        \node[dot, label=above right:{$v$}] (v) at (4,3.0) {};
        
        % Path \gamma in fiber x'
        \draw[thick,-latex] (pu) -- node[right] {$\gamma$} (v);
    
        % Fiber over x''
        \node[dot, label=right:{$(p\ct p')_*(u)$}] (ppu) at (8,1.3) {};
        \node[circle,
            fill,
            inner sep=1.5pt,
            label={[yshift=4pt]right:{$p'_*(p_*(u))$}}] 
                (pprimeu) at (8,1.6) {};
        \draw[-latex] (ppu) to[out=200,in=200] node[midway, left] {$\omega$} (8,1.6);
        % Note: visually separating p'*(p*(u)) might be too cluttered, so we treat the coherence \omega as the bottom anchor point or a tiny loop, but conceptually it starts here.
        
        \node[dot, label=right:{$p'_*(v)$}] (pv) at (8,3.0) {};
        \node[dot, label=right:{$\omega''\equiv\dep{x'',w}$}] (w) at (8,4.5) {};
    
        % Transport arrows (Horizontal)
        \draw[-latex, dashed] (u) to[bend left=10] (pu);
        \draw[-latex, dashed] (pu) to[out=20,in=135] node[above, pos=0.5] {$\fun{lift}(p_*(u),p')$} (8,1.6); % Slight offset to show distinct endpoints
        \draw[-latex, dashed] (v) to[bend left=10] node[above,pos=0.5] {$\fun{lift}(v,p')$} (pv);
    
        % The paths in the third fiber (The Sum)
        
        % 1. The Coherence (approximated as the gap/start)
        % 2. The transported \gamma
        \draw[thick, -latex] (8,1.6) -- node[right] {$\fun{ap}_{p'_*}(\gamma)$} (pv);
        
        % 3. The path \gamma'
        \draw[thick, -latex] (pv) -- node[right] {$\gamma'$} (w);
    
        % Labels for the total paths
        \draw[teal,-latex](u) to[out=45,in=135]
            node[
                pos=0.4,
                below right,
                black] {$\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\gamma})$} (v);
        \draw[teal,-latex] (v) to[out=70,in=155]
            node[
                midway,
                below right,
                black] {$\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p',\gamma'})$} (w);
    \end{tikzpicture}
    \]
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}
    Let\/ $A\colon\univ$ be a type and\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ a type family. Given an element\/ $\dep{x,u}\colon\Sigma_AB$ and a path\/ $p\colon x\eq{A}y$, we have
    \[
        \fun{pair}^=(\dep{p^{-1},\gamma})^{-1}
        \eq{\Sigma_AB}
        \fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}}),
    \]
    where\/ $\gamma\colon(p^{-1})_*(p_*(u))\eq{B(x)}u$ is the canonical path that cancels the transport along inverse paths.
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
    The equation is well-typed because
    \begin{align*}
        p^{-1}
            &\colon y\eq Ax,\\
        \fun{pair}^=(\dep{p^{-1},\gamma})
            &\colon\dep{y,p_*(u)}\eq{\Sigma_AB}\dep{x,u},\\[1mm]
        \lhs
            &\colon\dep{x,u}\eq{\Sigma_AB}\dep{y,p_*(u)},\\[1mm]
        \rhs
            &\colon\dep{x,u}\eq{\Sigma_AB}\dep{y,p_*(u)}.
    \end{align*}
    To verify the equality, we proceed by path induction on $p$. Thus, we can assume that $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case, $\gamma$ becomes $\fun{refl}_u$, and both sides compute definitionally to $\fun{refl}_{(x,u)}$.

    %
    
\end{proof}

\textbf{Note.} What follows is a generalization of Theorem~\ref{thm:pair-fxg} to\/ $\Sigma$-types. For simplicity, the statement is formulated for canonical dependent pairs; its extension to arbitrary terms is straightforward.

\begin{thm}\label{thm:pair-dependent-gxh}
    Let\/ $A,A'\colon\univ$ be types, and let\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ and\/ $B'\colon A'\to\univ$ be type families. Given\/ $g\colon A\to A'$ and\/ $h\colon\prod_{a\colon A}B(a)\to B'(g(a))$, define
    \begin{align*}
        f\colon
            \Bigl(
                \sum_{x\colon A}B(x)
            \Bigr)
            &\to
            \Bigl(
                \sum_{x'\colon A'}B'(x')
            \Bigr)
            \\
        \dep{a,b}&\mapsto\dep{g(a),h(a,b)}.
    \end{align*}
    Then, for\/ $\dep{x,u},\dep{y,v}\colon\Sigma_AB$, $p\colon x\eq{A}y$, and\/ $\gamma\colon p_*(u)\eq{B(y)}v$, we have
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f(\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\gamma}))
        \eq{f(x,u)\eq{\Sigma_{A'}B'}f(y,v)}
        \fun{pair}^=
            (\dep{\fun{ap}_g(p),\alpha\ct\fun{ap}_{h(y,\dummy)}(\gamma)}),
    \]
    where
    \[
        \alpha\colon\fun{ap}_g(p)_*
            (h(\dep{x,u}))
            \eq{B'(g(y))}
            h(\dep{y,p_*(u)})
    \]
    is the path given by\/ {\upshape Theorem~\ref{thm:general-post-composition-transport}}.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    Let us first verify that the equality is well-typed:
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\gamma})
            &\colon\dep{x,u}\eq{\Sigma_AB}\dep{y,v}.\\
        \lhs
            &\colon\dep{g(x),h(\dep{x,u})}
                \eq{\Sigma_{A'}B'}
                \dep{g(y),h(\dep{y,v})}.\\
            &\equiv f(\dep{x,u})\eq{\Sigma_{A'}B'}f(\dep{y,v}).\\[1mm]
        \fun{ap}_g(p)
            &\colon g(x)\eq{A'}g(y).\\
        \fun{ap}_{h(\dep{y,\dummy})}(\gamma)
            &\colon h(\dep{y,p_*(u)})\eq{B'(g(y))}h(\dep{y,v}).\\
        \alpha\ct\fun{ap}_{h(\dep{y,\dummy})}(\gamma)
            &\colon\fun{ap}_g(p)_*(h(\dep{x,u}))
                \eq{B'(g(y))}
                h(\dep{y,v}).\\
        \rhs
            &\colon\dep{g(x),h(\dep{x,u})}
                \eq{\Sigma_{A'}B'}
                \dep{g(y),h(\dep{y,v})}\\
            &\equiv f(\dep{x,u})\eq{\Sigma_{A'}B'}f(\dep{y,v}).
    \end{align*}
    Consider the path in $f(\dep{x,u})\eq{\Sigma_{A'}B'}f(\dep{y,v})$
    \begin{align*}
        Q(\dep{x,u},\dep{y,v},\dep{p,\gamma})
        \defeq
        \fun{ap}_f(\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\gamma}))
        \eq{}
        \fun{pair}^=
            (
            \dep{\fun{ap}_g(p),
            \alpha\ct\fun{ap}_{h(\dep{y,\dummy})}(\gamma)}
            ).
    \end{align*}
    By Lemma~\ref{lem:Sigma-goal-reduction} applied to $Q$,
    it suffices to exhibit an inhabitant of
    \[
        Q(
            \dep{x,u},
            \dep{x,u},
            \dep{\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u)}
        ).
    \]
    But this is trivial because both sides of the equation reduce to
    \begin{align*}
        \lhs&\equiv f(\dep{x,u}).\\[1mm]
        \alpha&\equiv\fun{refl}_{h(\dep{x,u})}.\\
        \fun{ap}_{h(\dep{x,\dummy})}(\fun{refl}_u)
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{h(\dep{x,u})}.\\
        \rhs&\equiv\fun{pair}^=
                (\dep{
                    \fun{refl}_{g(x)},
                    \fun{refl}_{h(x,u)}
                })\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{g(x),h(\dep{x,u})}}\\
            &\equiv f(\dep{x,u}),
    \end{align*}
    which is witnessed by $\fun{refl}_{f(\dep{x,u})}$.
\end{proof}

\section{Equality in the Unit Type}

To apply the framework~\ref{observational-framework} to the unit type $\fun1$, we proceed as in the previous cases.

\textsc{Code family:}
\begin{align*}
    \fun{Code}&\colon\fun1\to\fun1\to\univ\\
    \fun{Code}(x,y)&\defeq\fun1.
\end{align*}

\textsc{Base code:}
For $c\colon\fun{Code}(x,x)$ we specify $c\defeq\fstar$.

\needspace{2\baselineskip}
\textsc{Encode function:}
\begin{align*}
    \fun{encode}&\colon(x\eq{\fun1}y)\to\fun{Code}(x,y)\\
    \fun{encode}(p)&\defeq\fun{transport}^{C_x}(p,c)
\end{align*}
In particular, for $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$, we have
\[
    \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_x)\equiv c\equiv\fstar.
\]
Therefore, by induction on $p$, we deduce that
\[
    \fun{encode}(p)\eq{\fun1}\fstar
\]
and we take the \rhs to define the constant encode function $f\defeq\lambda x,y.\,\lambda p.\,\fstar$.

\textsc{Decode function:}
Let $g$ denote the backward $\fun{decode}$ map. Then
\[
    g\colon\prod_{x,y\colon\fun1}\fun{Code}(x,y)\to(x\eq{\fun1}y).
\]
To define it we proceed by induction on $x$. It suffices to construct $g(\fstar)$. The goal becomes a term of type
\[
    \prod_{y\colon\fun1}\fun1\to(\fstar\eq{\fun1}y).
\]
Induction on $y$ further reduces the goal to $\fun1\to(\fstar\eq{\fun1}\fstar)$, which is inhabited by the constant function $z\mapsto\fun{refl}_\fstar$. In particular,
\begin{equation}\label{eq:decode(star)}
    \fun{decode}(\fstar)\equiv\fun{refl}_\fstar.
\end{equation}

Thus, we have defined $g\colon\prod_{x,y\colon\fun1}\fun1\to(x\eq{\fun1}y)$ as the unique function that satisfies $g(\fstar,\fstar,\fstar) \equiv \fun{refl}_\fstar$.


\begin{thm}\label{thm:1-equivalence}
    For any\/ $x,y\colon\fun1$, we have\/ $(x\eq{\fun1}y)\simeq\fun1$.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    To verify the homotopies, we need to prove
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $f\circ g \sim \id_{\fun1}$.

        This translates into $f(g(x,y,u)) \eq{\fun1} u$ for all $x,y,u\colon\fun1$.
        By the induction principle of $\fun1$, we may set $x,y,u\equiv\fstar$, which satisfies the goal because $f$ maps every element to $\fstar$.

        \item $g\circ f \sim \id_{\prod_{x,y\colon\fun1}(x\eq{\fun1}y)}$.

        We must show $g(x,y,f(x,y,p))\eq{x\eq{\fun1}y}p$.
        By path induction, it suffices to check the case $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. The goal becomes
        \[
            g(x,x,f(x,x,\fun{refl}_x))\eq{x\eq{\fun1}x}\fun{refl}_x.
        \]
        By induction on $x$, it is enough to prove $g(\fstar,\fstar,f(\fstar,\fstar,\fun{refl}_\fstar))\eq{\fstar\eq{\fun1}\fstar}\fun{refl}_\fstar$. Since $f(\fstar,\fstar,\fun{refl}_\fstar)\equiv\fstar$, the goal reduces to $g(\fstar,\fstar,\fstar)\eq{\fstar\eq{\fun1}\fstar}\fun{refl}_\fstar$, which holds by the definition of $g$.\qedhere
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

The theorem has the following consequences:

\begin{description}[font=\normalfont\itshape]
    \item[Introduction rule.]
    We define the canonical element inhabiting the identity type of the unit for any two points
    \[
        \fun{triv} \colon x \eq{\fun1} y
    \]
    as\/ $\fun{triv}\defeq\fun{decode}(x,y,\fstar)$.

    \item[Elimination rule.]
    The dependent eliminator asserts that to define a function out of the identity type, we only need to specify its value on the canonical element.
    \[
        \fun{ind}_{=_{\fun1}}\colon
        \prod_{C\colon(x\eq{\fun1}y)\to\univ}
        C(\fun{triv})\to\prod_{p\colon x\eq{\fun1}y} C(p)
    \]

    \item[Computation rule.]
    When the eliminator is applied to the canonical element\/ $\fun{triv}$, it reduces propositionally\footnote{This is weaker than usual. The equality at the base case is definitional if we accept the\/ $\eta$-rule for the identity type [cf.~\nameref{subsection:eta-rule}].} to the base case\/ $c\colon C(\fun{triv})$.
    \[
        \fun{ind}_{=_{\fun1}}(C,c,\fun{triv})\eq{C(\fun{triv})}c.
    \]

    \item[Uniqueness rule.]
    This rule asserts that the type is contractible (a singleton); any inhabitant\/ $p$ is path-equal to the canonical element.
    \[
        \fun{uniq}_{=_{\fun1}}\colon
        \prod_{p\colon x\eq{\fun1}y}p
            \eq{x\eq{\fun1}y}\fun{triv}.
    \]
\end{description}

To derive the elimination rule, we use Theorem~\ref{thm:1-equivalence}, which gives us a homotopy:
\[
    \varepsilon_p\colon
        \fun{decode}(x,y,\fun{encode}(x,y,p))\eq{\fun1}p
\]
for every path\/ $p\colon x\eq{\fun1}y$. Since, by definition, $\fun{encode}(x,y,p)\equiv\fstar$, the homotopy simplifies:
\[
    \fun{decode}(x,y,\fun{encode}(x,y,p))
        \equiv\fun{decode}(x,y,\fstar)\equiv\fun{triv},
\]
and so
\[
    \varepsilon_p \colon \fun{triv}\eq{x\eq{\fun1}y}p.
\]
Now, given\/ $C\colon(x\eq{\fun1}y)\to\univ$ and\/ $c\colon C(\fun{triv})$, we want to construct\/ $f(p)\colon C(p)$.

We define
\[
    \fun{ind}_{=_{\fun1}}(C,c,p)
        \defeq\fun{transport}^C(\varepsilon_p,c).
\]
In the case\/ $p\equiv\fun{triv}$, we have:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:eta-rule-dependent}
    \varepsilon_{\fun{triv}}
        \eq{x\eq{\fun1}y}\fun{refl}_{\fun{triv}}.
\end{equation}
Therefore:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:definitional-base-case}
    \fun{ind}_{=_{\fun1}}(C,c,\fun{triv})
        \eq{C(\fun{triv})}
        \fun{transport}^C(\fun{refl}_{\fun{triv}},c)
        \equiv c.
\end{equation}

The Uniqueness rule is derived by taking the symmetry (inverse) of $\varepsilon_p$:
    \[
        \fun{uniq}_{=_{\fun1}}(p) \defeq \varepsilon_p^{-1}.
    \]

\subsection*{The $\eta$-rule for the Identity of\/ $\fun1$}
\label{subsection:eta-rule}

The\/ $\eta$-rule asserts that every inhabitant of the identity type of the unit is definitionally equal to reflexivity, namely
\begin{equation*}
    p\equiv\fun{refl}_\fstar
    \qquad(\text{for every } p\colon x\eq{\fun1}y).
\end{equation*}
Since the\/ $\eta$-rule for the Identity of\/ $\fun1$ is structurally impossible to state (as a general rule for arbitrary\/ $x,y$) without first assuming the\/ $\eta$-rule for\/ $\fun1$, this requires the\/ $\eta$-rule for the unit type.

\textbf{Extended framework.} For the unit type identity, we have
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}&\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to\fun{Code}(y,x)\\
    \fun{inv}(u)&\defeq u
\intertext{and}
    \ect&\colon\fun{Code}(x,y)\to\fun{Code}(y,z)
        \to\fun{Code}(x,z)\\
    u\ect v&\defeq v.
\end{align*}
The unit laws follow directly from the definitions above, namely
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}(c)&\equiv c\\
    c\ect u&\equiv u.
\end{align*}

\begin{prop}
    Given $x,y,z\colon\fun1$, and $p\colon x\eq{\fun1}y$ and $q\colon y\eq{\fun1}z$, we have
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\fun{decode}(x,x,\fstar)\eq{x\eq{\fun1}x}\fun{refl}_x$
        
        \item $\fun{decode}(y,x,u)\eq{y\eq{\fun1}x}\fun{decode}(x,y,u)^{-1}$
        
        \item $\fun{decode}(x,z,u\ect v)\eq{x\eq{\fun1}z}\fun{decode}(x,y,u)\ct\fun{decode}(y,z,v)$
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    This is a direct consequence of Theorem~\ref{thm:extended-framework}.
    %
    
\end{proof}

\section{Function Extensionality Axiom}\label{function-extensionality-axiom}

In this section we address the question of the identity type for dependent (and non-dependent) functions. To establish the context, let\/ $A\colon\univ$ be a type and\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ a type family. To analyze the identity in the section space\footnote{Consisting of all dependent functions\/ $s\colon A\to E$, where\/ $E$ is the total space\/ $\sum_{x\colon A}B(x)$, such that\/ $\pi_1(s(x))\eq A x$ for all\/ $x\colon A$.}
\[
    \Gamma\defeq\prod_{x\colon A}B(x)
\]
we apply the framework~\ref{observational-framework}.

\textsc{Code family:}
\begin{align*}
    \fun{Code}&\colon\Gamma\to\Gamma\to\univ\\
    \fun{Code}(f,g)&\defeq f\sim g
\intertext{i.e.,}
    \fun{Code}(f,g)&\defeq\prod_{x\colon A} f(x)\eq{B(x)}g(x).
\end{align*}


\textsc{Base code:} For the reflexive case, we define the term\/ $c\colon\fun{Code}(f,f)$ pointwise by reflexivity:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:happly-basecode}
    c \defeq \lambda x\colon A.\, \fun{refl}_{f(x)}.
\end{equation}

\textsc{Encode function:}
\begin{align*}
    \fun{encode}&\colon(f\eq\Gamma g)\to\fun{Code}(f,g)\\
    \fun{encode}(p)&\defeq\fun{transport}^{C_f}(p,c).
\end{align*}
Since\/ $C_f\defeq\fun{Code}(f,\dummy)$, we introduce the local family at a point\/ $x\colon A$
\[
    C_{f,x}\defeq\lambda h\colon\Gamma.\, f(x)\eq{B(x)}h(x).
\]
In particular, in the case where\/ $g\equiv f$ and\/ $p\equiv\fun{refl}_f$, we have
\begin{align*}
    \fun{encode}(\fun{refl}_f)(x)
        &\equiv\fun{transport}^{C_f}(\fun{refl}_f,c)(x)\\
        &\equiv c(x)\\
        &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x)}\\
        &\equiv\fun{transport}^{C_{f,x}}
            (\fun{refl}_f,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}).
\end{align*}
Hence, path induction implies
\[
    \fun{encode}(p)(x)\eq{C_{f,x}(g)}
        \fun{transport}^{C_{f,x}}(p,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}),
\]
for $p\colon f\eq\Gamma g$ and $x\colon A$.
We take the \rhs to define the standard name for the encode function \textsl{homotopy application\/}:
\begin{equation}\label{eq:homotopy-application}
    \begin{aligned}
        \fun{happly}&\colon(f\eq\Gamma g)\to\fun{Code}(f,g)\\
        \fun{happly}(p)&\defeq \lambda x\colon A.\,
                \fun{transport}^{C_{f,x}}(p,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}),
    \end{aligned}
\end{equation}
which can be illustrated by
\[
\begin{tikzcd}[row sep=0.2cm,column sep=-0.3cm]
        &\displaystyle\Gamma\equiv\prod_{x\colon A}B(x)
