        &&\qquad A
        &&B(x)\\
        &&&&&f(x)
            \arrow[dd,"\fun{happly}(p)(x)"',equal]\\
    f
            \arrow[rr,"p",bend left]
        &&g
        &\qquad x
            \arrow[rru,mapsto]
            \arrow[rrd,mapsto]&&\\
        &&&&&g(x)\\
        &\text{\small Path in function space}
        &&&\qquad\text{\small Function homotopy}
\end{tikzcd}
\]
Because of the base code we defined in \eqref{eq:happly-basecode}, we have
\begin{equation}\label{eq:happly-refl}
    \fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_f)\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}.
\end{equation}

Since the basic rules of type theory do not provide a way to construct a quasi-inverse for\/ $\fun{happly}$, we introduce the Function Extensionality axiom to formally establish the equivalence between function equality and pointwise homotopy.

\textbf{Axiom.} [Function Extensionality]. The homotopy application function \eqref{eq:homotopy-application} is an equivalence.\footnote{We will see in later chapters that this axiom follows both from univalence and from the interval type.}

The axiom asserts that\/ $\fun{happly}$ has a quasi-inverse
\begin{align}\label{axiom:FE}
    \fun{funext}&\colon\fun{Code}(f,g)\to(f\eq\Gamma g),
\end{align}
which, by definition, satisfies the following homotopies for any path\/ $p\colon f\eq\Gamma g$ and any pointwise homotopy\/ $\eta\colon\fun{Code}(f,g)$:
\begin{align*}
    \fun{funext}(\fun{happly}(p))
        &\eq{f\eq\Gamma g} p\\
    \fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(\eta))
        &\eq{\fun{Code}(f,g)}\eta.
\end{align*}

\textbf{Extended framework.} To apply the framework~\ref{extended-framework}, we define\footnote{See Definitions~\ref{defn:homotopy-inverse-and-ct}.}
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}&\colon\fun{Code}(f,g)\to\fun{Code}(g,f)\\
    \fun{inv}(\eta)&\defeq\eta^{-1}
\intertext{and}
    \ect&\colon\fun{Code}(f,g)\to\fun{Code}(g,h)
        \to\fun{Code}(f,h)\\
   \eta\ect\vartheta&\defeq\eta\ct\vartheta.
\end{align*}
The unit laws follow immediately from the definitional properties of path inversion and concatenation applied pointwise:
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}(c)&\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}^{-1}\\
        &\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}\\
        &\equiv c,
\intertext{and}
    c\ect\eta&\equiv(\lambda x.\,c(x))\ct\eta(x)\\
        &\equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}\ct\eta(x)\\
        &\equiv\lambda x.\,\eta(x)\\
        &\equiv\eta.
\end{align*}

\begin{ntn}
    From now on, we will use the superscript {\upshape\textsc{fe}} to indicate that a result depends on the function extensionality axiom.
\end{ntn}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:funext-functoriality}\fe
    Let\/ $A$,\/ $B$, and\/ $\Gamma$ be as above. If\/ $f, g\colon\Gamma$, then
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\fun{funext}(f,f,\lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{f(x)})\eq{f\eq\Gamma f}\fun{refl}_f$

        \item For\/ $\eta\colon f\sim g$, we have
        \[
            \fun{funext}(g,f,\eta^{-1})\eq{g\eq\Gamma f}
            \fun{funext}(f,g,\eta)^{-1}
        \]

        \item Given\/ $h\colon\Gamma$ and\/ $\vartheta\colon g\sim h$, we have
        \[
            \fun{funext}(f,h,\eta\ct\vartheta)\eq{f\eq\Gamma h}\fun{funext}(f,g,\eta)\ct\fun{funext}(g,h,\vartheta)
        \]
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    This is an immediate consequence of Theorem~\ref{thm:extended-framework}.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{Composition of Quasi-inverses}

Recall from Definition~\ref{defn:qinv-composition} that quasi-inverses can be composed.

\begin{prop}\fe
    Let\/ $f\colon A\to B$. Suppose that\/ $\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}\colon\fun{qinv}(f)$. Then\/ $\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta\ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}\colon\fun{qinv}(f)$ and both quasi-inverses are (propositionally) equal.
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    We construct the path in $\fun{qinv}(f)$ by pairs.
    \begin{enumerate}[1.]
        \item The path between the functions is $\fun{refl}_{f^{-1}}$.
        \item The path between the homotopy pairs is given component-wise:
        \begin{itemize}
            \item For the right homotopies: $\eta \equiv \eta$, so we use $\fun{refl}_\eta$.
            \item For the left homotopies: we need to show that 
            \[
                \vartheta\ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A}\eq{f^{-1}\circ f\sim\id_A}\vartheta.
            \]
            By function extensionality, this follows from the right unit law for paths.\footnote{Lemma \ref{lem:right-unit-law}.} Therefore,
            \[
                \fun{ru}_{\vartheta}\defeq
                    \fun{funext}(\lambda x.\,
                        \fun{ru}(\vartheta(x))).
            \]
        \end{itemize}
    \end{enumerate}
    Thus, the total identity path is
    \[
        \fun{pair}^=(\dep{\fun{refl}_{f^{-1}}
            ,\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_\eta,\fun{ru}_{\vartheta})})
            \colon\dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta\ct\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}
            \eq{\fun{qinv}(f)}
            \dep{f^{-1},(\eta,\vartheta)}.
    \]
\end{proof}

\begin{cor}\fe\label{cor:propositional-qinv-composition-with-id}
    In the particular case where one of the functions is the identity, we have
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\dep{\id_A,(\fun{refl}_{\id_A},\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}\circ\dep{f^{-1},(\eta_f,\vartheta_f)}\eq{\fun{qinv}(f)}(f^{-1}
            ,(\eta_f,\vartheta_f))$

        \item $\dep{f^{-1},(\eta_f,\vartheta_f)}\circ\dep{\id_A,(\fun{refl}_{\id_A},\fun{refl}_{\id_A})}\eq{\fun{qinv}(f)}\dep{f^{-1},(\eta_f,\vartheta_f)}$
    \end{enumerate}
\end{cor}



\subsection*{Non-dependent Functions}

The special case where\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ is constant refers to the non-dependent function type: $\Gamma\equiv A\to B$. Here the general case computes as follows. For\/ $f,g\colon A\to B$ and\/ $p\colon f\eq{A\to B}g$, we have
\begin{align*}
    C_{f,x}&\defeq\lambda g.\,f(x)\eq Bg(x)\\
    \fun{happly}(p)&\defeq\lambda x.\,
                \fun{transport}^{C_{f,x}}(p,\fun{refl}_{f(x)}).
\end{align*}
Furthermore, evaluating\/ $\fun{happly}(p)$ at a specific point\/ $x\colon A$ is propositionally equal to the action on paths of the evaluation functional\/ $\fun{ev}_x\colon (A\to B)\to B$, where\/ $\fun{ev}_x(h)\defeq h(x)$. That is, we have a path
\begin{equation}\label{eq:happly-is-ap-ev}
    \fun{happly}(p)(x) \eq{B} \fun{ap}_{\fun{ev}_x}(p),
\end{equation}
as it can be easily verified by path induction on $p$.

Function extensionality provides the quasi-inverse to\/ $\fun{happly}$, mapping pointwise homotopies back to paths between functions:
\[
    \fun{funext}\colon (f\sim g) \to (f\eq{A\to B}g).
\]

\subsection*{Transport Decomposition}\label{subs:transport-decomposition}

\paragraph{Non-dependent case.} Let\/ $X\colon\univ$ be a type and\/ $A,B\colon X\to\univ$ be type families. Let\/ $A\to B\colon X\to\univ$ denote (by abuse of notation) the type family
\[
    (A\to B)(x)\defeq A(x)\to B(x).
\]
Given a path\/ $p\colon x\eq X y$ and a function\/ $f\colon (A\to B)(x)$, we have the following diagram:
\begin{equation}\label{tik:non-dependent-transport-composition}
    \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=2.5cm]
        A(x) 
            \arrow[r, "f"] 
            \arrow[d, "{\fun{transport}^A(p)}"'] 
        & B(x) 
            \arrow[d, "{\fun{transport}^B(p)}"] 
        \\
        A(y) 
            \arrow[r, "{\fun{transport}^{A\to B}(p, f)}"'] 
        & B(y)
    \end{tikzcd}
\end{equation}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:non-dependent-transport-composition}
    The diagram~\eqref{tik:non-dependent-transport-composition} propositionally commutes in the function type\/ $A(y)\to B(y)$. In particular,
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{A\to B}(p,f)
            \eq{A(y)\to B(y)}
            \fun{transport}^B(p)
                \circ f
                \circ 
                \fun{transport}^A(p^{-1}).
    \]
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    First, observe that the diagram is well-typed because
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{A\to B}(p,f)\colon (A\to B)(y) \equiv A(y)\to B(y).
    \]
    To prove the commutativity, by path induction, it suffices to consider the case\/ $y\equiv x$ and\/ $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case, we obtain the square
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=2.5cm]
            A(x) 
                \arrow[r, "f"] 
                \arrow[d, "{\fun{transport}^A(\fun{refl}_x)}"'] 
            & B(x) 
                \arrow[d, "{\fun{transport}^B(\fun{refl}_x)}"] 
            \\
            A(x) 
                \arrow[r, "{\fun{transport}^{A\to B}(\fun{refl}_x, f)}"'] 
            & B(x)
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    which trivially (and definitionally) commutes because all transports of reflexivity reduce to identity functions.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:transport-decomposition-for-paths}
    Let\/ $A\colon\univ$ be a type and\/ $a\colon A$ a term. Given\/ $p\colon x_1\eq Ax_2$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        1.\,&\fun{transport}^{x\mapsto(a\eq Ax)}(p,q)
            \eq{}q\ct p
            &&\text{for }q\colon a\eq Ax_1,\\
        2.\,&\fun{transport}^{x\mapsto(x\eq Aa)}(p,q)
            \eq{}p^{-1}\ct q
            &&\text{for }q\colon x_1\eq Aa,\\
        3.\,&\fun{transport}^{x\mapsto(x\eq Ax)}(p,q)
            \eq{}p^{-1}\ct q\ct p
            &&\text{for }q\colon x_1\eq Ax_1.
    \end{align*}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof} For type verification, observe the following
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs(1)&\colon a\eq Ax_2.
            &\lhs(2)&\colon x_2\eq Aa.
            &\lhs(3)&\colon x_2\eq Ax_2.\\
            \rhs(1)&\colon a\eq Ax_2.
            &\rhs(2)&\colon x_2\eq Aa.
            &\rhs(3)&\colon x_2\eq Ax_2.
        \end{align*}
    
    By induction on $p$ it suffices to consider the case $x_2\equiv x_1$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_{x_1}$. In that case
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^{x\mapsto(a\eq Ax)}(\fun{refl}_{x_1},q)
            &\equiv q
            \equiv\fun{refl}_{x_1}\ct q.\\
        \fun{transport}^{x\mapsto(x\eq Aa)}(\fun{refl}_{x_1},q)
            &\equiv q
            \equiv\fun{refl}_{x_1}^{-1}\ct q.\\
        \fun{transport}^{x\mapsto(x\eq Ax)}(\fun{refl}_{x_1},q)
            &\equiv q\\
            &\eq{x\eq Ax}\fun{refl}_{x_1}^{-1}
                \ct q
                \ct\fun{refl}_{x_1}.
    \end{align*}
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:transport-in-function-intersection}
    Let\/ $f\colon A\to C$ and\/ $g\colon B\to C$ be two functions. Define the type family\/ $P\colon A\times B\to\univ$ by\/ $P(x,y)\defeq f(x)\eq{C}g(y)$. Then, given paths\/ $p\colon x_1\eq{A}x_2$,\/ $q\colon y_1\eq{B}y_2$, and an element\/ $r\colon f(x_1)\eq{C}g(y_1)$, as illustrated by the paths in\/ $C$ below
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}
            \fun1
                    \arrow[rdd,"x_1"]
                    \arrow[rrd,"y_1"']
                    \arrow[rdd,"x_2"',bend right=40]
                    \arrow[rrd,"y_2",bend left=36]
                    \arrow[rrdd,
                        "\scriptstyle r",
                        phantom,
                        description,
                        pos=0.65]
                    \arrow[rdd,
                        "\scriptstyle p",
                        phantom,
                        description,
                        bend right=20,
                        pos=0.5]
                    \arrow[rrd,
                        "\scriptstyle q",
                        phantom,
                        description,
                        bend left=18,
                        pos=0.5]\\
                &&B
                    \arrow[d,"g"]\\
                &A
                    \arrow[r,"f"']
                &C
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^P\bigl(\fun{pair}^=(p,q),r\bigr)
            \eq{}\fun{ap}_f(p)^{-1}\ct r\ct\fun{ap}_g(q).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    The transport on the \lhs defines a map
    \[
        (f(x_1)\eq Cg(y_1))\to(f(x_2)\eq Cg(y_2)).
    \]
    Hence, the \lhs inhabits $f(x_2)\eq Cg(y_2)$. The \rhs is a concatenation of paths $f(x_2)\eq Cf(x_1)$, $f(x_1)\eq Cg(y_1)$, and $g(y_1)\eq Cg(y_2)$, which also computes to a path in $f(x_2)\eq Cg(y_2)$.

    By path induction on $p$ and then on $q$, it suffices to assume $x_2\equiv x_1$, $p\equiv\fun{refl}_{x_1}$, $y_2\equiv y_1$ and $q\equiv\fun{refl}_{y_1}$. In this case the \lhs computes to $r$, as it does the \rhs:
    \[
        \fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_{x_1})^{-1}
            \ct r
            \ct\fun{ap}_g(\fun{refl}_{y_1})
        \equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x_1)}^{-1}
            \ct r
            \ct\fun{refl}_{g(y_1)}
        \eq{f(x_1)\eq Cg(y_1)}r.
    \]
\end{proof}
\paragraph{Dependent case.} To generalize the non-dependent case, we consider the situation where
\begin{align*}
    B&\colon\prod_{x\colon X}A(x)\to\univ.
\intertext{The components from the non-dependent context generalize as follows:}
    \Pi_AB&\colon X\to\univ\\
    \Pi_AB(x)&\defeq\prod_{u\colon A(x)}B(x,u)\\
    f&\colon\Pi_AB(x).
\intertext{We introduce the total space and the uncurried family:}
    \Sigma_XA&\defeq\sum_{x\colon X}A(x)
        &&\text{(total space)}\\
    \hat B&\colon\Sigma_XA\to\univ
        &&\text{(uncurried\/ $B$)}\\
    \hat{B}(\omega)&\defeq B(\pi_1(\omega),\pi_2(\omega))
        &&\text{(induction principle)}.
\end{align*}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:dependent-transport-decomp}
    Let\/ $A\colon X\to\univ$ and\/ $B\colon\prod_{x\colon X}A(x)\to\univ$ be type families,\/ $x,y\colon X$ and\/ $p\colon x\eq Xy$. Given\/ $f\colon \Pi_A B(x)$ and\/ $u\colon A(x)$, define
    \begin{alignat*}2
        p_*&\defeq\fun{transport}^A(p),
        &\quad\gamma&\defeq\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}})
            \colon\dep{x,u}\eq{\Sigma_XA}\dep{y,p_*(u)}.
    \end{alignat*}
    Then the following diagram of elements commutes propositionally:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge,row sep=large]
            u
                \arrow[r,mapsto,"p_*"]
                \arrow[d,mapsto,"f"']
            &p_*(u)
                \arrow[d,
                    mapsto,
                    "{\fun{transport}^{\Pi_A B}(p,f)}"] 
        \\
            f(u)
                \arrow[r,mapsto,"\fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\gamma)"']
        &\fun{transport}^{\Pi_A B}(p,f)(p_*(u))
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    Explicitly, we have the equality
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\gamma,f(u))
        \eq{B(y,p_*(u))}
        \bigl(\fun{transport}^{\Pi_A B}(p,f)\bigr)(p_*(u)).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Type verification.] 
        Note that, since $u\colon A(x)$, we have $f(u)\colon B(x,u)$. Hence,
        \[
            \fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\gamma)
                \colon B(x,u)\to B(y,p_*(u))
        \]
        and
        \[
            \lhs\equiv\fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\gamma,f(u))
                \colon B(y,p_*(u)).
        \]
        Since
        \begin{align*}
            &\fun{transport}^{\Pi_AB}(p)
                \colon\Pi_A B(x)\to\Pi_AB(y),
        \intertext{we obtain}
            &\fun{transport}^{\Pi_AB}(p,f)\colon\Pi_AB(y),
        \intertext{and so}
            &\rhs\equiv\bigl(\fun{transport}^{\Pi_AB}(p,f)\bigr)(p_*(u))
                \colon B(y,p_*(u)).
        \end{align*}
        Therefore, both sides of the equation are of type $B(y,p_*(u))$.
        \item[Inhabitation.] By path induction, it suffices to consider the case $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In that case, we deduce that $\gamma\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}}$. Therefore,
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs&\equiv\fun{transport}^{\hat B}
                (\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,u}},f(u))\\
                &\equiv f(u)
        \intertext{and}
            \rhs&\equiv\bigl(\fun{transport}^{\Pi_A B}
                (\fun{refl}_x,f)\bigr)(u)\\
                &\equiv f(u),
        \end{align*}
        which establishes that $\lhs\equiv\rhs$.
    \end{description}
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}
    The previous theorem is to\/ $\Pi$-types what Theorem~\ref{thm:composite-transport} is to\/ $\Sigma$-types. To better visualize the analogy, let us rewrite the equality of Theorem~\ref{thm:composite-transport} using the path\/ $\gamma\defeq\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}})$ in the total space.
    
    Let
    \[
        \Sigma_AB\colon X\to\univ,
        \quad\Sigma_AB(x)\defeq\sum_{u\colon A(x)}B(x,u).
    \]
    Then, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \explain[\text{transport }\dep{u,z}\text{ along }p]
            {\fun{transport}^{\Sigma_AB}(p)(\dep{u,z})}
        &\eq{\Sigma_AB(y)}
            \bigdep{
            \explain[\text{transport }u]{p_*(u)},
            \explain[\text{transport }z\text{ along }\gamma]
            {\fun{transport}^B(\gamma)(z)}
            }\\
    \explain[\text{transport }f(u)\text{ along }\gamma]
        {\fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\gamma,f(u))}
        &\eq{B(y,p_*(u))}
        \bigl(
        \explain[\text{transport }f\text{ along }p]
        {\fun{transport}^{\Pi_A B}(p,f)}
        \bigr)(p_*(u)).
    \end{align*}
    In words,
    \begin{align*}
        \text{transport a dependent pair}
            &= \text{pair the transports},\\
        \text{transport an evaluation}
            &= \text{evaluate the transport}.
    \end{align*}
    This means that transport commutes with dependent pairing in the first case, and with function application in the second.
\end{rem}

\begin{cor}\label{cor:dependent-transport-decomp}
    With the preceding notation, for\/ $v\colon A(y)$ we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{\Pi_AB}(p,f)(v)
        \eq{B(y,v)}
        \fun{transport}^{\hat B}
        \bigl(
            \delta^{-1},f((p^{-1})_*(v))
        \bigr),
    \]
    where\/ $\delta\defeq\fun{pair}^=(\dep{p^{-1},\fun{refl}_{(p^{-1})_*(v)}})$.
\end{cor}

\begin{proof}
    Even though this can be derived from the theorem, it is much simpler to use path induction and verify the definitional equality.
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Type verification:]
        First observe that, by definition,
        \[
            \lhs\equiv\fun{transport}^{\Pi_AB}(p,f)(v)
                \colon B(y,v).
        \]
        To compute the $\rhs$, we need to compute $\delta$. Let $w\defeq(p^{-1})_*(v)\colon A(x)$. By Definition~\ref{defn:Sigma-pair}, we have
        \[
            \fun{pair}^=\colon
                \biggl(
                \sum_{q\colon\pi_1(\omega)\eq X\pi_1(\omega')}
                q_*(\pi_2(\omega))\eq{A(\pi_1(\omega'))}\pi_2(\omega')
                \biggr)
                \to(\omega\eq{\Sigma_XA}\omega').
        \]
        In our case, $\omega\defeq\dep{y,v}$, $\omega'\defeq\dep{x,w}$, and $q\defeq p^{-1}$. Therefore,
        \[
            \fun{pair}^=\colon
                \biggl(
                \sum_{q\colon y\eq X x}
                q_*(v)\eq{A(x)}w
                \biggr)
                \to(\dep{y,v}\eq{\Sigma_XA}\dep{x,w}).
        \]
        Thus, we can apply $\fun{pair}^=$ to the dependent pair $\dep{q,r}$, provided that $r\colon q_*(v)\eq{A(x)}w$. Since $q_*(v)\defeq(p^{-1})_*(v)\equiv w$, we may take $r\defeq\fun{refl}_w$ to deduce that 
        \[
            \dep{p^{-1},\fun{refl}_w}
                \colon\dom(\fun{pair}^=).
        \]
        Moreover,
        \[
            \delta\defeq
                \fun{pair}^=(\dep{p^{-1},\fun{refl}_w})
                    \colon\dep{y,v}\eq{\Sigma_XA}\dep{x,w}.
        \]
        Therefore,
        \[
            \fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\delta^{-1})\colon
                \hat B(\dep{x,w})\to\hat B(\dep{y,v}),
        \]
        which is definitionally equal to
        \[
            \fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\delta^{-1})
                \colon B(x,w)\to B(y,v).
        \]
        Since $f\colon\Pi_AB(x)$, we have $f(w)\colon B(x,w)$. Hence,
        \[
            \rhs\equiv\fun{transport}^{\hat B}(\delta^{-1},f(w))
                \colon B(y,v).
        \]
        \item[Inhabitation:] By path induction on $p$, the goal reduces to the case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. We obtain
        \begin{align*}
            \lhs&\equiv
                \fun{transport}^{\Pi_AB}(\fun{refl}_x,f)(v)\\
                &\equiv f(v),\\
            \delta&\equiv\fun{pair}^=\bigl(
                    \dep{\fun{refl}_x,
                    \fun{refl}_{(\fun{refl}_x)_*(v)}}
                \bigr)\\
                &\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,v}}
                    &&\text{; Rem.~\ref{rem:pair=-at-base-code}}\\
            \rhs
            &\equiv
                \fun{transport}^{\hat B}
                    \bigl(\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,v}},f((\fun{refl}_x)_*(v))\bigr)
                &&;\ \delta^{-1}\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,v}}\\
            &\equiv f((\fun{refl}_x)_*(v))\\
            &\equiv f(v).
        \end{align*}\qedhere
    \end{description}
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:transport-function-codomain}
    Let\/ $A$ be a type, $P\colon X\to\univ$ a type family. Given $x,y\colon A$ and\/ $p\colon x\eq Xy$, for any function\/ $f\colon A\to P(x)$, we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{\lambda z.\,(A\to P(z))}(p,f)
            \eq{A\to P(y)}\lambda a.\,\fun{transport}^P(p,f(a)).
    \]
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    The \lhs $\fun{transport}$ maps $p$ to a function $(A\to P(x))\to(A\to P(y))$. Therefore, the \lhs at $p$ maps $f\colon A\to P(x)$ to a function $A\to P(y)$.

    The \rhs $\fun{transport}$ at $p$ is a map from $P(x)$ to $P(y)$. Thus, given $a\colon A$, its value at $f(a)\colon P(x)$ is an element of $P(y)$. In sum the \rhs is also a map from $A$ to $P(y)$.

    To verify the propositional equality, by based path induction on $p$, it suffices to consider the case $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In that case the \lhs reduces to $f$ and the \rhs to $\lambda a.\,f(a)$, which is definitionally equal to $f$.

    %
    
\end{proof}

\begin{rem}
    Suppose we have two type families $A,B\colon X\to\univ$, a point $x\colon X$ and a function $f\colon A(x)\to B(x)$. Then, given a second point $y\colon X$ and a path $p\colon x\eq Xy$, to transport $f$ along $p$ for getting a new function 
    \[
        p_*(f)\colon A(y)\to B(y),
    \]
    we can specify
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge, row sep=large]
            A(y)
                    \arrow[r,dashed,"p_*(f)"]
                    \arrow[d,"{(p^{-1})_*}"']
                &B(y)\\
            A(x)
                    \arrow[r,"f"']
                &B(x)
                    \arrow[u,"p_*"']
        \end{tikzcd}
        \qquad
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=large, row sep=large]
            v
                    \arrow[r,dashed,maps to]
                    \arrow[d,maps to]
                &{p_*\bigl(f((p^{-1})_*(v))\bigr)}\\
            {(p^{-1})_*(v)}
                    \arrow[r,maps to]
                &{f((p^{-1})_*(v))}
                    \arrow[u,maps to]
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
\end{rem}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:transport^A->B}
    Let\/ $A, B\colon X\to\univ$ be type families, and consider the family of function types\/ $A\to B\colon X\to\univ$ defined by\/ $(A\to B)(x)\defeq A(x)\to B(x)$. For any path\/ $p\colon x\eq Xy$, function\/ $f\colon A(x)\to B(x)$, and element\/ $v\colon A(y)$, the transport of\/ $f$ along\/ $p$ evaluates as
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{A\to B}(p,f)(v) \eq{B(y)} p_*\bigl(f((p^{-1})_*(v))\bigr),
    \]
    where $p_*\equiv\fun{transport}^B(p,\dummy)$ and $(p^{-1})_*\equiv\fun{transport}^A(p,\dummy)$.
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    By path induction on $p\colon x\eq Xy$, it suffices to consider the base case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. But in that case both sides are definitionally reduced to $f(v)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lem}\label{lem:non-dependent-i-j-paths}
    Let\/ $A\colon X\to\univ$ be a type family and\/ $p\colon x\eq Xy$ a path in~$X$. Then, given a second type family\/ $B\colon X\to\univ$ and a non-dependent function\/ $f\colon A(x)\to B(x)$, for any\/ $u\colon A(x)$ there are two paths
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:non-dependent-i-j-paths}
        \begin{aligned}
            i(p,u)&\colon p_*(f)(p_*(u))
                \eq{B(y)}p_*\bigl(f(p^{-1}_*(p_*(u)))\bigr),\\
            j(p,u)&\colon p_*\bigl(f(p^{-1}_*(p_*(u)))\bigr)
                \eq{B(y)}p_*(f(u)),
        \end{aligned}
    \end{equation}
    where we use the abbreviations:
    \begin{equation}\label{eq:non-dependent-p*-meanings}
        \begin{aligned}
            p_*(f)&\defeq\fun{transport}^{A\to B}(p,f),\\
            p_*(f(u))&\defeq\fun{transport}^B(p,f(u)),\\
            p_*(u)&\defeq\fun{transport}^A(p,u).
        \end{aligned}
    \end{equation}
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    Define the motive
    \begin{align*}
        P&\colon\prod_{y\colon X}(x\eq Xy)\to\univ\\
        P(y,p)&\defeq \prod_{u\colon A(x)}
            \fun{Eq}_i(y,p,u) \times \fun{Eq}_j(y,p,u),
    \end{align*}
    where $\fun{Eq}_i$ and $\fun{Eq}_j$ are the identity types corresponding to $i(p,u)$ and $j(p,u)$.
    
    By based path induction, it suffices to construct an inhabitant of $P(x,\fun{refl}_x)$.
    In this case, given $u\colon A(x)$, both equalities reduce to $f(u)\eq{B(x)}f(u)$. Hence,
    \[
        \lambda u.\,(\fun{refl}_{f(u)},\,\fun{refl}_{f(u)})
            \colon P(x,\fun{refl}_x).
    \]
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\fe\label{thm:function-equality-equivalence}
    Let\/ $A\colon X\to\univ$ be a type family and\/ $p\colon x\eq Xy$ a path in $X$. Then, given a second type family $B\colon X\to\univ$ and two functions\/ $f\colon A(x)\to B(x)$ and\/ $g\colon A(y)\to B(y)$, there is an equivalence
    \begin{align*}
        \bigl(p_*(f)\eq{A(y)\to B(y)}g\bigr)
            &\simeq(p_*\circ f\sim g\circ p_*),
    \end{align*}
    where $p_*\circ f$ and $g\circ p_*$ have signature
    \[
        p_*\circ f,\;g\circ p_*\colon A(x)\to B(y).
    \]
    Moreover, if\/ $q\colon p_*(f)\eq{A\to B}g$ corresponds under this equivalence to\/ $\hat q$, then for any\/ $u\colon A(x)$, the path
    \[
        \fun{happly}(q,p_*(u))
            \colon p_*(f)(p_*(u))\eq{B(y)}g(p_*(u))
    \]
    satisfies
    \[
        \fun{happly}(q,p_*(u))
        \eq{B(y)}
        i(p,u)\ct j(p,u)\ct\hat q(u),
    \]
    where\/ $i(p,u)$ and\/ $j(p,u)$ are the paths given by\/ \eqref{eq:non-dependent-i-j-paths}.
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    To define the motive
    \[
        P\colon\prod_{y\colon X}(x\eq Xy)\to\univ,
    \]
    we proceed as follows:
    \begin{enumerate}[-]
        \item For $y\colon X$ and $p\colon x\eq Xy$, let
        \begin{align*}
            \fun L(y,p,g)
                &\defeq p_*(f)\eq{A(y)\to B(y)}g,\\
            \fun R(y,p,g)
                &\defeq p_*\circ f\sim g\circ p_*.
        \end{align*}

        \item Then define
        \[
            P(y,p)\defeq\prod_{g\colon A(y)\to B(y)}
                \;\sum_{e\colon \fun L\simeq\fun R}
                \fun E(y,p,g,e),
        \]
        where
        \[
            \fun E(y,p,g,e)\defeq\!\!\!
                \prod_{q\colon\fun L(y,p,g)}
                \,\prod_{u\colon A(x)}
                    \!\!\fun{happly}(q,p_*(u))
                    \eq{B(y)}
                    i(p,u)\ct j(p, u)\ct e(q)(u),
        \]
        and $i(p,u)$ and $j(p,u)$ are the paths defined in \eqref{eq:non-dependent-i-j-paths}. The following diagram, where the arrows represent paths, shows that $\fun E$ is well defined:
        \[
            \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=4em, row sep=3em]
                p_*(f)(p_*(u))
                        \arrow[r,"{\fun{happly}(q, p_*(u))}"]
                        \arrow[d,"{i(p,u)}"']
                    &g(p_*(u))\\
                {p_*\bigl(f((p^{-1})_*(p_*(u)))\bigr)}
                        \arrow[r,"{j(p,u)}"']
                    &{p_*(f(u))}
                        \arrow[u,"e(q)(u)"']
            \end{tikzcd}
        \]
        To see this, recall from \eqref{eq:happly-is-ap-ev} that $\fun{happly}(q,v)\eq{B(y)}\fun{ap}_{\ev v}(p)$, which shows that the top arrow represents the resulting path. Moreover, since $e\colon\fun L\simeq\fun R$ and $q\colon p_*(f)\eq{A(y)\to B(y)}g$, by identifying $e$ with its first projection, we obtain $e(q)\colon\fun R$ and $e(q)(u)\colon p_*(f(u))\eq{B(y)}g(p_*(u))$.
    \end{enumerate}
    By based path induction, i.e., by equation \eqref{eq:ind'=A} applied to $P(y,p)$, we have to construct an inhabitant for the case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case:
    \begin{enumerate}[-]
        \item $p_*\equiv\id$, $\fun L(x,\fun{refl}_x,g)\equiv f\eq{A(x)\to B(x)}g$, and $\fun R(x,\fun{refl}_x,g)\equiv f\sim g$.

        \item $i(\fun{refl}_x,u)\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(u)}$ and $j(\fun{refl}_x,u)\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(u)}$.

        \item We choose $e\defeq\fun{happly}$, which is an equivalence by the function extensionality axiom.
        The type $\fun E(x,\fun{refl}_x,g,\fun{happly})$ requires us to verify that for every $q\colon f\eq{A(x)\to B(x)}g$ and $u\colon A(x)$,
        \[
            \fun{happly}(q,u)
            \eq{B(x)}
            \fun{refl}_{f(u)}
                \ct \fun{refl}_{f(u)}
                \ct\fun{happly}(q,u).
        \]
        But this is inhabited by $\fun{refl}_{\fun{happly}(q,u)}$.
    \end{enumerate}
    Thus, the map
    \[
        g\mapsto(\fun{happly}
        ,\lambda q.\,\lambda u.\,\fun{refl}_{\fun{happly}(q,u)})
    \]
    inhabits $P(x,\fun{refl}_x)$, which completes the proof.
\end{proof}

What follows is a generalization of Lemma~\ref{lem:non-dependent-i-j-paths} and Theorem~\ref{thm:function-equality-equivalence} for dependent functions. The notation is the one introduced in the Dependent case of section \nameref{subs:transport-decomposition}.

\begin{lem}\label{lem:dependent-i-j-path}
    Let $A\colon X\to\univ$ be a type family and $p\colon x\eq Xy$ a path in~$X$. Then, given a second type family $B\colon\prod_{x\colon X}A(x)\to\univ$ and a dependent function $f\colon\Pi_AB(x)$, we have two paths
            \begin{align*}
                i(p,u)&\colon p_*(f)(p_*(u))
                    \eq{B(y,p_*(u))}\Phi((p^{-1})_*(p_*(u)))\\
                j(p,u)&\colon \Phi((p^{-1})_*(p_*(u)))
                    \eq{B(y,p_*(u))}\fun{Tr}(p,f,u),
            \end{align*}
            with
            \begin{align*}
                \Phi(w)&\defeq
                    \fun{transport}^{\hat B}
                    \bigl(\fun{pair}^=
                        (p^{-1},\fun{refl}_w)^{-1},f(w)
                    \bigr)\\
                \fun{Tr}(p,f,u)&\defeq
                    \fun{transport}^{\hat B}
                    \bigl(
                        \fun{pair}^=(p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}),
                        f(u)
                    \bigr).
            \end{align*}
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Type verification:] 
        Observe that\footnote{See the notation used in Theorem~\ref{thm:dependent-transport-decomp}.}
        \begin{alignat*}6
            u&\colon A(x),&\quad p_*(u)&\colon A(y),
                &\quad w\equiv(p^{-1})_*(p_*(u))&\colon A(x).
        \end{alignat*}
        Thus, as shown in Corollary~\ref{cor:dependent-transport-decomp}, \textsc{type verification}, for $v\defeq p_*(u)$:
        \begin{alignat*}4
            \fun{pair}^=(p^{-1},\fun{refl}_w)^{-1}
                    &\colon(x,w)\eq{\Sigma_XA}(y,p_*(u)),
                    &\quad f(w)&\colon B(x,w),\\
            \Phi(w)&\colon B(y,p_*(u)),
                &\quad\fun{Tr}(p,f,u)&\colon B(y,p_*(u)).
        \end{alignat*}
        Then all expressions are correctly typed.

        \item[Inhabitation:] To construct the witnesses $i(p,u)$ and $j(p,u)$, define the motive
        \begin{align*}
            P&\colon\prod_{y\colon X}(x\eq Xy)\to\univ\\
            P(y,p)&\defeq\prod_{u\colon A(x)}
                \fun{Eq}_i(y,p,u)\times\fun{Eq}_j(y,p,u),
        \end{align*}
        where $\fun{Eq}_i$ and $\fun{Eq}_j$ are the types of $i(p,u)$ and $j(p,u)$.
    
        By based path induction, to show that $P(y,p)$ is inhabited it suffices to construct a witness of $P(x,\fun{refl}_x)$. In this case:
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item $p$ and $p^{-1}$ reduce definitionally to $\fun{refl}_x$.
            
            \item Since the transport operations $p_*$ reduce to identity functions, we get $p_*(u)\equiv u$ and $p_*(f)\equiv f$.
            
            \item The fiber coordinate $w\defeq(p^{-1})_*(p_*(u))$ reduces definitionally to $u$.
            
            \item $\Phi(w)$ becomes $f(u)$.
    
            \item Finally,
            \begin{align*}
                \fun{Tr}(\fun{refl}_x,f,u)
                &\equiv\fun{transport}^{\hat B}
                \bigl(
                    \fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_u),
                    f(u)
                \bigr)\\
                &\equiv\fun{transport}^{\hat B}
                    \big(\fun{refl}_{(x,u)},f(u)\big)
                        &&\text{; Rem.~\ref{rem:pair=-at-base-code}}\\
                &\equiv f(u).
            \end{align*}
        \end{enumerate}
        In consequence, for any $u\colon A(x)$, the goals become:
        \begin{align*}
            i(\fun{refl}_x,u)&\colon f(u)\eq{B(x,u)}f(u),\\
            j(\fun{refl}_x,u) &\colon f(u)\eq{B(x,u)}f(u).
        \end{align*}
        These are clearly inhabited by $\fun{refl}_{f(u)}$.
        Thus, the term
        \[
            \lambda u.\,(\fun{refl}_{f(u)},\, \fun{refl}_{f(u)})
        \]
        witnesses $P(x,\fun{refl}_x)$, completing the proof.\qedhere
    \end{description}
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\fe\label{thm:dependent-function-equality-equivalence}
    Let\/ $A\colon X\to\univ$ and\/ $B\colon\prod_{x\colon X}A(x)\to\univ$ be two type families. Given a path $p\colon x\eq Xy$ and two functions\/ $f\colon\Pi_AB(x)$ and\/ $g\colon\Pi_AB(y)$, there is an equivalence
    \[
        \bigl(p_*(f)\eq{\Pi_AB(y)}g\bigr)
        \simeq
        %\prod_{u\colon A(x)}\fun{Tr}(p,f,u)\eq{B(y,p_*(u))}g(p_*(u))
        \bigl(\fun{Tr}(p,f)\sim g\circ p_*\bigr),
    \]
    where
    \[
        \fun{Tr}(p,f,u)\defeq
            \fun{transport}^{\hat B}
            \bigl(
                \fun{pair}^=(\dep{p,\fun{refl}_{p_*(u)}}),
                f(u)
            \bigr).
    \]
    Moreover, if\/ $q\colon p_*(f)\eq{\Pi_AB(y)}g$ corresponds under this equivalence to\/ $\hat q$, then for any\/ $u\colon A(x)$, the path
    \[
        \fun{happly}(q,p_*(u))
        \colon p_*(f)(p_*(u))\eq{B(y,p_*(u))}g(p_*(u))
    \]
    is equal to the concatenated path
    \[
        i(p,u)\ct j(p,u)\ct\hat q(u),
    \]
    where\/ $i(p,u)$ and $j(p,u)$ are the paths given by\/ {\upshape Lemma~\ref{lem:dependent-i-j-path}}, as illustrated in the following diagram:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=6em, row sep=3em]
            p_*(f)(p_*(u))
                    \arrow[r,"{\fun{happly}(q, p_*(u))}"]
                    \arrow[d,"{i(p,u)}"']
                &g(p_*(u))\\
            \Phi((p^{-1})_*(p_*(u)))
                    \arrow[r,"{j(p,u)}"']
            &\fun{Tr}(p,f,u)
                    \arrow[u,"\hat q(u)"']
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    with $\Phi$ defined in\/ {\upshape Lemma~\ref{lem:dependent-i-j-path}}.
\end{thm}

\needspace{2\baselineskip}
\begin{proof}${}$
    \begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
        \item[Type verification:] We need to verify that both sides of the equivalence are well-formed elements of\/ $\univ$.
        
        For the \lhs, observe that $p_*(f)$ and $g$ both inhabit the function type $\Pi_AB(y)$; thus, the identity type $p_*(f)\eq{\Pi_AB(x)}g$ is well-formed.

        For the \rhs, we must ensure the terms inhabit the same fiber.
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item By Lemma~\ref{lem:dependent-i-j-path}, $\fun{Tr}(p,f,u) \colon B(y, p_*(u))$.
            
            \item Since $g\colon \Pi_AB(y)$ and $p_*(u)\colon A(y)$, we have $g(p_*(u)) \colon B(y, p_*(u))$.
        \end{enumerate}
        Since both terms inhabit $B(y, p_*(u))$, the identity type on the right is also well-formed.
        
        \item[Inhabitation:] To define the motive
        \[
            P\colon\prod_{y\colon X}(x\eq Xy)\to\univ
        \]
        proceed as follows:
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item For $y\colon X$ and $p\colon x\eq Xy$, let
            \begin{align*}
                \fun L(y,p,g)
                    &\defeq p_*(f)\eq{\Pi_AB(y)}g,\\
                \fun R(y,p,g)
                    &\defeq\fun{Tr}(p,f)\sim g\circ p_*.
            \end{align*}
    
            \item Then define
            \[
                P(y,p)\defeq\prod_{g\colon\Pi_AB(y)}
                    \;\sum_{e\colon\fun L\simeq\fun R}
                    \fun E(y,p,g,e),
            \]
            where
            \[
                \fun E(y,p,g,e)\defeq\!\!\!
                    \prod_{q\colon\fun L(y,p,g)}
                    \;\prod_{u\colon A(x)}
                        \fun{happly}(q,v)
                        \eq{B(y,v)}
                        \delta(p,u)\ct e(q)(u),
            \]
            with $v\defeq p_*(u)$ and $\delta(p,u)\defeq i(p,u)\ct j(p,u)$.
        \end{enumerate}
        By based path induction, it suffices to specify an inhabitant for the case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case:
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item $\fun L(x,\fun{refl}_x,g)\equiv f\eq{}g$,  $\fun{Tr}(\fun{refl}_x,f,u)\equiv f(u)$, $\fun R(x,\fun{refl}_x,g)\equiv f\sim g$.
    
            \item $i(\fun{refl}_x,u)$ and $j(\fun{refl}_x,u)$ reduce to $\fun{refl}_{f(u)}$.
    
            \item Take $e\defeq\fun{happly}$, which is an equivalence by function extensionality. The type $\fun E(x,\fun{refl}_x,g,\fun{happly})$ requires us to verify that for every $q\colon f\eq{\Pi_AB}g$ and $u\colon A(x)$,
            \[
                \fun{happly}(q,u)
                \eq{B(x,u)}
                \fun{refl}_{f(u)}
                \ct\fun{happly}(q,u).
            \]
            This is inhabited by $\fun{refl}_{\fun{happly}(q,u)}$.
        \end{enumerate}
        Thus, the map
        \[
            g\mapsto(\fun{happly}
            ,\lambda q.\,\lambda u.\,\fun{refl}_{\fun{happly}(q,u)})
        \]
        inhabits $P(x,\fun{refl}_x)$, which completes the proof.\qedhere
    \end{description}
\end{proof}

\section{Naturality of Function Extensionality}\label{naturality-of-funcext}

Let $f,g\colon A\to B$ be functions. Recall that a homotopy $\eta\colon f\sim g$ translates pointwise into a path $\eta(x)\colon f(x)\eq{B}g(x)$ for each $x\colon A$, whereas an identity path $p\colon f\eq{A\to B}g$ operates at the level of the function types. These two notions are related by the equivalence $\fun{happly}\colon(f\eq{}g)\simeq(f\sim g)$.

The left whiskering of a function $h\colon B\to C$ and a homotopy $\eta$ is defined pointwise as
\begin{align*}
    (h\lwct \eta)(x)&\defeq\fun{ap}_h(\eta(x))
        &&\text{(homotopy whiskering)}
    \intertext{For an identity path $p\colon f\eq{A\to B}g$, we define left whiskering as}
    h\lwct p&\defeq\fun{ap}_{h\circ-}(p)
        &&\text{(function identity whiskering)}
\end{align*}
\[
    \begin{tikzcd}[every cell/.append style={font=\small},
        scale=0.5]
        A
                \arrow[r,"f",bend left]
                \arrow[r,"g"',bend right]
                \arrow[rr,"h\circ f",dashed,bend left=55]
                \arrow[rr,"h\circ f"',dashed,bend right=55]
                \arrow[r,phantom,description,"\scriptstyle p"]
            &B
                \arrow[r,"h"]
            &C
    \end{tikzcd}
\]

\begin{lem}\label{lem:left-whiskering-naturality}
    Both notions of whiskering are related by
    \[
        \fun{happly}(h\lwct p)(x)\eq{C}(h\lwct\fun{happly}(p))(x),
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    Note that $\fun{happly}$ maps $h\lwct p$ to a~homotopy. Furthermore, since $\fun{happly}(p)$ is already a homotopy, the whiskering on the \rhs\ is a homotopy whiskering.

    By based path induction on $p$, it suffices to consider $g\equiv f$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_f$:
    \begin{align*}
        \lhs&\equiv
            \fun{happly}(h\lwct\fun{refl}_f)(x)\\
            &\equiv\fun{happly}(\fun{ap}_{h\circ-}(\fun{refl}_f))(x)\\
            &\equiv\fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_{h\circ f})(x)\\
            &\equiv(\lambda y.\,\fun{refl}_{h\circ f(y)})(x)\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{h\circ f(x)}.\\[1mm]
        \rhs&\equiv
            (h\lwct\fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_f))(x)\\
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_h
                \bigl(
                    \fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_f)(x)
                \bigr)\\
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_h
                \bigl(
                    (\lambda y.\,\fun{refl}_{f(y)})(x)
                \bigr)\\
            &\equiv\fun{ap}_h(\fun{refl}_{f(x)})\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{h\circ f(x)}.
    \end{align*}
\end{proof}

Analogously, based on the definition of right homotpy whiskering
\begin{align*}
    \eta\rwct h&\defeq\lambda z.\,\eta(h(z))
        \colon f\circ h\sim g\circ h.
    \intertext{we introduce right function identity whiskering of a path $p$ with a function $k\colon C\to A$ as}
    p\rwct h&\defeq\fun{ap}_{-\circ h}(p),    
\end{align*}
\[
    \begin{tikzcd}
        C
                \arrow[r,"h"]
                \arrow[rr,"f\circ h",dashed,bend left=55]
                \arrow[rr,"g\circ h"',dashed,bend right=55]
            &A
                \arrow[r,"f",bend left]
                \arrow[r,"g"',bend right]
                \arrow[r,phantom,description,"\scriptstyle p"]
            &B
    \end{tikzcd}
\]

\begin{lem}\label{lem:right-whiskering-naturality}
    Given\/ $z\colon C$, we have
    \[
        \fun{happly}(p\rwct h)(z)\eq{B}\fun{happly}(p)(h(z)).
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    By based path induction on $p$, we can set $g\equiv f$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_f$:
    \begin{align*}
        \lhs&\equiv
            \fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_f\rwct h)(z)\\
                &\equiv\fun{happly}
                    \bigl(
                        \fun{ap}_{-\circ h}(\fun{refl}_f)
                    \bigr)(z)\\
                &\equiv\fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_{f\circ h})(z)\\
                &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f\circ h(z)}.\\[1mm]
        \rhs&\equiv
            \fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_f)(h(z))\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(h(z))}.
    \end{align*}
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:funext-naturality}\fe{\upshape[Naturality of function extensionality]}
    With the preceding notation, given $\eta\colon f\sim g$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{funext}(h\lwct\eta)&\eq{}h\lwct\fun{funext}(\eta)
    \intertext{and}
        \fun{funext}(\eta\rwct k)&\eq{}\fun{funext}(\eta)\rwct k.
    \end{align*}
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    Using the homotopy $\fun{happly}\circ\fun{funext}\sim\fun{id}$, we deduce that
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(h\lwct\eta))(x)
            &\eq{}(h\lwct\eta)(x)\\
            &\eq{}\fun{ap}_h(\eta(x))
        \intertext{and, since $\fun{funext}(\eta)\colon f\eq{A\to B}g$,}
        \fun{happly}(h\lwct\fun{funext}(\eta))(x)
            &\eq{}\bigl(
                    h\lwct\fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(\eta))
                \bigr)(x)
                &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:left-whiskering-naturality}}\\
            &\eq{}(h\lwct\eta)(x)\\
            &\eq{}\fun{ap}_h(\eta(x)).
    \end{align*}
    Hence, $\fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(h\lwct\eta))(x)\eq{}\fun{happly}(h\lwct\fun{funext}(\eta))(x)$. The first equality follows by applying $\fun{funext}$.

    For the second equality, evaluating $\fun{happly}$ at a point $z\colon C$ yields
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{happly}(\lhs)(z)
            &\equiv\fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(\eta\rwct k))(z)\\
            &\eq{}(\eta\rwct k)(z)\\
            &\equiv\eta(k(z))
    \intertext{and}
        \fun{happly}(\rhs)(z)
            &\equiv\fun{happly}
                \bigl(
                    \fun{funext}(\eta)\rwct k
                \bigr)(z)\\
            &\eq{}\fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(\eta))(k(z))
                &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:right-whiskering-naturality}}\\
            &\eq{}\eta(k(z)).
    \end{align*}
    Since both sides are pointwise equal, $\fun{funext}$ yields the second identity.
    
\end{proof}


In categorical terms, the maps $(h\circ\dummy)$ and $(\dummy\circ k)$ act as functors, and $\fun{happly}$ and $\fun{funext}$ act as natural isomorphisms between the $\Hom$-functors defined by identity types and those defined by homotopies.
\[
    \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=large]
        f\eq{A\to B}g
                \arrow[r,"h\lwct -"]
                \arrow[d,"\fun{happly}"',shift right]
            &h\circ f\eq{A\to C}h\circ g
                \arrow[d,"\fun{happly}",shift left]\\
        f\sim g
                \arrow[r,"h\lwct -"']
                \arrow[u,"\fun{funext}"',shift right]
            &h\circ f\sim h\circ g
                \arrow[u,"\fun{funext}",shift left]
    \end{tikzcd}
    \quad
    \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=large]
        f\eq{A\to B}g
                \arrow[r,"-\rwct k"]
                \arrow[d,"\fun{happly}"',shift right]
            &f\circ k\eq{C\to B}g\circ k
                \arrow[d,"\fun{happly}",shift left]\\
        f\sim g
                \arrow[r,"-\rwct k"']
                \arrow[u,"\fun{funext}"',shift right]
            &f\circ k\sim g\circ k
                \arrow[u,"\fun{funext}",shift left]
    \end{tikzcd}
\]

\begin{rem}
    If we formally interpret functions as paths and function composition as concatenation, function identity terms become\/ $2$-paths. Taking this analogy further, we can apply to it the general notion of left path whiskering introduced in Remark~\ref{rem:path-whiskering-defn}. It formally becomes
    \[
        h\lwct p\defeq\fun{ap}_{\fun{lct}_h}(p),
    \]
    for\/ $p\colon f\eq{A\to B}g$, where\/ $\fun{lct}_h\defeq x\mapsto h\ct x$. Interpreting concatenation analytically as function composition, we have\/ $h\ct x\equiv h\circ x$, so\/ $\fun{lct}_h\equiv h\circ -$ and\/ $h\lwct p\equiv\fun{ap}_{h\circ -}(p)$. Therefore, the definition of left whiskering introduced above matches precisely the general one.

    Analogously, applying the general notion of right path whiskering yields
    \[
        p\rwct k\defeq\fun{ap}_{\fun{rct}_k}(p),
    \]
    where\/ $\fun{rct}_k\defeq x\mapsto x\ct k$. Under the same interpretation, we have\/ $x\ct k\equiv x\circ k$, so\/ $\fun{rct}_k\equiv -\circ k$ and\/ $p\rwct k\equiv\fun{ap}_{-\circ k}(p)$. Thus, the definition of right function identity whiskering also aligns perfectly with the general one.
\end{rem}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:function-path-whiskering-properties}
    Let $h\colon B\to C$, $f,g\colon A\to B$, and $p\colon f\eq{A\to B}g$. Then
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $h\lwct p^{-1}\eq{}(h\lwct p)^{-1}$
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:transport-in-commutative-squares}
    Let\/ $f\colon A\to C$ and\/ $g\colon B\to C$ be functions, and let\/ $X$ be a type. Define the family
    \begin{align*}
        W&\colon(X\to A)\times(X\to B)\to\univ\\
        W(u,v)&\defeq f\circ u\eq{X\to C}g\circ v.
    \end{align*}
    Given paths\/ $p\colon u_1\eq{}u_2$ and\/ $q\colon v_1\eq{}v_2$, and a path\/ $r\colon f\circ u_1\eq{}g\circ v_1$, as illustrated below
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}
            X
                    \arrow[rdd,"u_1"]
                    \arrow[rrd,"v_1"']
                    \arrow[rdd,"u_2"',bend right=40]
                    \arrow[rrd,"v_2",bend left=36]
                    \arrow[rrdd,
                        "\scriptstyle r",
                        phantom,
                        description,
                        pos=0.65]
                    \arrow[rdd,
                        "\scriptstyle p",
                        phantom,
                        description,
                        bend right=20,
                        pos=0.5]
                    \arrow[rrd,
                        "\scriptstyle q",
                        phantom,
                        description,
                        bend left=18,
                        pos=0.5]\\
                &&B
                    \arrow[d,"g"]\\
                &A
                    \arrow[r,"f"']
                &C
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^W\bigl(\fun{pair}^=(p,q),r\bigr)
            \eq{}(f\lwct p)^{-1}\ct r\ct(g\lwct q).
    \]
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    This is a corollary of Theorem~\ref{thm:transport-in-function-intersection}.
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:path-interchange}
    Let\/ $X,Y,Z\colon\univ$ be types, $f,g\colon Y\to Z$ equal functions with $p\colon f\eq{Y\to Z}g$, and\/ $u,v\colon X\to Y$ equal functions with $q\colon u\eq{X\to Y}v$, as depicted below
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=huge]
            X
                    \arrow[r,"u",bend left=35]
                    \arrow[r,"v"',bend right=35]
                    \arrow[r,"\scriptstyle q",phantom]
                &Y
                    \arrow[r,"f",bend left=35]
                    \arrow[r,"g"',bend right=35]
                    \arrow[r,"\scriptstyle p",phantom]
                &Z.
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    Then, we have the canonical equality
    \[
        (f\lwct q)\ct(p\rwct v)
        \eq{f\circ u\eq{X\to Z}g\circ v}
        (p\rwct u)\ct(g\lwct q).
    \]
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    This can be derived from \S\,\ref{homotopy-evaluated-on-homotopy} by function extensionality. However, here we give an independent proof.

    First observe that the path on the \lhs is a concatenation of a path $f\circ u\eq{X\to Z}f\circ v$ and a path $f\circ v\eq{X\to Z}g\circ v$, which computes to a path that inhabits $f\circ u\eq{X\to Z}g\circ v$.

    In the \rhs the first path inhabits $f\circ u\eq{X\to Z}g\circ u$ while the second inhabits $g\circ u\eq{X\to Z}g\circ v$. Thus, their concatenation also computes to a path of type $f\circ u\eq{X\to Z}g\circ v$.

    We proceed by path induction on both \/ $p$ and \/ $q$. It suffices to consider the case where \/ $f\equiv g$ with \/ $p\equiv\fun{refl}_f$, and \/ $u\equiv v$ with \/ $q\equiv\fun{refl}_u$.

    Under these definitions, the left-hand side evaluates to
    \[
        (f\lwct\fun{refl}_u)\ct(\fun{refl}_f\rwct u)
        \equiv\fun{refl}_{f\circ u}\ct\fun{refl}_{f\circ u}
        \equiv\fun{refl}_{f\circ u}.
    \]
    Similarly, the right-hand side evaluates to
    \[
        (\fun{refl}_f\rwct u)\ct(f\lwct\fun{refl}_u)
        \equiv\fun{refl}_{f\circ u}\ct\fun{refl}_{f\circ u}
        \equiv\fun{refl}_{f\circ u}.
    \]
    Since both sides compute to the reflexivity path \/ $\fun{refl}_{f\circ u}$, they are judgmentally equal.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{Homotopy Whiskering}\label{homotopy-whiskering}
Given equivalent functions $f,g\colon A\to B$ with $\alpha\colon f\sim g$, and $f',g'\colon B\to C$ with $\beta\colon f'\sim g'$,
\[
    \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=large]
        A
                \arrow[r,"f",bend left=49]
                \arrow[r,"g\vphantom'"',bend right=49]
                \arrow[r,"\scriptstyle\alpha",phantom]
            &B
                \arrow[r,"f'",bend left=49]
                \arrow[r,"g'"',bend right=49]
                \arrow[r,"\scriptstyle\beta",phantom]
            &C
    \end{tikzcd}
\]
the \textsl{horizontal composition} $\beta\hct\alpha$ is defined using whiskering and homotopy concatenation\footnote{See Definition~\ref{defn:homotopy-inverse-and-ct}.} as
\[
    \beta\hct\alpha\defeq(\beta\rwct f)\ct(g'\lwct\alpha)
        \colon(f'\circ f)\sim(g'\circ g). 
\]

\begin{prop}\label{prop:homotopy-whiskering}\fe
    With the preceding notation,
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item $\beta\hct\alpha\eq{(f'\circ f)\sim(g'\circ g)}(f'\lwct\alpha)\ct(\beta\rwct g)$
    \item $\beta\hct\fun{refl}_f\eq{}\beta\rwct f$
    \item $\fun{refl}_{f'}\lwct\alpha\equiv g'\lwct\alpha$
    \end{enumerate}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}${}$
    For part a) we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{funext}(\beta\hct\alpha)
            &\eq{}\fun{funext}(\beta\rwct f)
                \ct\fun{funext}(g'\lwct\alpha)
                &&\text{; Prop.~\ref{prop:funext-functoriality}}\\
            &\eq{}(\fun{funext}(\beta)\rwct f)
                \ct(g'\lwct\fun{funext}(\alpha))
                &&\text{; Thm.~\ref{thm:funext-naturality}}\\
            &\eq{}(f'\lwct\fun{funext}(\alpha))
                \ct(\fun{funext}(\beta)\rwct g)
                &&\text{; Prop.~\ref{prop:funext-functoriality}}\\
            &\eq{}\fun{funext}((f'\lwct\alpha)\ct(\beta\rwct g)),
    \end{align*}
    and the result follows by evaluation of $\fun{happly}$.

    Parts b) and c) are direct consequences of Remark~\ref{rem:whiskering-with-id}.
\end{proof}

\section{The Univalence Axiom}

To apply the observational framework~\ref{observational-framework} to the universe \/\(\univ\), we identify the observational equality with the type of equivalences.
\begin{description}[font=\normalfont\scshape]
    \item[Code family.]
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{Code}&\colon\univ\to\univ\to\univ\\
        \fun{Code}(A,B)&\defeq A\simeq B.
    \end{align*}
    
    \item[Base code.]
    We specify the base code \/$c \colon \fun{Code}(A,A)$ as \/$c \defeq \id_A$. This is an abuse of notation  [cf.~Proposition~\ref{prop:equivalence-is-an-equivalence-relation}] for the canonical equivalence
    \[
        \dep{\id_A,(\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}},\dep{\id_A,\fun{refl}})}\colon A\simeq A.
    \]
   
    \item[Encode function.]
    To define
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{encode}&\colon(A\eq\univ B)\to\fun{Code}(A,B),
    \end{align*}
    with $C_A\defeq\fun{Code}(A,\dummy)$, we will use based path induction. Given $X\colon\univ$ and $q\colon A\eq\univ X$, consider the motive
    \[
        D(X,q)\defeq A\to X.
    \]
    To define the depending function
    \[
        \prod_{X\colon\univ}\;\prod_{q\colon A\eq\univ X}A\to X,
    \]
    it suffices to specify $d\colon D(A,\fun{refl}_A)\equiv A\to A$. Then, for $d\defeq\id_A$, we obtain
    \[
        f(p)\defeq\fun{ind}'_{=A}(A,D,\id_A,B,p),
    \]
    for $p\colon A\eq\univ B$.
    
    To further characterize this map, consider the type family $\id_\univ\colon\univ\to\univ$. Given $p\colon A\eq\univ B$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}&\colon(A\eq\univ B)
            \to(A\to B).
    \end{align*}
    We claim that $f(p)\eq{A\to B}\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p)$. To prove this by path induction on~$p$, it suffices to restrict ourselves to the case $B\equiv A$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$. In this case
    \begin{align*}
        \lhs&\equiv f(\fun{refl}_A)\\
            &\equiv\fun{ind}'_{=A}(A,D,\id_A,A,\fun{refl}_A)\\
            &\equiv\id_A,\\[1mm]
        \rhs&\equiv\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{refl}_A)\\
            &\equiv\fun{\id_A}
            &&\text{; Thm.~\ref{thm:transportP}}
    \end{align*}
    
\begin{thm}\label{thm:idtoeqv-def}
    Given\/ $A,B\colon\univ$, the encode function defined above is propositionally equal to the function
    \begin{align}\label{eq:idtoeqv}
        \fun{idtoeqv}&\colon(A\eq\univ B)\to(A\simeq B)
    \intertext{induced by}
        p&\mapsto\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p),\nonumber
    \end{align}
    where for each path\/ $p$, the quasi-inverse of the map\/ $\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p)$ is given by\/ $\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p^{-1})$, with right and left homotopies respectively provided by
    \[
        \fun{transportinv}_r^{\id_\univ}(p)
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        \fun{transportinv}_l^{\id_\univ}(p).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    For a given path\/ $p\colon A\eq\univ B$, the verification that\/ $\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p^{-1})$ acts as a quasi-inverse for\/ $\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p)$ via the stated homotopies follows directly from Lemma~\ref{lem:transportinv}.
\end{proof}
    
    \begin{defn}
        The theorem allows us to take $\fun{idtoeqv}$ as our encode function.
    \end{defn}
    
    
    \item[Decode function.] To define the decoding map we need to add the following
    
    \textbf{Axiom.} [Univalence] For any $A,B\colon\univ$, the function \eqref{eq:idtoeqv} is an equivalence.
    
    \begin{rem}
        The Univalence Axiom asserts that $\fun{idtoeqv}$ is an equivalence. In particular, $(A\eq\univ B)\simeq(A\simeq B)$. Moreover, it allows us to establish the following rules
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item the induction principle:
            \[
                \fun{ua}\colon(A\simeq B)\to(A\eq\univ B),
            \]
            \item the elimination rule:
            \[
                \fun{idtoeqv}\colon
                    (A\eq\univ B)\to(A\simeq B),
            \]
            \item the propositional computation rule: for $f\colon A\simeq B$ and $x\colon A$,
            \[
                \fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ua}(f))(x)\eq Bf(x),
            \]
            \item the propositional uniqueness principle: for $p\colon A\eq\univ B$,
            \[
                \fun{ua}(\fun{idtoeqv}(p))\eq{A\eq\univ B}p.
            \]
        \end{enumerate}
    \end{rem}
\end{description}


\textbf{Extended framework.}
The groupoid structure corresponds to the groupoid structure of equivalences:
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}&\colon(A\simeq B)\to(B\simeq A)\\
    \fun{inv}(e)&\defeq e^{-1}
\intertext{and}
    \ect&\colon(A\simeq B)\to(B\simeq C)\to(A\simeq C)\\
    e\ect e'&\defeq e'\circ e,
\end{align*}
with inverse and composition is defined in Proposition~\ref{prop:equivalence-is-an-equivalence-relation}.

The first unit laws holds definitionally
\begin{align*}
    \fun{inv}(c)
        &\equiv(\id_A,(\id_A,\fun{refl},\id_A,\fun{refl}))^{-1}\\
        &\equiv(\id_A,(\id_A,\fun{refl},\id_A,\fun{refl}))\\
        &\equiv c
    \intertext{and the second propositionally, by Corollary~\ref{cor:propositional-qinv-composition-with-id}}
    c\ect d
        &\equiv(\id_A,(\id_A,\fun{refl},\id_A,\fun{refl}))\circ d\\
        &\eq{A\simeq B}d.
\end{align*}

\begin{prop}\ua\label{prop:transport-ua-precomp}
    Let\/ $E,A,B\colon\univ$ be types. Then, given an equivalence $e \colon E\simeq A$ and a function\/ $g\colon E\to B$, we have
    \[
        \fun{transport}^{\lambda X.\,(X\to B)}(\fun{ua}(e),g)
            \sim g \circ e^{-1}.
    \]
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    Let $p\defeq\fun{ua}(e)$. Then $p\colon E\eq\univ A$ and $p^{-1}\eq{A\eq\univ E}\fun{ua}(e^{-1})$. By Lemma~\ref{lem:transport^A->B} applied to the identity type family $\id_\univ$ and the constant $\lambda X.\,B$, given $a\colon A$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^{\lambda X.\,(X\to B)}
            (p,g)(a)
            &\eq{B}
                \fun{transport}^{\lambda X.\,B}
                \bigl(
                    p,
                    g(
                        \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}
                        (
                            p^{-1},a
                        )
                    )
                \bigr)\\
            &\stackrel{\text{(1)}\hphantom{_B}}{\eq{B}}g
                (
                    \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p^{-1},a)
                )\\
            &\stackrel{\text{(2)}\hphantom{_B}}{\eq{B}}g(\fun{idtoeqv}(p^{-1})(a))\\
            &\eq{B}g(\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ua}(e^{-1}))(a))\\
            &\equiv g(e^{-1}(a)),
    \end{align*}
    \begin{enumerate}[(1)]
        \item holds because the transport of a constant family is the identity map [cf.~Exercise~\ref{exr:constant-fibration}].
        \item follows from Theorem~\ref{thm:idtoeqv-def}. \qedhere
    \end{enumerate}
\end{proof}

\begin{prop}\label{prop:id-transport-and-ap}
    Let\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ be a type family and\/ $x,y\colon A$. Given a path\/ $p\colon x\eq{A}y$ and an element\/ $u\colon B(x)$, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^B(p,u)
            &\eq{B(y)}\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{ap}_B(p),u) \\
            &\equiv\pi_1
                \bigl(
                    \fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ap}_B(p))
                \bigr)(u),
    \end{align*}
    where
    \[
        \pi_1\colon
            \Bigl(
                \sum_{f\colon B(x)\to B(y)}\fun{isequiv}(f)
            \Bigr)
            \to\bigl(B(x)\to B(y)\bigr)
    \]
    is the first projection of the $\Sigma$-type.\footnote{Notation~\ref{ntn:abuse-equivalence} is sometimes used to identify $\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ap}_B(p))\colon B(x)\simeq B(y)$ with its projection onto $B(x)\to B(y)$.}
\end{prop}

\begin{proof}
    The types of both sides of the first equality are:
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^B(p)\colon B(x)\to B(y),\;u\colon B(x)
        &\implies\fun{transport}^B(p,u)\colon B(y)\\
        \fun{ap}_B(p)\colon B(x)\to B(y),\;u\colon B(x)
        &\implies\fun{transport}^{\id\univ}(\fun{ap}_B(p),u)
            \colon B(y),
    \end{align*}
    and the equality follows by path induction on $p$, since both sides reduce to $u$ when $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$.
\end{proof}


\begin{rem}
    The first equality of Proposition~\ref{prop:id-transport-and-ap} is a direct consequence of Lemma~\ref{lem:post-composition-transport}, for the case $f\equiv B$ and $P\equiv\id_\univ$.

    Conversely, Lemma~\ref{lem:post-composition-transport} can be derived from the proposition applying it twice in different contexts:
        \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^{P\circ f}(p,u) 
            &\eq{P(f(y))} \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}
            (\fun{ap}_{P\circ f}(p),u)
                &&;\ B\equiv P\circ f,\; P\equiv\id_\univ\\
            &\eq{P(f(y))} \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{ap}_P(\fun{ap}_f(p)), u)
                &&;\ \fun{ap}_{P\circ f}\eq{} \fun{ap}_P\circ\fun{ap}_f\\
            &\eq{P(f(y))} \fun{transport}^P(\fun{ap}_f(p),u)
                &&;\ B\equiv P,\; p\equiv\fun{ap}_f(p).
    \end{align*}
    Here is an illustration. Compare with Remark~\ref{rem:Pf-diagram}.
    \[
        \hspace{2cm}
        \begin{tikzpicture}[scale=1.0,>=stealth,font=\small]
            \draw[thick,name path=A]
                (0.5,0) node[left] {$A$} to[out=10,in=170] (6,0);
                
            \draw[thick,name path=U]
                (0.5,2.0) node[left] {$\univ$} to[out=10,in=170] (6,2.0);
                
            \draw[gray,thin,name path=Bx]
                (1,2) -- (1,5.5)
                node[above,black] {$B(x)$};
                
            \draw[gray,thin,name path=By]
                (5,2) -- (5,5.5)
                node[above,black] {$B(y)$};
                
            \path[name path=Lx] (1,-0.5) -- (1,1);
            \path[name path=Ly] (5,-0.5) -- (5,1);
            
            \path [name intersections={of=A and Lx,by=x}];
            \fill (x) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$x$};
            
            \path [name intersections={of=A and Ly,by=y}];
            \fill (y) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$y$};
            
            \path [name intersections={of=U and Bx,by=ptBx}];
            \fill (ptBx) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$B(x)$};
            
            \path [name intersections={of=U and By,by=ptBy}];
            \fill (ptBy) circle (1.5pt) node[below right] {$B(y)$};
            
            \draw[-latex,gray,dashed] 
                (x) -- node[midway,left,black] {$B$} (ptBx);
            \draw[-latex,gray,dashed] 
                (y) -- node[midway,right,black] {$B$} (ptBy);
                
            \draw[-latex]
                (x) to[out=30,in=150]
                node[midway,above] {$p$} (y);
                
            \draw[-latex]
                (ptBx) to[out=30,in=150]
                node[midway,above] {$\fun{ap}_B(p)$} (ptBy);
                
            \coordinate (u) at (1,3.7);
            \fill (u) circle (1.5pt) node[left] {$u$};

            \coordinate (v) at (5, 4);
            \fill (v) circle (1.5pt) node[right] {$(y,p_*(u))$};

            \draw[dashed,teal] (u) to[out=15,in=170]
                node[midway,above,black] {$\fun{lift}(u,p)$} (v);
            
            \coordinate (tu) at (5, 5);
            \fill (tu) circle (1.5pt) node[right,align=left] 
                {$\fun{transport}^B(p,u)$\\
                \quad$\eq{B(y)}\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{ap}_B(p),u)$};

            \draw[-latex,teal,thick] (v) -- (tu);
                
            \draw[-latex,orange,thick]
                (u) to[out=35,in=165] (tu);
        \end{tikzpicture}
    \]
\end{rem}

\section*{Partial Summary}
Before proceeding with other types, let us recap what we have seen so far.
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.5}
    \begin{tabular}{llc}
        \hline\small
        \textbf{Type}
            &\small\textbf{Interface}
            &\small\textbf{Extensional Equality} \\
        \hline
        \small$A\times B$
            &\small $\pi_1$ and $\pi_2$
            &\small $(\pi_1(u)=\pi_1(v))\times(\pi_2(u)=\pi_2(v))$\\
        \small$\displaystyle\prod_{x\colon A}B(x)$
            &\small Application: $f(x)$
            &\small$\displaystyle\prod_{x\colon A}f(x)=g(x)$\\
        \small$\displaystyle\sum_{x\colon A}B(x)$
            &\small$\pi_1$ and $\pi_2$
            &\small$\displaystyle\sum_{p\colon\pi_1(u)=\pi_1(v)}
                \!\!\!\!\!p_*\pi_2(u)=\pi_2(v)$
            \\
        \small$\fun1$
            &\small None
            &\small$x=\fun\star$\\
        \small$\univ$
            &\small Equivalences
            &\small $A\simeq B$\\
        \hline
    \end{tabular}
\end{center}

\section{Equality in Identity Types}

The Observational Equality Framework \ref{observational-framework} aims to implement \textsl{structural decomposition}: it characterizes the identity type of a compound type (such as $\Sigma$-types, Cartesian products, or $\Pi$-types) in terms of the identity types of its components. 

The framework cannot be applied to an identity type itself. An identity type $a\eq Aa'$ presents no structural components to unpack. The type of paths between paths, $p\eq{a\eq Aa'}q$, is instead part of the higher homotopy structure of the base type $A$. 

Even if we fix a generic base type $A$, there is no universal formula to characterize its $2$-paths. The complexity of these iterated identity types is precisely what gives the theory its rich homotopical character. We can only provide an observational characterization of $p\eq{a\eq Aa'}q$ when $A$ is instantiated with a concrete type constructor (such as $B\times C$ or $\univ$). In those cases, we simply re-apply the structural theorems already established for those specific types.

Nevertheless, we can use the Observational Equality Framework \ref{observational-framework} to make the following

\begin{rem}\label{rem:characterization-of-2-paths}
    Suppose that, for some type $A$, we have a full characterization of $a \eq A a'$ given by the equivalence
    \[
        \fun{encode}\colon(a\eq A a')\simeq\fun{Code}(a,a').
    \]
    Then, by Theorem~\ref{thm:f-equiv-implies-apf-equiv}, the function application
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{\fun{encode}}\colon(p\eq{a\eq A a'}q)\to(\fun{encode}(p)\eq{\fun{Code}(a,a')}\fun{encode}(q))
    \]
    is also an equivalence. Therefore, the equality $p\eq{a\eq Aa'}q$ between paths $p,q\colon a\eq Aa'$ is fully characterized by the equality of their encoded representations in the structurally simpler type $\fun{Code}(a,a')$.


Before working the details of this observation in concrete cases, we need two results.

\begin{lem} {\upshape [Transport in Identity Types]}
    \label{lem:transport-in-identity-types}
    Let\/ $A$ and\/ $B$ be types, and\/ $f,g\colon A\to B$ functions. Consider the type family\/ $P(x)\defeq f(x)\eq B g(x)$. Then, for any path\/ $\gamma\colon x\eq A y$ and any path\/ $q\colon P(x)$, the transport of\/ $q$ along\/ $\gamma$ is given by
    \[
        \fun{transport}^P(\gamma,q)\eq{P(y)}
        \fun{ap}_f(\gamma)^{-1}\ct q\ct\fun{ap}_g(\gamma).
    \]
\end{lem}

\begin{proof}
    The \lhs of the equality inhabits $P(y)$. This is also the case with the \rhs:
    \[
        \explain[f(y)\eq Bf(x)]{\fun{ap}_f(\gamma)^{-1}}
        \ct\explain[f(x)\eq Bg(x)]{q\vphantom{{}_g(}}
        \ct\explain[g(x)\eq Bg(y)]{\fun{ap}_g(\gamma)}\colon P(y).
    \]    
    Therefore, we can apply path induction on $\gamma$. It suffices to assume that $y\equiv x$ and $\gamma\equiv\fun{refl}_x$.
    \begin{align*}
        \lhs&\equiv\fun{transport}^P(\fun{refl}_x,q)\\
            &\equiv q,\\[1mm]
        \rhs&\equiv\fun{ap}_f(\fun{refl}_x)^{-1}
            \ct q\ct\fun{ap}_g(\fun{refl}_x)\\
            &\equiv\fun{refl}_{f(x)}\ct q\ct\fun{refl}_{g(x)}\\
            &\eq{P(x)}q.
    \end{align*}
    Since $\fun{refl}_q$ inhabits the identity type, the proof is complete.
\end{proof}

\begin{thm}\label{thm:transport-in-Sigma-identity}
    Let\/ $A$ be a type and\/ $B\colon A\to\univ$ a type family. For any two points\/ $\omega,\omega'\colon\Sigma_AB$ and any two paths\/ $p,q\colon\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega'$, let
    \[
        a\defeq\pi_1(\omega),\quad u\defeq\pi_2(\omega)
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        a'\defeq\pi_1(\omega'),\quad u'\defeq\pi_2(\omega').
    \]
    Then, there is an equivalence
    \[
        \varepsilon\colon
        (p\eq{\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega'}q)
            \simeq
            \sum_{\alpha\colon p_1\eq{}q_1}
                \fun{transport}^P(\alpha, p_2)\eq{P(q_1)} q_2,
    \]
    where
    \[
        p_1\defeq\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(p),
            \quad p_2\defeq\fun{apd}_{\pi_2}(p)
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        q_1\defeq\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(q),
        \quad q_2\defeq\fun{apd}_{\pi_2}(q),
    \]
    and the type family\/ $P\colon(a\eq Aa')\to\univ$ for\/ $r\colon a\eq Aa'$ is defined as
    \[
        P(r)\defeq T(r)\eq{B(a')}u',
        \quad\text{with}\quad
        T(r)\defeq\fun{transport}^B(r,u).
    \]
\end{thm}

\begin{proof}
    Let us denote the total space of the encoded identity type as
    \[
        E\defeq\sum_{r\colon a\eq Aa'}P(r).
    \]
    Section \ref{equality-in-Sigma-types}~\nameref{equality-in-Sigma-types} establishes an equivalence
    \[
        \fun{encode}\colon(\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega')
            \xrightarrow\simeq E.
    \]
    Theorem~\ref{thm:f-equiv-implies-apf-equiv} applied to $\fun{encode}$ yields an equivalence:
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{\fun{encode}}\colon(p\eq{\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega'}q)
        \xrightarrow\simeq
        (\fun{encode}(p)\eq E\fun{encode}(q)),
    \]
    where $\fun{encode}(p)\equiv\dep{p_1,p_2}$ and $\fun{encode}(q)\equiv\dep{q_1,q_2}$. Hence:
    \[
        \fun{ap}_{\fun{encode}}\colon
            (p\eq{\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega'}q)
            \xrightarrow\simeq
            (\dep{p_1,p_2}\eq E\dep{q_1,q_2}).
    \]
    Applying the characterization of equality in $\Sigma$-types a second time, this time to the $\Sigma$-type $E$ itself, we obtain a second encoding:
    \[
        \fun{enc}\colon\bigl(\dep{p_1, p_2}
        \eq E\dep{q_1,q_2}\bigr)
        \simeq
        \!\!\!
        \sum_{\alpha\colon p_1\eq{a\eq Aa'}q_1}
        \!\!\!\fun{transport}^P(\alpha,p_2)\eq{P(q_1)}q_2.
    \]
    Composing $\fun{ap}_{\fun{encode}}$ with $\fun{enc}$ yields the desired equivalence:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=2cm]
            p\eq{\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega'}q
                    \arrow[r,"\fun{ap}_{\fun{encode}}"]
                    \arrow[rd,dashed,"\varepsilon"']
                &\dep{p_1,p_2}\eq E\dep{q_1,q_2}
                    \arrow[d,"\fun{enc}"]\\
                &{\displaystyle\sum_{\alpha\colon p_1\eq{}q_1}
                    \fun{transport}^P(\alpha,p_2)\eq{P(q_1)}q_2}
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
\end{proof}

    Here are examples of Remark~\ref{rem:characterization-of-2-paths}.
    \begin{enumerate}[a), font=\upshape]
        \item \textbf{Product Types:} Consider two paths $p,q\colon\omega\eq{A\times B}\omega'$ in the product type $A\times B$. Since the identity type $\omega\eq{A\times B}\omega'$ is equivalent to the type of pairs of paths $(\pi_1(\omega)\eq A\pi_1(\omega'))\times(\pi_2(\omega)\eq B\pi_2(\omega'))$, the identity type $p\eq{\omega\eq{A\times B}\omega'}q$ is equivalent to the product of their respective identity types. Thus, an identity between $p$ and $q$ is equivalent to a pair of identities:
        \begin{align*}
            \fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(p)
            &\eq{\pi_1(\omega)
            \eq A\pi_1(\omega')}\fun{ap}_{\pi_1}(q)
            \intertext{and}
            \fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(p)
            &\eq{\pi_2(\omega)\eq B\pi_2(\omega')}\fun{ap}_{\pi_2}(q).
        \end{align*}

        \item \textbf{Dependent Pair Types:} For a dependent pair type $\Sigma_AB$, consider two paths $p,q\colon\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega'$. Let us denote the projections of the endpoints as 
        \begin{alignat*}2
            a&\defeq\pi_1(\omega),\quad
            u&\defeq\pi_2(\omega)
            \intertext{and}
            a'&\defeq\pi_1(\omega'),
            \quad u'&\defeq\pi_2(\omega').
        \end{alignat*}
        For any path $r\colon a\eq Aa'$, let us define the transport function
        \[
            T(r)\defeq\fun{transport}^B(r,u).
        \]
        The projected paths of the endpoints are then given by
        \begin{align*}
            p_1,q_1&\colon a\eq Aa'\\
            p_2&\colon T(p_1)\eq{B(a')}u',\\
            q_2&\colon T(q_1)\eq{B(a')}u'.
        \end{align*}
        As Theorem~\ref{thm:transport-in-Sigma-identity} establishes, calculating the equality between paths $p$ and $q$ reduces to providing a pair of identities $(\alpha, \beta)$, where
        \begin{align*}
            \alpha&\colon p_1\eq{a\eq Aa'}q_1\\
            %\quad\text{and}\quad
            \beta&\colon\fun{transport}^P(\alpha, p_2)\eq{P(q_1)}q_2,
        \end{align*}
        with the identity family
        \begin{align*}
            P&\colon a\eq Aa'\to\univ\\
            P(r)&\defeq T(r)\eq{B(a')}u'.
        \end{align*}
        To understand the geometric meaning of $\beta$, we can compute the action of transport in the family $P$. 
        
        Applying Lemma~\ref{lem:transport-in-identity-types} to our case with
        \begin{align*}
            x&\defeq p_1\\
            y&\defeq q_1\\
            \gamma&\defeq\alpha\colon p_1\eq{}q_1\\
            q&\defeq p_2\colon T(p_1)\eq{}u'\\
            f&\defeq T\colon(a\eq Aa')\to B(a')\\
            g&\defeq r\mapsto u'
        \intertext{yields}
            \fun{transport}^P(\alpha,p_2)
            &\eq{P(q_1)}\fun{ap}_T(\alpha)^{-1}\ct p_2\ct\fun{ap}_{r\mapsto u'}(\alpha)\\
            &\eq{P(q_1)}\fun{ap}_T(\alpha)^{-1}\ct p_2\ct\fun{refl}_{u'}
                &&\text{; Lem.~\ref{lem:ap-const}}\\
            &\eq{P(q_1)}\fun{ap}_T(\alpha)^{-1}\ct p_2.
        \end{align*}
        Concatenating the inverse of this computation with $\beta$ gives
        \[
            \beta'\colon\fun{ap}_T(\alpha)^{-1}\ct p_2 \eq{P(q_1)} q_2.
        \]
        Redefining $\beta'$ as $\fun{ap}_T(\alpha)\ct\beta'$ yields
        \[
            \beta'\colon p_2 \eq{P(q_1)} \fun{ap}_T(\alpha)\ct q_2.
        \]
        Since the composition $(\alpha,\beta)\mapsto(\alpha,\beta')$ is an equivalence, we obtain as result a decomposition of the $2$-path $p\eq{\omega\eq{\Sigma_AB}\omega'}q$ into a $2$-path $\alpha$ in the base type $A$ and a $2$-path $\beta'$ in the target fiber $B(a')$, mirroring the decomposition of $1$-paths in the total space.

        The following picture illustrates this geometric construction. The direct path $p_2$ and the concatenated indirect path $\fun{ap}_T(\alpha)\ct q_2$ form a triangle within the target fiber, and $\beta'$ acts as the homotopy between them.
        \[
            \begin{tikzpicture}[font=\small]
                % Base space A
                \draw[thick, fill=gray!10] (0, 0) ellipse (4.5cm and 0.7cm);
                \node at (-3.8, 0) {$A$};
                
                % Points in base
                \node[circle, fill, inner sep=1.5pt, label=left:{$a$}] (x) at (-2.5, 0) {};
                \node[circle, fill, inner sep=1.5pt, label=right:{$a'$}] (y) at (2.5, 0) {};
                
                % Paths p_1, q_1 in base
                \draw[-latex, thick] (x) to[bend left=11] node[pos=0.3, above] {$p_1$} coordinate[pos=0.3] (p_pos) (y);
                \draw[-latex, thick] (x) to[bend right=11] node[pos=0.73, below] {$q_1$} coordinate[pos=0.7] (q_pos) (y);
                \draw[-latex, double, shorten >=10pt, shorten <=10pt] (p_pos) -- node[above right, inner sep=1pt] {$\alpha$} (q_pos);
            
                % Fibers
                \draw[thick, dashed] (x) -- ++(0, 5.5) node[above] {$B(a)$};
                \draw[thick, dashed] (y) -- ++(0, 5.5) node[above] {$B(a')$};
            
                % Point in source fiber
                \node[circle, fill, inner sep=1.5pt, label=left:{$u$}] (u_node) at (-2.5, 2.5) {};
            
                % Points in target fiber
                \node[circle, fill, inner sep=1.5pt, label=right:{$u'$}] (v_node) at (2.5, 1) {};
                \node[circle, fill, inner sep=1.5pt, label=right:{$T(p_1)$}] (tp) at (2.5, 4.5) {};
                \node[circle, fill, inner sep=1.5pt, label=right:{$T(q_1)$}] (tq) at (2.5, 2.8) {};
            
                % Transport paths mapping 
                \draw[-latex, dashed, gray] (u_node) to[bend left=15] node[above, sloped] {\small transport along\/ $p_1$} (tp);
                \draw[-latex, dashed, gray] (u_node) to[bend right=10] node[below, sloped] {\small transport along\/ $q_1$} (tq);
            
                % Path alpha's effect in the target fiber B(a')
                \draw[-latex, thick] (tp) to node[right] {$\fun{ap}_T(\alpha)$} (tq);
            
                % Paths p_2, q_2
                \draw[-latex, thick] (tp) to[bend right=60] node[pos=0.35,left] {$p_2$} coordinate[pos=0.4] (p2_pos) (v_node);
                \draw[-latex, thick] (tq) to node[right] {$q_2$} coordinate[pos=0.5] (q2_pos) (v_node);
                
                % The double arrow for beta'
                \draw[-latex, double, shorten >=4pt, shorten <=4pt] (p2_pos) -- node[xshift=2pt,yshift=8pt] {$\beta'$} (tq);
            \end{tikzpicture}
        \]
            
        \item \textbf{Function Types:} For a dependent function type\/ $\Gamma\defeq\prod_{x\colon A}B(x)$, consider two paths $p,q\colon f\eq\Gamma g$. By function extensionality, the identity type $f\eq\Gamma g$ is equivalent to the homotopy type $\prod_{x\colon A}f(x)\eq{B(x)}g(x)$ via the function $\fun{happly}$. Therefore, an identity $p\eq{f\eq\Gamma g}q$ is equivalent to a second-order homotopy between their applications:
        \[
            \prod_{x\colon A}\fun{happly}(p)(x)\eq{f(x)\eq{B(x)}g(x)}\fun{happly}(q)(x).
        \]

        
    \end{enumerate}
\end{rem}


\subsection*{Transport in Identity Families}

When the Observational Equality Framework encodes a path, it usually generates a type containing the transport operator. For instance, when encoding an equality in dependent pairs, the second coordinate is a $2$-path of type $\fun{transport}^P(\alpha,p_2)\eq{} q_2$. This expression is ``opaque'' because $\fun{transport}$ is a primitive. It asserts that a path is moved between fibers to match types, but it does not specify what the resulting path looks like in terms of simpler operations.

To make sense of these abstract $2$-paths, we must evaluate how paths are transported within families of the form\/ $E(x) \defeq f(x) \eq{} g(x)$.

The following results establish computational rules for these transport operations. Beginning with simple identity families where one or both endpoints are fixed, we then consider families defined by functions into a fixed codomain, and finally address the general case of dependent functions. These rules provide the computational engine that allows us to translate abstract transport terms into concrete path concatenations.

\begin{lem}\label{lem:path-equivalences}
    Let\/ $A$ be a type, let\/ $a, x_1, x_2\colon A$, and consider a path\/ $p\colon x_1\eq{A}x_2$. Then, we have the following:
    \begin{enumerate}[a), font=\upshape]
        \item Let\/ $E_1\colon A\to\univ$ be the type family\/ $E_1(x)\defeq a\eq{A}x$. Then,
        \begin{enumerate}[i),font=\upshape]
