                    \arrow[rd,"r_D",phantom,description]
                    \arrow[rdd,"u"',bend right]
                    \arrow[rrrd,"v",bend left]
                    \arrow[rrd,"h_R"',bend left,dashed]\\
                &A
                    \arrow[r,"\pi_C"]
                    \arrow[d,"\pi_B"']
                &C
                    \arrow[r,"\pi_E"]
                    \arrow[d,"\pi_D"']
                    \arrow[rd,
                        "\lrcorner",
                        phantom,
                        very near start]
                &E
                    \arrow[d,"g_E"]\\
                &B
                    \arrow[r,"g_B"']
                &D
                    \arrow[r,"g_D"']
                &F
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    We define
    \[
        \psi(\dep{(u,v),q})\defeq\dep{(u,h_R),r_D^{-1}}.
    \]
    For the backward function, we set
    \begin{align*}
        \phi\colon\Sigma_L(X)&\to\Sigma(X)\\
        \dep{(u,k),r}&\mapsto
            \dep{
                (u,\pi_E\circ k),
                (g_D\lwct r)\ct(p_R\rwct k)
            },
    \end{align*}
    where $r\colon g_B\circ u\eq{X\to D}\pi_D\circ k$.
    
    We claim that $\psi$ and $\phi$ are quasi-inverses.
    
    Using $r^{-1}$ for the first coordinate of the pair and $\fun{refl}_{\pi_E\circ k}$ for the second, we obtain
    \begin{align*}
        \dep{
            (\pi_D\circ k,\pi_E\circ k),
            p_R\rwct k
        }
        &\eq{\Sigma_R(X)}
        \dep{
            (g_B\circ u,\pi_E\circ k),
            \fun{transport}^{W_R}(\gamma,p_R\rwct k)
        },
    \end{align*}
    where
    \[
        \gamma\defeq\fun{pair}^=(r^{-1},\fun{refl}_{\pi_E\circ k}).
    \]
    Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-in-commutative-squares} yields:
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^{W_R}&\bigl(\gamma, p_R\rwct k\bigr)\\
            &\eq{W_R(g_B\circ u,\pi_E\circ k)}
                (g_D\lwct r^{-1})^{-1}
                \ct(p_R\rwct k)
                \ct(g_E\lwct\fun{refl}_{\pi_E\circ k})\\
            &\eq{W_R(g_B\circ u,\pi_E\circ k)}
                (g_D\lwct r)
                \ct(p_R\rwct k),
    \end{align*}
    since $(g_E\lwct\fun{refl}_{\pi_E\circ k})\eq{g_E\circ\pi_E\circ k\eq{X\to F}g_E\circ\pi_E\circ k}\fun{refl}_{g_E\circ\pi_E\circ k}$. Therefore,
    \begin{align*}
        \varphi_R(k)
            &\equiv
                \dep{
                    (\pi_D\circ k,\pi_E\circ k),
                    p_R\rwct k
                }\\
            &\eq{\Sigma_R(X)}
                \dep{
                    (g_B\circ u,\pi_E\circ k),
                    (g_D\lwct r)\ct(p_R\rwct k)
                }.
    \end{align*}
    
    Let us first compute the composition $\psi\circ\phi$. Let $s\defeq\phi(\dep{(u,k),r})$. By definition,
    \begin{align*}
        \psi(s)&\equiv\psi
            \bigl(\dep{
                (u,\pi_E\circ k),
                (g_D\lwct r)\ct(p_R\rwct k)
            }\bigr)\\
        &\equiv\dep{(u,h_R),r_D^{-1}},
    \end{align*}
    where $h_R$ is defined by the equation
    \[
        e_1\colon\varphi_R(h_R)
        \eq{\Sigma_R(X)}
        \dep{
            (g_B\circ u,\pi_E\circ k),
            (g_D\lwct r)\ct(p_R\rwct k)
        },
    \]
    and $r_D\colon\pi_D\circ h_R\eq{}g_B\circ u$ is extracted from the first component of the base path of~$e_1$.

    From our previous derivation, we also have an explicit equality
    \[
        e_2\colon\varphi_R(k)
        \eq{\Sigma_R(X)}
        \dep{
            (g_B\circ u,\pi_E\circ k),
            (g_D\lwct r)\ct(p_R\rwct k)
        },
    \]
    whose base path is $\gamma\defeq\fun{pair}^=(r^{-1},\fun{refl}_{\pi_E\circ k})$.

    Concatenating these paths yields $e_1\ct e_2^{-1}\colon\varphi_R(h_R)\eq{\Sigma_R(X)}\varphi_R(k)$. Because $\varphi_R$ is an equivalence, there is a path $\alpha\colon h_R\eq{X\to C}k$ such that $\varphi_R\lwct\alpha\eq{}e_1\ct e_2^{-1}$.


    Concatenating these paths yields\/ $e_1\ct e_2^{-1}\colon\varphi_R(h_R)\eq{\Sigma_R(X)}\varphi_R(k)$. Because\/ $\varphi_R$ is an equivalence, it is an embedding, which implies there is a unique path\/ $\alpha\colon h_R\eq{X\to C}k$ such that\/ $\varphi_R\lwct\alpha\eq{}e_1\ct e_2^{-1}$.

    By the definition of $\varphi_R$, the base path of $\varphi_R\lwct\alpha$ equals $(\pi_D\lwct\alpha,\pi_E\lwct\alpha)$. Since the first component of $e_1\ct e_2^{-1}$ is $r_D\ct(r^{-1})^{-1}$, we deduce that
    \[
        \pi_D\lwct\alpha\eq{}r_D\ct r.
    \]
    To establish the equality $\dep{(u,h_R),r_D^{-1}}\eq{\Sigma_L(X)}\dep{(u,k),r}$, we use the base path $\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_u,\alpha)$ and compute the transport of $r_D^{-1}$ in the family $W_L$. By Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-in-commutative-squares},
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^{W_L}&\bigl(\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_u,\alpha), r_D^{-1}\bigr)\\
            &\eq{}(g_B\lwct\fun{refl}_u)^{-1}\ct r_D^{-1}\ct(\pi_D\lwct\alpha)\\
            &\eq{}\fun{refl}_{g_B\circ u}^{-1}\ct r_D^{-1}\ct(r_D\ct r)\\
            &\eq{}r.
    \end{align*}

    For the other composition, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \phi(\psi(\dep{(u,v),q)})
            &\equiv\phi(\dep{(u,h_R),r_D^{-1}})\\
            &\equiv
                \dep{
                    (u,\pi_E\circ h_R),
                    (g_D\lwct r_D^{-1})\ct(p_R\rwct h_R)
                }.
    \end{align*}
    By the definition of $h_R$, we have a witness
    \[
        r_E\colon\pi_E\circ h_R\eq{X\to E}v.
    \]
    Thus, with $\varepsilon\defeq\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_u,r_E)$, the question reduces to proving that
    \[
        \fun{transport}^W(
            \varepsilon,(
                g_D\lwct r_D^{-1})\ct(p_R\rwct h_R)
            )\eq{}q.
    \]
    By Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-in-commutative-squares}, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^W&\bigl(
            \varepsilon,
            (g_D\lwct r_D^{-1})\ct(p_R\rwct h_R)
        \bigr)\\
            &\eq{}(g_D\circ g_B\lwct\fun{refl}_u)^{-1}
                \ct\bigl((g_D\lwct r_D^{-1})\ct(p_R\rwct h_R)\bigr)
                \ct(g_E\lwct r_E)\\
            &\eq{}\fun{refl}_{g_D\circ g_B\circ u}^{-1}
                \ct(g_D\lwct r_D^{-1})\ct(p_R\rwct h_R)
                \ct(g_E\lwct r_E)\\
            &\eq{}(g_D\lwct r_D^{-1})\ct(p_R\rwct h_R)\ct(g_E\lwct r_E).
    \end{align*}
    By the definition of $h_R\defeq\varphi_R^{-1}((g_B\circ u,v),q)$, we have
    \[
        \varphi_R(h_R)\eq{\Sigma_R(X)}\dep{(g_B\circ u,v),q}
    \]
    and
    \[
        r_D\colon\pi_D\circ h_R\eq{X\to D}g_B\circ u.
    \]
    Therefore,
    \[
        q\eq{}\fun{transport}^{W_R}
            \bigl(
                \fun{pair}^=(r_D,r_E),p_R\rwct h_R
            \bigr).
    \]
    Using Proposition~\ref{prop:transport-in-commutative-squares} again, we obtain
    \[
        q\eq{}(g_D\lwct r_D)^{-1}\ct(p_R\rwct h_R)\ct(g_E\lwct r_E),
    \]
    as desired.

\end{solution}

\begin{exr}\fe\label{exr:2-simeq-2-simeq-2}
    Show that\/ $(\fun2\simeq\fun2)\simeq\fun2$.
\end{exr}

\begin{solution}
    We will need the following lemma:

    \textbf{Lemma.}\quad\textit{There is a function $\fun{neq}\colon(1_{\fun2}\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2})\to\fun0$.}

    \textsc{Proof:}
        Let $P\colon\fun2\to\univ$ be the type family defined by $P(1_{\fun2})\defeq\fun1$ and $P(0_{\fun2})\defeq\fun0$. Then, we define
        \[
            \fun{neq}\defeq\lambda x\colon1_{\fun2}\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2}.\,
                \fun{transport}^P(x,\fun\star).
        \]
        \localqed
    
    By \nref{lpar:exactly-two-booleans}, there is a witness
    \[
        \varepsilon\colon\prod_{x\colon\fun2}
            (x\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2})+(x\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}).
    \]
    In particular,
    \[
        \varepsilon(f(1_{\fun2}))\colon
            (f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2})
            +(f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}).
    \]
    Fix $f\colon\fun2\simeq\fun2$. Suppose that $f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}$, and let $p$ witness this identity. We want to prove that $f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2}$. Consider the diagram
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=2cm]
            f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2}
                    \arrow[rd,"\id"]
                    \arrow[d,"\fun{inl}"']\\
            (f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2})+(f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2})
                    \arrow[r,"\gamma_p",near start,dashed]
                &f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2}\\
            f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}
                    \arrow[ru,"g"']
                    \arrow[u,"\fun{inr}"]
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    where $g$ is defined as follows. Given $r\colon f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}$, we have
    \[
        p\ct r^{-1}\colon f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}f(1_{\fun2}).
    \]
    Hence, $\fun{ap}_{f^{-1}}(p\ct r^{-1})\colon0_{\fun2}\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}$, and we can use the lemma to set
    \[
        g(r)\defeq\fun{rec}_{\fun0}
            \bigl(
                f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2},
                \fun{neq}(\fun{ap}_{f^{-1}}(p\ct r^{-1}))
            \bigr).
    \]
    As the diagram shows, we obtain
    \[
        \gamma_p\defeq
        \fun{rec}_+\bigl(f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2},\id,g\bigr).
    \]
    It follows that
    \[
        \gamma_p(\varepsilon(f(1_{\fun2})))
            \colon f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2},
    \]
    which constructs a function 
    \begin{align*}
        \bigl(\lambda p.\,\gamma_p(\varepsilon(f(1_{\fun2})))\bigr)
        \colon
        \bigl(f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}\bigr)
        \to
        \bigl(f(1_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2}\bigr).        
    \end{align*}
    Since $\fun{not}$\footnote{See Exercise~\ref{exr:not}.} is characterized by its evaluation at $0_{\fun2}$ and $1_{\fun2}$, the function extensionality axiom yields a function
    \[
        (f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2})
            \to(f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\fun{not}).
    \]
    A similar argument yields a function
    \[
        (f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2})
            \to(f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\id).
    \]
    These functions combine to construct a map
    \[
        (f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2})
        +
        (f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2})
        \to
        (f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\id)
        +
        (f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\fun{not}).
    \]
    Since
    \[
        \varepsilon(f(0_{\fun2}))\colon
            (f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}0_{\fun2})
            +(f(0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}),
    \]
    we deduce the existence of a dependent function
    \[
        \phi\colon\prod_{f\colon\fun2\simeq\fun2}
            (f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\id)
            +
            (f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\fun{not}).
    \]
    Let us now define $\psi_f$ as illustrated in the diagram:
    \[
        \begin{tikzcd}[column sep=2cm]
            f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\id
                    \arrow[d,"\fun{inl}"']
                    \arrow[rd,"p\mapsto1_{\fun2}"]\\
            (f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\id)+(f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\fun{not})
                    \arrow[r,"\psi_f",near start]
                &\fun2\\
            f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\fun{not}
                    \arrow[u,"\fun{inr}"]
                    \arrow[ru,"q\mapsto0_{\fun2}"']
        \end{tikzcd}
    \]
    We can define the functions $\alpha$ and $\beta$ as follows:
    \begin{align*}
        \alpha&\colon(\fun2\simeq\fun2)\to\fun2,
        &\beta&\colon\fun2\to(\fun2\simeq\fun2),\\
        \alpha(f)&\defeq\psi_f(\phi(f)),
        &\beta(1_{\fun2})&\defeq\id,\\
        &&\beta(0_{\fun2})&\defeq\fun{not}.
    \end{align*}
    In addition,
    \begin{align*}
        \beta(\psi_f(\fun{inl}(p)))
            &\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\beta(1_{\fun2})
            \equiv\id,\\
        \beta(\psi_f(\fun{inr}(q)))
            &\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\beta(0_{\fun2})
            \equiv\fun{not}.
    \end{align*}
    To prove that $\beta(\alpha(f))\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}f$, we need to show that
    \[
        \beta(\psi_f(\phi(f)))\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}f.
    \]
    To do this, we define the motive $P\colon(f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\id)+(f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\fun{not})\to\univ$ as
    \[
        P(x)\defeq\beta(\psi_f(x))\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}f.
    \]
    By the induction principle, the goal reduces to proving the cases for $\fun{inl}$ and $\fun{inr}$. Using the calculations above for $\beta\circ\psi_f$, we obtain the equalities
    \begin{align*}
        P(\fun{inl}(p))&\eq{}(\id\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}f),\\
        P(\fun{inr}(q))&\eq{}(\fun{not}\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}f).
    \end{align*}
    In the first case, $p\colon f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\id$; in the second, $q\colon f\eq{\fun2\simeq\fun2}\fun{not}$. Therefore, their inverses inhabit the respective types:
    \[
        p^{-1}\colon P(\fun{inl}(p))
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        q^{-1}\colon P(\fun{inr}(q)).
    \]
    For the backward composition, observe that
    \begin{align*}
        \alpha(\beta(1_{\fun2}))
            &\equiv\alpha(\id)\\
            &\equiv\psi_\id(\phi(\id))\\
            &\equiv\psi_\id(\fun{inl}(\fun{refl}_\id))\\
            &\equiv1_{\fun2},\\[1mm]
        \alpha(\beta(0_{\fun2}))
            &\equiv\alpha(\fun{not})\\
            &\equiv\psi_{\fun{not}}(\phi(\fun{not}))\\
            &\equiv
                \psi_{\fun{not}}(\fun{inr}(\fun{refl}_{\fun{not}}))\\
            &\equiv0_{\fun2}.
    \end{align*}
\end{solution}

\begin{exr}
    Suppose we add to type theory the equality reflection rule which says that if there is an element\/ $p\colon x=y$, then in fact\/ $x\equiv y$. Prove that for any\/ $p\colon x=x$ we have\/ $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$.
\end{exr}

\begin{solution}
    Under the stated conditions, it suffices to prove that if $p\colon x\eq{}x$, then $p\eq{}\fun{refl}_x$. In other words, we have to prove that the type
    \[
        \prod_{x\colon A}\;\prod_{p\colon x\eq{A}x}p\eq{}\fun{refl}_x
    \]
    is inhabited. More generally, we consider the type
    \[
        \prod_{x,y\colon A}\;\prod_{p\colon x\eq{A}y}p\eq{}\fun{refl}_x.
    \]
    By path induction on $p$, we can restrict ourselves to the case where $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$, in which case the goal becomes trivial.
    %
    
\end{solution}

\begin{exr}
    Show that\/ {\upshape Proposition~\ref{prop:id-transport-and-ap}} can be strengthened to
    \[
        \fun{transport}^B(p,\dummy)\eq{B(x)\to B(y)}\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ap}_B(p))
    \]
    without using function extensionality. (In this and other similar cases, the apparently weaker formulation has been chosen for readability and consistency.)
\end{exr}

\begin{solution}
    The implicit assumptions here are that $B\colon A\to\univ$ is a type family, and that $p\colon x\eq{A}y$.

    The \rhs denotes the equivalence $\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ap}_B(p))$ of type $B(x)\simeq B(y)$. By abuse of notation, it is identified with its underlying function $f\colon B(x)\to B(y)$, which computes exactly as $\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{ap}_B(p),\dummy)$.

    Therefore, the goal is to show that the type
    \[
        \fun{transport}^B(p,\dummy)
        \eq{B(x)\to B(y)}
        \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{ap}_B(p),\dummy)
    \]
    is inhabited.

    Since both sides are clearly of the same type $B(x)\to B(y)$, to prove the equality we can apply path induction on $p$. Hence, it suffices to consider the case $y\equiv x$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In this case, we have
    \begin{align*}
        \lhs
            &\equiv\fun{transport}^B(\fun{refl}_x,\dummy)\\
            &\equiv\id_{B(x)}.\\[1mm]
        \rhs
            &\equiv\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{refl}_{B(x)},\dummy)\\
            &\equiv\id_{B(x)}.
    \end{align*}
    Thus, both sides are definitionally equal in the base case, meaning $\fun{refl}_{\id_{B(x)}}$ inhabits the goal type. Path induction then yields the equality in the general case.
    %
    
\end{solution}


\begin{exr}${}$\fe\ \ua
    \begin{enumerate}[a),font=\upshape]
        \item Show that if\/ $A\simeq B$ and\/ $A'\simeq B'$, then\/ $(A\times A')\simeq(B\times B')$.
        \item Give two proofs of this fact, one using univalence and one not using it, and show that the two proofs are equal.
        \item Formulate and prove analogous results for the other type formers:\/ $\Sigma$, $\to$, $\Pi$, and\/ $+$.\footnote{Function extensionality is used for $\Pi$-types.}
    \end{enumerate}
\end{exr}

\needspace{2\baselineskip}
\begin{solution}${}$
    \begin{enumerate}[a), font=\upshape]
        \item Let $(f,(\eta,\vartheta))\colon A\simeq B$ and $(g,(\eta',\vartheta'))\colon A'\simeq B'$. Consider the function
        \begin{align*}
            (f\times g)\colon(A\times A')&\to(B\times B')\\
            (a,a')&\mapsto(f(a),g(a')).
        \end{align*}
        Let $f^{-1}$ and $g^{-1}$ be the respective quasi-inverses of $f$ and $g$. Then,
        \begin{align*}
            (f\times g)\circ(f^{-1}\times g^{-1})(b,b')
            &\equiv
            \bigl(
                f(f^{-1}(b)),g(g^{-1}(b'))
            \bigr).
        \end{align*}
        Since $\eta(b)\colon f(f^{-1}(b))\eq{B}b$ and $\eta'(b')\colon g(g^{-1}(b'))\eq{B'}b'$, we define
        \[
            (\eta\wedge\eta')(b,b')
                \defeq\fun{pair}^=\bigl(\eta(b),\eta'(b')\bigr),
        \]
        which provides the first homotopy
        \[
            (\eta\wedge\eta')\colon(f\times g)\circ(f^{-1}\times g^{-1})
                \sim\id_{B\times B'}.
        \]
        By symmetry we obtain
        \[
            (\vartheta\wedge\vartheta')\colon
                (f^{-1}\times g^{-1})\circ(f\times g)
                \sim\id_{A\times A'}.
        \]
        Note that this defines the product of equivalences:
        \begin{equation}\label{eq:eqv-product}
            (f,(\eta,\vartheta))\times(g,(\eta',\vartheta'))
                \defeq
                    \bigl(
                        f\times g,
                        (
                            \eta\wedge\eta',
                            \vartheta\wedge\vartheta'
                        )
                    \bigr).
        \end{equation}

        \item By univalence, we can apply the $\fun{ua}$ function to the equivalences $(f,(\eta,\vartheta))$ and $(g,(\eta',\vartheta'))$ to obtain paths $\phi\colon A\eq{\univ}B$ and $\psi\colon A'\eq{\univ}B'$.

        This transforms the question into proving that $(A\times A')\eq{\univ}(B\times B')$ is inhabited.
    
        By based path induction, first on $\phi$ and then on $\psi$, the goal reduces to the base case where $B\equiv A$ with $\phi\equiv\fun{refl}_A$, and $B'\equiv A'$ with $\psi\equiv\fun{refl}_{A'}$. In this case, the target equality is trivially witnessed by $\fun{refl}_{A\times A'}$.

        Applying $\fun{idtoeqv}$ yields the required equivalence.

        \bigskip
        
        To show that both proofs are the same, we need to be more precise.
        \begin{enumerate}[-]
            \item Fix $B\equiv A$ and $\phi\equiv\fun{refl}_A$. Consider the motive
            \begin{align*}
                E&\colon\prod_{X\colon\univ}(A'\eq{\univ}X)\to\univ\\
                E(X)&\defeq\lambda z.\,
                    (A\times A')\eq\univ(A\times X),
            \end{align*}
            where $E(X)$ is constant (it does not depend on $z$).
            
            For the base case $c_{\fun{refl}}\colon E(A',\fun{refl}_{A'})$, we take reflexivity:
            \[
                c_{\fun{refl}}\defeq\fun{refl}_{A\times A'}.
            \]
            The induction principle yields:
            \[
                \gamma_\psi\defeq
                    \fun{ind}_=(E,\fun{refl}_{A\times A'},B',\psi)
                        \colon(A\times A')\eq\univ(A\times B').
            \]
        
            \item To complete the based induction on $\phi$, we fix $\psi\colon A'\eq{\univ}B'$ and introduce the motive
            \begin{align*}
                F_\psi&\colon\prod_{Y\colon\univ}
                    (A\eq{\univ}Y)\to\univ\\
                F_\psi(Y)&\defeq\lambda z.\,
                    (A\times A')
                    \eq{\univ}(Y\times B'),
            \end{align*}
            where, as before, $F_\psi(Y)$ is constant on $z$. For the base case where $Y\equiv A$, we take $\gamma_\psi$. Thus, we can define
            \[
                \gamma\defeq\fun{ind}_=(F_\psi,\gamma_\psi,B,\phi)
                    \colon(A\times A')\eq{\univ}(B\times B').
            \]
            Consider the goal type
            \begin{align*}
                \prod_{\phi\colon A\eq\univ B}\;
                \prod_{\psi\colon A'\eq\univ B'}
                    \fun{idtoeqv}(\gamma)
                    \eq{}
                    \fun{idtoeqv}(\phi)\times\fun{idtoeqv}(\psi),
            \end{align*}
            where the product on the \rhs is the one defined in \eqref{eq:eqv-product}.
            
            Since both sides of the equation inhabit the type $(A\times A')\simeq(B\times B')$, to prove that it is inhabited we may proceed by path induction on $\phi$ and $\psi$. Thus, we assume $B\equiv A$ with $\phi\equiv\fun{refl}_A$, and $B'\equiv A'$ with $\psi\equiv\fun{refl}_{A'}$. Then,
            \begin{align*}
                \gamma_\psi
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_{A\times A'},\\
                \gamma
                    &\equiv\gamma_\psi
                        \equiv\fun{refl}_{A\times A'},\\
                \fun{idtoeqv}(\gamma)
                    &\equiv(\id_{A\times A'},(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})),\\
                \fun{idtoeqv}(\phi)
                    &\equiv(\id_A,(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})),\\
                \fun{idtoeqv}(\psi)
                    &\equiv(\id_{A'},(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})),\\
                \fun{idtoeqv}(\phi)\times\fun{idtoeqv}(\psi)
                    &\equiv
                        \bigl(
                            \id_A\times\id_{A'},
                            (
                                \fun{refl}\wedge\fun{refl},
                                \fun{refl}\wedge\fun{refl}
                            )
                        \bigr).
            \intertext{Consequently, we need to verify that}
                \id_{A\times A'}
                    &\eq{}\id_A\times\id_{A'}
            \intertext{and}
                \fun{refl}\wedge\fun{refl}
                    &\eq{}\fun{refl}.
            \end{align*}
            The first equality is actually definitional, modulo abuse of notation. The second follows from function extensionality because
            \begin{align*}
                \fun{refl}(x)&\defeq\fun{refl}_x,\\
                (\fun{refl}\wedge\fun{refl})(x,y)
                    &\equiv\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_y)\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_{(x,y)}\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}(x,y).
            \end{align*}       
        \end{enumerate}

        \item We proceed by type former
        \begin{enumerate}
\item[$\Sigma$)] Let\/ $X\colon\univ$ be a type and\/ $A,B\colon X\to\univ$ be type families. Suppose that for each\/ $x\colon X$, we have an equivalence\/ $\dep{f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x)}\colon A(x)\simeq B(x)$. We define the induced function
            \begin{align*}
                f\colon\Bigl(\sum_{x\colon X}A(x)\Bigr)
                    &\to\Bigl(\sum_{x\colon X}B(x)\Bigr)\\
                \dep{x,a}&\mapsto\dep{x,f_x(a)}.
            \end{align*}
            For each\/ $x\colon X$, let\/ $f_x^{-1}\colon B(x)\to A(x)$ denote the quasi-inverse of\/ $f_x$. We define the proposed inverse
            \begin{align*}
                f^{-1}\colon\Bigl(\sum_{x\colon X}B(x)\Bigr)
                    &\to\Bigl(\sum_{x\colon X}A(x)\Bigr)\\
                \dep{x,b}&\mapsto\dep{x,f_x^{-1}(b)}.
            \intertext{Then,}
                f\circ f^{-1}(\dep{x,b})
                    &\equiv f(\dep{x,f_x^{-1}(b)})\\
                    &\equiv\dep{x,f_x(f_x^{-1}(b))}\\
                    &\eq{\Sigma_XB}\dep{x,b}
                    &&\text{(by\/ }\eta_x(b)\text{)}.
            \end{align*}
            By symmetry,\/ $f^{-1}\circ f(\dep{x,a})\eq{\Sigma_XA}\dep{x,a}$. Thus, we can define
            \begin{align*}
                \eta&\colon f\circ f^{-1}\sim\id_{\Sigma_XB}\\
                \eta(\dep{x,b})&\defeq\fun{pair}^=(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\eta_x(b)}),
            \end{align*}
            which provides the required homotopy.
            
            Similarly, we obtain
            \begin{align*}
                \vartheta&\colon f^{-1}\circ f\sim\id_{\Sigma_XA}\\
                \vartheta(\dep{x,a})&\defeq\fun{pair}^=(\dep{\fun{refl}_x,\vartheta_x(a)}).
            \end{align*}
            This construction yields an equivalence over the\/ $\Sigma$-types:
            \begin{equation}\label{eq:eqv-Sigma}
                \sum_{x\colon X}\dep{f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x)}
                    \defeq\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)}.
            \end{equation}
            Using the univalence axiom function $\fun{ua}$, we may transform, for each $x\colon X$, the equivalence $f_x$ into a path $p_x\colon A(x)\eq\univ B(x)$. This allows us to define the homotopy
            \begin{align*}
                \varepsilon&\colon A\sim B\\
                \varepsilon(x)&\defeq p_x.
            \end{align*}
            We obtain $\fun{funext}(\varepsilon)\colon A\eq\univ B$. In particular, using equality~\eqref{eq:happly-is-ap-ev},
            \[
                \fun{funext}(\varepsilon)(x)
                    \eq{A(x)\eq\univ B(x)}\fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(\varepsilon))(x)
                    \equiv\varepsilon(x)
                    \equiv\fun{ua}(f_x).
            \]
            Now consider
            \begin{align*}
                \sigma\colon(X\to\univ)&\to\univ\\
                P&\mapsto\sum_{x\colon X}P(x).
            \end{align*}
            Then, $\fun{ap}_\sigma(\fun{funext}(\varepsilon))\colon\Sigma_XA\eq\univ\Sigma_XB$, as desired.
            
            \bigskip

            To verify that both proofs are actually the same, we introduce the goal
            \begin{equation}\label{eq:Sigma-goal}
                \fun{idtoeqv}
                    \bigl(
                        \fun{ap}_\sigma(p)
                    \bigr)
                \eq{\Sigma_XA\simeq\Sigma_XB}
                \dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)},
            \end{equation}
            where $p\defeq\fun{funext}(\varepsilon)\colon A\eq\univ B$.
            
            To use based path induction to prove the goal, we must first generalize it to an arbitrary path $p\colon A\eq\univ B$. For an arbitrary $p$, we define $\varepsilon_p\defeq\fun{happly}(p)$, and for each $x\colon X$, the following equivalence between $A(x)$ and $B(x)$:
            \begin{align*}
                f_{p,x}
                    &\defeq\fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}
                        (\varepsilon_p(x))\\
                \eta_{p,x}
                    &\defeq\fun{transportinv}_r^{\id_\univ}
                        (\varepsilon_p(x))\\
                \vartheta_{p,x}
                    &\defeq\fun{transportinv}_l^{\id_\univ}
                        (\varepsilon_p(x)).
            \end{align*}
            
            Let $\dep{f_p,(\eta_p,\vartheta_p)}$ denote the total equivalence between the $\Sigma$-types induced by this family of equivalences.
            
            We can now apply based path induction on $p$, assuming $B\equiv A$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$. In this base case, the components of the \lhs of \eqref{eq:Sigma-goal} evaluate to
            \begin{align*}
                \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}
                    &(\fun{ap}_\sigma(p))
                    \equiv\id_{\Sigma_XA}\\
                \fun{transportinv}_r^{\id_\univ}
                    &(\fun{ap}_\sigma(p))
                    \equiv\fun{refl}\\
                \fun{transportinv}_l^{\id_\univ}
                    &(\fun{ap}_\sigma(p))
                    \equiv\fun{refl}.
            \end{align*}
            For the \rhs of \eqref{eq:Sigma-goal}, the assumption $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$ implies that
            \[
                \varepsilon_p
                    \equiv\fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_A)
                    \equiv\lambda x.\,\fun{refl}_{A(x)},
            \]
            so that $\varepsilon_p(x)\equiv\fun{refl}_{A(x)}$. Therefore, by definition of the induced components,
            \begin{align*}
                f_{p,x}&\equiv\id_{A(x)}\\
                \eta_{p,x}&\equiv\fun{refl}\\
                \vartheta_{p,x}&\equiv\fun{refl}.
            \end{align*}
            Thus, the total function $f_p(\dep{x,a})\defeq\dep{x,f_{p,x}(a)}$ reduces to $\dep{x,a}$, and the global homotopies $\eta_p$ and $\vartheta_p$, which are constructed using $\fun{pair}^=$, satisfy
            \begin{align*}
                \eta_p(\dep{x,a})
                    &\equiv\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x,\eta_{p,x}(a))\\
                    &\equiv\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_a)\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,a}},
            \intertext{and}
                    \vartheta_p(\dep{x,a})
                    &\equiv\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x,\vartheta_{p,x}(a))\\
                    &\equiv\fun{pair}^=(\fun{refl}_x,\fun{refl}_a)\\
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}_{\dep{x,a}}.
            \end{align*}
            Since both sides evaluate to the identity equivalence in the base case, the equality
            \[
                \fun{idtoeqv}
                    \bigl(
                        \fun{ap}_\sigma(p)
                    \bigr)
                \eq{\Sigma_XA\simeq\Sigma_XB}
                \dep{f_p,(\eta_p,\vartheta_p)}
            \]
            holds for an arbitrary path $p$.
            
            Applying this equality to $p\defeq\fun{funext}(\varepsilon)$ yields
            \begin{align*}
                \dep{f_{p,x},(\eta_{p,x},\vartheta_{p,x})}
                    &\equiv\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{happly}
                        (\fun{funext}(\varepsilon))(x))\\
                    &\equiv\fun{idtoeqv}
                        (\fun{ua}(
                            \dep{
                                f_x,
                                (\eta_x,\vartheta_x)
                            }
                            )
                        )\\
                    &\eq{}(f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x)).
            \end{align*}
            Thus, the generalized equivalence $\dep{f_p, (\eta_p,\vartheta_p)}$ evaluates precisely to the arbitrarily chosen equivalence $\dep{f,(\eta, \vartheta)}$, completing the proof.

            \item[$\to$)] Here we have to prove that, given equivalences $\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)}\colon A\simeq B$ and $\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')}\colon A'\simeq B'$, the type $(A\to A')\simeq(B\to B')$ is inhabited.

            Consider the function
            \begin{align*}
                (f\to g)\colon(A\to A')&\to(B\to B')\\
                u&\mapsto v,
            \end{align*}
            where $v$ is defined by the commutativity of the diagram
            \[
                \begin{tikzcd}[row sep=large]
                    A
                        \arrow[r,"u"]
                        \arrow[d,"f"']
                    &A'
                        \arrow[d,"g"]\\
                    B
                        \arrow[r,"v"',dashed]
                        \arrow[u,"f^{-1}",bend left=50]
                    &B'
                \end{tikzcd}
            \]
            That is, $(f\to g)\defeq\lambda u.\,g\circ u\circ f^{-1}$. We define the quasi-inverse as
            \[
                 (f\to g)^{-1}\defeq\lambda v.\,g^{-1}\circ v\circ f.
            \]
            Note that, for $b\colon B$, we have
            \begin{align*}
                (f\to g)\circ(f\to&g)^{-1}(v)(b)\\
                    &\equiv(f\to g)(g^{-1}\circ v\circ f)(b)\\
                    &\equiv(g\circ g^{-1}\circ v)(f(f^{-1}(b)))\\
                    &\eq{B'}(g\circ g^{-1})(v(b))
                        &&\text{; }((g\circ g^{-1}\circ v)\lwct\eta)(b)\\
                    &\eq{B'}v(b)
                        &&\text{; }(\eta'\rwct v)(b).
            \end{align*}
            Thus,
            \[
                ((g\circ g^{-1}\circ v)\lwct\eta)\ct(\eta'\rwct v)
                \colon(f\to g)\circ(f\to g)^{-1}(v)\sim v.
            \]
            Since Proposition~\ref{prop:homotopy-whiskering} implies
            \begin{align*}
                ((g\circ g^{-1}\circ v)\lwct\eta)\ct(\eta'\rwct v)
                \eq{}\eta'\hct(v\lwct\eta),
            \end{align*}
            we can express the global right homotopy as
            \begin{align*}
                (f\to g)\circ(f\to g)^{-1}&\sim\id_{B\to B'}\\
                v&\mapsto\eta'\hct(v\lwct\eta).
            \end{align*}
            By symmetry, we deduce
            \begin{align*}
                (f\to g)^{-1}\circ(f\to g)&\sim\id_{A\to A'}\\
                u&\mapsto\vartheta'\hct(u\lwct\vartheta).
            \end{align*}
            
            \bigskip

            Using the univalence axiom, we can transform the equivalences into equalities:
            \[
                \fun{ua}(\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)})\colon A\eq\univ B
                \quad\text{and}\quad
                \fun{ua}(\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')})\colon A'\eq\univ B'.
            \]
            Now suppose we have generic paths $p\colon A\eq\univ B$ and $q\colon A'\eq\univ B'$. To prove that
            \[
                (A\to A')\eq\univ(B\to B'),
            \]
            by based path induction on $p$, we can assume $B\equiv A$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$. The goal becomes
            \[
                (A\to A')\eq\univ(A\to B').
            \]
            Thus, we may further assume $B'\equiv A'$ and $q\equiv\fun{refl}_{A'}$. In this case, the goal becomes 
            \[
                (A\to A')\eq\univ(A\to A'),
            \]
            which is inhabited by $\fun{refl}_{A\to A'}$. Combining both inductions we obtain
            \[
                \fun{rec}_{=_\univ}
                    \bigl(
                        A'\to B',
                        \fun{rec}_{=_\univ}
                            (
                                A\to B',
                                \fun{refl}_{A\to A'},
                                A\to A'
                            ),
                        A'\to B'
                    \bigr)
            \]
            as a witness of our goal.
            
            Let $\varepsilon(p,q)\colon(A\to A')\eq\univ(B\to B')$ denote the path obtained by our double recursion. Applying $\fun{idtoeqv}$ to the equivalences we have yields:
            \[
                \fun{idtoeqv}\bigl(\varepsilon(
                    \fun{ua}(\dep{
                        f,
                        (\eta,\vartheta)
                    }),
                    \fun{ua}(\dep{
                    g,
                    (\eta',\vartheta')
                    })
                    )\bigr)
                    \colon(A\to A')\simeq(B\to B').
            \]

            \bigskip

            To verify that both proofs are equivalent, we have to show that
            \begin{align*}
                \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon)
                    &\eq{}(f\to g)\\
                \fun{transportinv}_r^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon)
                    &\eq{}\lambda v.\,\eta'\hct(v\lwct\eta)\\
                \fun{transportinv}_l^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon)
                    &\eq{}\lambda u.\,\vartheta'\hct(u\lwct\vartheta),
            \end{align*}
            where
            \[
                \epsilon\defeq
                    \varepsilon
                        \bigl(
                            \fun{ua}(\dep{
                                f,(\eta,\vartheta)
                            }),
                            \fun{ua}(\dep{
                                g,(\eta',\vartheta')
                            })
                        \bigr).
            \]
            If we generalize to $\epsilon_{p,q}\defeq\varepsilon(p,q)$, as we defined it above, we can introduce
            \begin{align*}
                \dep{f_p,(\eta_p,\vartheta_p)}
                    &\defeq\fun{idtoeqv}(p)\\
                \dep{g_q,(\eta'_q,\vartheta'_q)}
                    &\defeq\fun{idtoeqv}(q).
            \end{align*}
            We claim that
            \begin{equation}\label{eq:p-q-claim}
                \begin{aligned}
                    \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon_{p,q})
                        &\eq{}(f_p\to g_q)\\
                    \fun{transportinv}_r^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon_{p,q})
                        &\eq{}\lambda v.\,\eta'_q\hct(v\lwct\eta_p)\\
                    \fun{transportinv}_l^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon_{p,q})
                        &\eq{}\lambda u.\,
                            \vartheta'_q\hct(u\lwct\vartheta_p).
                \end{aligned}
            \end{equation}
            In fact, by based path induction first on $p$ and then on $q$, we only need to consider the case $B\equiv A$, $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$ and $B'\equiv A'$, $q\equiv\fun{refl}_{A'}$. In that case, $\epsilon_{p,q}$ becomes $\fun{refl}_{A\to A'}$, $\dep{f_p,(\eta_p,\vartheta_p)}\equiv\dep{\id_A,(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})}$, and $\dep{g_q,(\eta'_q,\vartheta'_q)}\equiv\dep{\id_{A'},(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})}$. Consequently,
            \begin{align*}
                \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon_{p,q})
                    &\equiv\id_{A\to A'},\\
                (f_p\to g_q)&\equiv\id_{A\to A'};
            \intertext{moreover, Lemma~\ref{lem:transportinv} and Proposition~\ref{prop:homotopy-whiskering} yield}
                \fun{transportinv}_r^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon_{p,q})
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}\\
                \lambda v.\,\eta'_q\hct(v\lwct\eta_p)
                    &\eq{}\fun{refl}\\
                \fun{transportinv}_l^{\id_\univ}(\epsilon_{p,q})
                    &\equiv\fun{refl}\\
                \lambda u.\,
                        \vartheta'_q\hct(u\lwct\vartheta_p)
                    &\eq{}\fun{refl},
            \end{align*}
            proving the claim.
            
            Specializing \eqref{eq:p-q-claim} to $p\equiv\fun{ua}(\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)})$ and $q\equiv\fun{ua}(\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')})$ reduces the question to proving that the $p$- and $q$-equivalences equal the original ones. But
            \begin{align*}
                \dep{f_p,(\eta_p,\vartheta_p)}
                    &\equiv \fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ua}
                    (\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta))})\\
                    &\eq{A\simeq B}\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)}
            \intertext{and}
                \dep{g_q,(\eta'_q,\vartheta'_q)}
                    &\equiv\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ua}(
                        \dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')})
                    )\\
                    &\eq{A'\simeq B'}
                        \dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')},
            \end{align*}
            which complete the proof.

            \item[$\Pi$)] Suppose that there are equivalences $(f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x))\colon A(x)\simeq B(x)$. We have to prove that $\Pi_XA\simeq\Pi_XB$. Consider the function
            \begin{align*}
                f\colon\Bigl(\prod_{x\colon X}A(x)\Bigr)
                    &\to\prod_{x\colon X}B(x)\\
                    u&\mapsto\lambda x.\,f_x(u(x)).
            \intertext{For the back function we define}
                f^{-1}\colon\Bigl(\prod_{x\colon X}B(x)\Bigr)
                    &\to\prod_{x\colon X}A(x)\\
                    v&\mapsto\lambda x.\,f_x^{-1}(v(x)).
            \end{align*}
            Clearly, these functions are mutual quasi-inverses. To construct the required homotopies, we apply function extensionality:
            \begin{align*}
                \eta&\colon f\circ f^{-1}\sim\id_{\Pi_XB}\\
                \eta(v)&\defeq\fun{funext}(\lambda x.\,\eta_x(v(x))),
            \intertext{and}
                \vartheta&\colon f^{-1}\circ f\sim\id_{\Pi_XA}\\
                \vartheta(u)&\defeq\fun{funext}(\lambda x.\,\vartheta_x(u(x))).
            \end{align*}

            \bigskip

            Applying the univalence axiom to the point-wise equivalences yields
            \[
                \fun{ua}(\dep{f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x)})
                    \colon A(x)\eq\univ B(x).
            \]
            Let $\varepsilon(x)\defeq\fun{ua}(\dep{f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x)})$. This means that $\varepsilon\colon A\sim B$ and so, $\fun{funext}(\varepsilon)\colon A\eq{X\to\univ}B$.
            
            Define the function
            \begin{align*}
                \Pi_X\colon(X\to\univ)&\to\univ\\
                P&\mapsto\Pi_xP.
            \end{align*}
            Using the path above, we obtain
            \[
                \fun{ap}_{\Pi_X}(\fun{funext}(\varepsilon))
                    \colon \Pi_XA\eq\univ\Pi_XB.
            \]
            The conclusion follows by applying $\fun{idtoeqv}$ to the resulting path.

            \bigskip

            To verify that both proofs are equivalent, we have to show that
            \[
                \fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ap}_{\Pi_X}(\fun{funext}(\varepsilon)))
                    \eq{}\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)}.
            \]
            Fix a generic path $p\colon A\eq{X\to\univ}B$. For each $x\colon X$, define
            \[
                \dep{f^p_x,(\eta^p_x,\vartheta^p_x)}
                    \defeq\fun{idtoeqv}
                        \bigl(
                            \fun{happly}(p)(x)
                        \bigr)
                        \colon A(x)\simeq B(x).
            \]
            We can then construct a global equivalence with functions
            \begin{alignat*}2
                f^p\colon\Pi_XA&\to\Pi_XB
                &g^p\colon\Pi_XB&\to\Pi_XA\\
                u&\mapsto\lambda x.\,f^p_x(u(x))
                &v&\mapsto\lambda x.\,(f^p_x)^{-1}(v(x))
            \intertext{and homotopies}
                \eta^p&\colon f^p\circ g^p\sim\id_{\Pi_XB}
                &\vartheta^p&\colon g^p\circ f^p\sim\id_{\Pi_XA}\\
                v&\mapsto\fun{funext}(\lambda x.\,\eta^p_x(v(x)))
                &u&\mapsto \fun{funext}
                    (\lambda x.\,\vartheta^p_x(u(x))).
            \end{alignat*}
            Thus, the global equivalence $E(p)$ is defined as
            \[
                E(p)\defeq\dep{f^p,(\eta^p,\vartheta^p)}.
            \]
            We claim that
            \[
                \fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ap}_{\Pi_X}(p))\eq{}E(p).
            \]
            By based path induction on $p$, it suffices to consider $B\equiv A$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$. In this case, we have
            \begin{align*}
                \lhs 
                    &\equiv\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ap}_{\Pi_X}(\fun{refl}_A))\\
                    &\equiv\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{refl}_{\Pi_XA})\\
                    &\equiv\dep{\id_{\Pi_XA}, (\fun{refl}_{\id_{\Pi_XA}}, \fun{refl}_{\id_{\Pi_XA}})}.
            \intertext{On the other hand, given $x\colon X$, by equation \eqref{eq:happly-refl}}
                    \fun{happly}(\fun{refl}_A)(x)
                        &\equiv\fun{refl}_{A(x)}.
            \intertext{Then}
                \dep{f^{\fun{refl}_A}_x, (\eta^{\fun{refl}_A}_x, \vartheta^{\fun{refl}_A}_x)}
                    &\equiv\dep{\id_{A(x)},(\fun{refl}_{\id_{A(x)}}, \fun{refl}_{\id_{A(x)}})}.
            \end{align*}
            Substituting these into the definitions of our global functions $f^{\fun{refl}_A}$ and $g^{\fun{refl}_A}$ yields
            \begin{align*}
                f^{\fun{refl}_A}(u) 
                    &\equiv \lambda x.\, \id_{A(x)}(u(x)) \equiv \lambda x.\, u(x) \equiv u, \\
                g^{\fun{refl}_A}(v) 
                    &\equiv \lambda x.\, \id_{A(x)}(v(x)) \equiv \lambda x.\, v(x) \equiv v.
            \end{align*}
            Thus, both global functions reduce definitionally to the identity function on the $\Pi$-type. Substituting the pointwise homotopies into the global ones yields
            \begin{align*}
                \eta^{\fun{refl}_A}(v) 
                    &\equiv \fun{funext}(\lambda x.\, \fun{refl}_{v(x)}), \\
                \vartheta^{\fun{refl}_A}(u) 
                    &\equiv \fun{funext}(\lambda x.\, \fun{refl}_{u(x)}).
            \end{align*}
            Hence,
            \begin{align*}
                \eta^{\fun{refl}_A}(v) &\equiv \fun{refl}_v, \\
                \vartheta^{\fun{refl}_A}(u) &\equiv \fun{refl}_u,
            \end{align*}
            which implies $\eta^{\fun{refl}_A} \equiv \fun{refl}_{\id_{\Pi_XA}}$ and $\vartheta^{\fun{refl}_A} \equiv \fun{refl}_{\id_{\Pi_XA}}$. It follows that
            \begin{align*}
                \rhs
                    &\equiv E(\fun{refl}_A)\\
                    &\equiv\dep{f^{\fun{refl}_A},
                        (\eta^{\fun{refl}_A}, \vartheta^{\fun{refl}_A})}\\
                    &\equiv\dep{
                        \id_{\Pi_XA},
                            (
                                \fun{refl}_{\id_{\Pi_XA}}, 
                                \fun{refl}_{\id_{\Pi_XA}}
                            )
                    }.
            \end{align*}
            In conclusion, $\lhs\equiv\rhs$, and the claimed equality follows. Specializing it to the path $p\defeq\fun{funext}(\varepsilon)$ yields the desired equality because, for each $x\colon X$,
            \begin{align*}
                \fun{idtoeqv}
                    \bigl(
                        \fun{happly}(\fun{funext}(\varepsilon))(x)
                    \bigr)
                    &\eq{}\fun{idtoeqv}(\varepsilon(x))\\
                    &\equiv\fun{idtoeqv}
                        \bigl(
                            \fun{ua}(\dep{f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x)})
                        \bigr)\\
                    &\eq{}\dep{f_x,(\eta_x,\vartheta_x)}.
            \end{align*}
            Since the pointwise components defining $E(\fun{funext}(\varepsilon))$ are propositionally equal to the original point-wise equivalences, the assembled global equivalence is equal to $\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)}$.

            \item[$+$)] In this case, we are given two equivalences $\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)}\colon A\simeq B$ and $\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')}\colon A'\simeq B'$, and we have to construct an equivalence between $(A+A')$ and $(B+B')$. To do that, we define
            \begin{align*}
                (f+g)\colon(A+A')&\to(B+B')\\
                \fun{inl}(a)&\mapsto\fun{inl}(f(a))\\
                \fun{inr}(a')&\mapsto\fun{inr}(g(a')).
            \intertext{For the inverse, we introduce}
                (f+g)^{-1}&\defeq(f^{-1}+g^{-1}),
            \intertext{and for the homotopies,}
                (\eta+\eta')(\fun{inl}(b))
                    &\defeq\fun{inl}(\eta(b))\\
                (\eta+\eta')(\fun{inr}(b'))
                    &\defeq\fun{inr}(\eta'(b'))\\
                (\vartheta+\vartheta')(\fun{inl}(a))
                    &\defeq\fun{inl}(\vartheta(a))\\
                (\vartheta+\vartheta')(\fun{inr}(a'))
                    &\defeq\fun{inr}(\vartheta'(a')).           
            \end{align*}
            It is clear that
            \begin{equation}\label{eq:eqv-coproduct}
                \dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)}
                    +\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')}
                    \defeq\dep{f+g,(\eta+\eta',\vartheta+\vartheta')}
            \end{equation}
            is the desired equivalence.

            \bigskip
        
            Using the univalence axiom, we obtain paths $\fun{ua}(\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)})\colon A\eq\univ B$ and $\fun{ua}(\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')})\colon A'\eq\univ B'$. Suppose we have generic paths $p\colon A\eq\univ B$ and $q\colon A'\eq\univ B'$. We can construct a path
            \[
                p+q\colon(A+A')\eq\univ(B+B')
            \]
            by based path induction, first on $p$, and then on $q$, as follows: considering the case where $B\equiv A$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$, and $B'\equiv A'$ and $q\equiv\fun{refl}_{A'}$, we can simply define $p+q\defeq\fun{refl}_{A+A'}$.
            
            Thus, specializing this construction to the paths $p\defeq\fun{ua}(\dep{f,(\eta,\vartheta)})$ and $q\defeq\fun{ua}(\dep{g,(\eta',\vartheta')})$, and then applying $\fun{idtoeqv}$ to the resulting path, we arrive at the desired equivalence.

            \bigskip

            To show that both proofs are the same, we need to be more precise about the second one.
            \begin{enumerate}[-]
                \item Fix $B\equiv A$ and $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$. Consider the motive
                \begin{align*}
                    E&\colon\prod_{X\colon\univ}(A'\eq{\univ}X)\to\univ\\
                    E(X)&\defeq\lambda z.\,
                        (A+A')\eq\univ(A+X),
                \end{align*}
                where $E(X)$ is constant (it does not depend on $z$).
                
                For the base case $c_{\fun{refl}}\colon E(A',\fun{refl}_{A'})$, we take reflexivity:
                \[
                    c_{\fun{refl}}\defeq\fun{refl}_{A+A'}.
                \]
                The induction principle yields:
                \[
                    \gamma_q\defeq
                        \fun{ind}_=(E,\fun{refl}_{A+A'},B',q)
                            \colon(A+A')\eq\univ(A+B').
                \]
            
                \item To complete the based induction on $p$, we fix $q\colon A'\eq{\univ}B'$ and introduce the motive
                \begin{align*}
                    F_q&\colon\prod_{Y\colon\univ}
                        (A\eq{\univ}Y)\to\univ\\
                    F_q(Y)&\defeq\lambda z.\,
                        (A+A')
                        \eq{\univ}(Y+B'),
                \end{align*}
                where, as before, $F_q(Y)$ is constant on $z$. For the base case where $Y\equiv A$, we take $\gamma_q$. Thus, we can define
                \[
                    \gamma\defeq\fun{ind}_=(F_q,\gamma_q,B,p)
                        \colon(A+A')\eq{\univ}(B+B').
                \]
                Consider the goal type
                \begin{align*}
                    \prod_{p\colon A\eq\univ B}\;
                    \prod_{q\colon A'\eq\univ B'}
                        \fun{idtoeqv}(\gamma)
                        \eq{}
                        \bigl(
                            \fun{idtoeqv}(p)+\fun{idtoeqv}(q)
                        \bigr),
                \end{align*}
                where the coproduct on the \rhs is the one defined in \eqref{eq:eqv-coproduct}.
            
                Since both sides of the equation are terms of type $(A+A')\simeq(B+B')$, to prove that the identity type is inhabited, we may proceed by path induction on $p$ and $q$. Thus, we assume $B\equiv A$ with $p\equiv\fun{refl}_A$, and $B'\equiv A'$ with $q\equiv\fun{refl}_{A'}$. Then,
                \begin{align*}
                    \gamma_q
                        &\equiv\fun{refl}_{A+A'},\\
                    \gamma
                        &\equiv\gamma_q
                            \equiv\fun{refl}_{A+A'},\\
                    \fun{idtoeqv}(\gamma)
                        &\equiv\dep{\id_{A+A'},(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})},\\
                    \fun{idtoeqv}(p)
                        &\equiv\dep{\id_A,(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})},\\
                    \fun{idtoeqv}(q)
                        &\equiv\dep{\id_{A'},(\fun{refl},\fun{refl})},\\
                    \fun{idtoeqv}(p)+\fun{idtoeqv}(q)
                        &\equiv
                            \dep{
                                \id_A+\id_{A'},
                                (
                                    \fun{refl}+\fun{refl},
                                    \fun{refl}+\fun{refl}
                                )
                            }.
                \intertext{Consequently, we need to verify that}
                    \id_{A+A'}
                        &\eq{}\id_A+\id_{A'}
                \intertext{and}
                    \fun{refl}+\fun{refl}
                        &\eq{}\fun{refl}.
                \end{align*}
                The first equality is true by coproduct induction. Therefore, it holds by function extensionality. The second also follows from function extensionality because
                \begin{align*}
                    \fun{refl}(x)&\defeq\fun{refl}_x,\\
                    (\fun{refl}+\fun{refl})(\fun{inl}(x))
                        &\equiv\fun{refl}(\fun{inl}(x)),\\
                    (\fun{refl}+\fun{refl})(\fun{inr}(y))
                        &\equiv\fun{refl}(\fun{inr}(y)).
                \end{align*}
            \end{enumerate}
        \end{enumerate}
    \end{enumerate}
\end{solution}

\begin{exr}
    State and prove a version of Equation~{\upshape\eqref{eq:nat-transformation}} from Section~{\upshape\nameref{types-as-categories}} for dependent functions.
\end{exr}

\begin{solution}
    Let\/ $P\colon X\to\univ$ be a type family. Given two dependent functions\/ $f,g\colon\prod_{x\colon X}P(x)$, a homotopy\/ $\eta\colon f\sim g$, and a path\/ $p\colon x\eq{X}y$, we have
    \[
       \fun{apd}_f(p)\ct\eta(y)\eq{P(y)}p_*(\eta(x))\ct\fun{apd}_g(p).
    \]
    To prove this, first observe that the types match:
    \[
       \explain[p_*(f(x))\eq{}f(y)]{\fun{apd}_f(p)}
       \ct
       \explain[f(y)\eq{}g(y)]{\eta(y)}
       \eq{P(y)}
       \explain[p_*(f(x))\eq{}p_*(g(x))]
       {{\fun{ap}_{p_*}(\explain[f(x)\eq{}g(x)]{\eta(x)})}}
       \ct
       \explain[p_*(g(x))\eq{}g(y)]{\fun{apd}_g(p)},
    \]
    where
    \[
        p_*\defeq\fun{transport}^P(p)\colon P(x)\to P(y).
    \]
    Therefore, to complete the proof, we may apply based path induction on\/ $p$ and assume that\/ $y\equiv x$ and\/ $p\equiv\fun{refl}_x$. In that case, the expression reduces to
    \[
        \fun{refl}_{f(x)}\ct\eta(x)
            \eq{P(x)}\eta(x)\ct\fun{refl}_{g(x)},
    \]
    which is trivially inhabited because
    \[
        \fun{refl}_{f(x)}\ct\eta(x)\equiv\eta(x)
        \quad\text{and}\quad
        \fun{ru}(\eta(x))^{-1}\colon\eta(x)
            \eq{P(x)}\eta(x)\ct\fun{refl}_{g(x)}.
    \]
\end{solution}

\begin{exr}\ua
    The lemma in {\upshape Exercise~\ref{exr:2-simeq-2-simeq-2}} shows that $0_{\fun2}\ne_{\fun2}1_{\fun2}$. Show that, nevertheless, 
    \[
        \dep{\fun2,0_{\fun2}}
        \eq\puniv
        \dep{\fun2,1_{\fun2}}.
    \]
\end{exr}

\begin{solution}
    Recall that $0_{\fun2}\ne_{\fun2}1_{\fun2}$ is a notation for $\neg(0_{\fun2}\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2})$, which in turn is a notation for $(0_{\fun2}\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2})\to\fun0$.

    By Theorem~\ref{thm:pair-equivalence},
    \begin{align*}
        \bigl(
            \dep{\fun2,0_{\fun2}}
            \eq\puniv
            \dep{\fun2,1_{\fun2}}
        \bigr)
            \simeq\sum_{p\colon\fun2\eq\univ\fun2}
                \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(p,0_{\fun2})\eq{\fun2}1_{\fun2}.
    \end{align*}
    By Exercise~\ref{exr:2-simeq-2-simeq-2}, we know that $\fun{not}\colon\fun2\to\fun2$ defines an equivalence. Therefore, $\fun{ua}(\fun{not})$ is a path in $\fun2\eq\univ\fun2$. Hence,
    \begin{align*}
        \fun{transport}^{\id_\univ}(\fun{ua}(\fun{not}))(0_{\fun2})
            &\eq{\fun2}\fun{idtoeqv}(\fun{ua}(\fun{not}))(0_{\fun2})
                &&\text{; Thm.~\ref{thm:idtoeqv-def}}\\
            &\eq{\fun2}\fun{not}(0_{\fun2})\\
            &\equiv1_{\fun2},
    \end{align*}
    which shows that the \rhs of the equivalence is inhabited by $\dep{\fun{ua}(\fun{not}),\fun{refl}_{1_{\fun2}}}$. Thus, the \lhs is inhabited as well.
    
\end{solution}
